href="/wiki/.bq" title=".bq">.bq</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[h]</a></sup></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Netherlands</b> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Nederland</i>, <small></small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[&#712;ne&#720;d&#601;rl&#593;nt]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nl-Nederland.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0a/Nl-Nederland.ogg" title="Nl-Nederland.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> located mainly in <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Europe" title="Northwestern Europe">Northwestern Europe</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> portion of the Netherlands consists of <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Netherlands" title="Provinces of the Netherlands">twelve separate provinces</a> that border <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> to the south, and the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> to the northwest, with <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">maritime borders</a> in the North Sea with Belgium, Germany and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[12]</a></sup> Including three island territories in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Sea</a>&#8212;<a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>&#8212; it forms a <a href="/wiki/Constituent_state" title="Constituent state">constituent country</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>. The official language is <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, but a secondary official language in the <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">province of Friesland</a> is <a href="/wiki/West_Frisian_language" title="West Frisian language">West Frisian</a>.\n</p><p>The five largest cities in the Netherlands are <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utrecht" title="Utrecht">Utrecht</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven" title="Eindhoven">Eindhoven</a>. Amsterdam is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_of_the_Netherlands" title="Capital of the Netherlands">country\'s capital</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[13]</a></sup> while The Hague holds the seat of the <a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">States General</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_Netherlands" title="Cabinet of the Netherlands">Cabinet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Netherlands" title="Supreme Court of the Netherlands">Supreme Court</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[14]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rotterdam" title="Port of Rotterdam">Port of Rotterdam</a> is the largest <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">port</a> in Europe, and the largest in any country outside <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[15]</a></sup> The country is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Ten_(economics)" title="Group of Ten (economics)">G10</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a>, as well as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> and the trilateral <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux Union</a>. It hosts several <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental organisations</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_court" title="International court">international courts</a>, many of which are centered in The Hague, which is consequently dubbed \'the world\'s legal capital\'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p><span id="name"></span><i>Netherlands</i> literally means \'<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_Countries" title="Lower Countries">lower countries</a>\' in reference to its low elevation and flat topography, with only about 50% of its land exceeding 1 metre (3&#160;ft 3&#160;in) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>, and nearly 17% falling below sea level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eupedia_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eupedia-25">[17]</a></sup> Most of the areas below sea level, known as <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder"><i>polders</i></a>, are the result of <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a> that began in the 16th century. With a population of 17.25 million people, all living within a total area of roughly 41,500 square kilometres (16,000&#160;sq&#160;mi)&#8212;of which the land area is 33,700 square kilometres (13,000&#160;sq&#160;mi)&#8212;the Netherlands is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_population_density" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by population density">one of the most densely populated countries in the world</a>. Nevertheless, it is the world\'s second-largest <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">exporter</a> of food and agricultural products (after the United States), owing to its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertile_soil" title="Fertile soil">fertile soil</a>, mild climate, and <a href="/wiki/Intensive_farming" title="Intensive farming">intensive agriculture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hollandtrade.com_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-hollandtrade.com-27">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Netherlands was, historically, the <i>third</i> country in the world to have <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">representative government</a>, and it has been a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary structure</a> since 1848. The country has a tradition of <a href="/wiki/Pillarisation" title="Pillarisation">pillarisation</a> and a long record of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_tolerance" title="Social tolerance">social tolerance</a>, having <i>legalised</i> <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_the_Netherlands" title="Abortion in the Netherlands">abortion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_the_Netherlands" title="Prostitution in the Netherlands">prostitution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia_in_the_Netherlands" title="Euthanasia in the Netherlands">human euthanasia</a>, along with maintaining a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progressive_politics" title="Progressive politics">progressive</a> <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Drug policy of the Netherlands">drug policy</a>. The Netherlands abolished the <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_the_Netherlands" title="Capital punishment in the Netherlands">death penalty</a> in 1870, allowed <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage" title="Women\'s suffrage">women\'s suffrage</a> in 1917, and became the world\'s first country to legalise <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_Netherlands" title="Same-sex marriage in the Netherlands">same-sex marriage</a> in 2001. Its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed_market" title="Mixed market">mixed-market</a> <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">advanced economy</a> had the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">thirteenth-highest</a> <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> globally. The Netherlands ranks among the highest in international indexes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Press_freedom" title="Press freedom">press freedom</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Economic_freedom" title="Economic freedom">economic freedom</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">human development</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Happiness" title="Happiness">happiness</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[i]</a></sup> Its strong performance on these indexes is owed in large part to a generous <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a> that provides <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_the_Netherlands" title="Healthcare in the Netherlands">universal healthcare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Netherlands" title="Education in the Netherlands">public education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Netherlands" title="Transport in the Netherlands">infrastructure</a>, in addition to <a href="/wiki/Welfare" title="Welfare">social benefits</a>. The country is also known for its "<a href="/wiki/Polder_model" title="Polder model">polder model</a>", a leading <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomics" title="Socioeconomics">socioeconomic model</a> based on <a href="/wiki/Consensus_decision-making" title="Consensus decision-making">consensus decision-making</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" islands</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Politics"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Politics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 areas</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Language"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Language</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Art,_philosophy_and_literature"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Art, philosophy and literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Dutch_value_system"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Dutch value system</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Dutch_people_and_ecology"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Dutch people and ecology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">8.4</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39"><a href="#Film_and_television"><span class="tocnumber">8.5</span> <span class="toctext">Film and television</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">8.6</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">8.7</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-42"><a href="#Colonial_heritage"><span class="tocnumber">8.8</span> <span class="toctext">Colonial heritage</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Terminology_of_the_Low_Countries" title="Terminology of the Low Countries">Terminology of the Low Countries</a></div>\n<p>The Netherlands\' turbulent history and shifts of power resulted in exceptionally many and widely varying names in different languages. There is diversity even within languages. This holds also for English, where Dutch is the adjective form and the <a href="/wiki/Misnomer" title="Misnomer">misnomer</a> <a href="/wiki/Holland" title="Holland">Holland</a> a synonym for the country "Netherlands". Dutch comes from <a href="/wiki/Theodiscus" title="Theodiscus">Theodiscus</a> and in the past centuries, the hub of Dutch culture is found in its most populous region, Holland, home to the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>; government headquarters at <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>; and Europe\'s largest port <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>. Referring to the Netherlands as Holland in the English language is similar to calling the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> "England" by people outside the UK. The term is so pervasive among potential investors and tourists, however, that the Dutch government\'s international websites for tourism and trade are "holland.com" and "hollandtradeandinvest.com".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[24]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The region of Holland consists of <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Holland" title="South Holland">South Holland</a>, two of the nation\'s twelve provinces, formerly a single province, and earlier still, the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Holland" title="County of Holland">County of Holland</a>, a remnant of the dissolved <a href="/wiki/Frisian_Kingdom" title="Frisian Kingdom">Frisian Kingdom</a>. Following the decline of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brabant" title="Duchy of Brabant">Duchy of Brabant</a> and the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">County of Flanders</a>, Holland became the most economically and politically important county in the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> region. The emphasis on Holland during the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years\' War">Eighty Years\' War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Wars" title="Anglo-Dutch Wars">Anglo-Dutch Wars</a> in the 16th, 17th and 18th century, made Holland serve as a <i><a href="/wiki/Pars_pro_toto" title="Pars pro toto">pars pro toto</a></i> for the entire country, which is now considered either incorrect,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[26]</a></sup> informal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[27]</a></sup> or, depending on context, opprobrious. Nonetheless, Holland is widely used in reference to the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands national football team</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[28]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The region called the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> (comprising <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, the Netherlands and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>) and the Country of the Netherlands, have the same <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">toponymy</a>. Place names with <i>Neder</i> (or <i>lage</i>), <i>Nieder</i>, <i>Nether</i> (or <i>low</i>) and <i>Nedre</i> (in <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic languages</a>) and <i>Bas</i> or <i>Inferior</i> (in <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>) are in use in places all over Europe. They are sometimes used in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deictic" title="Deictic">deictic</a> relation to a higher ground that consecutively is indicated as <i>Upper</i>, <i>Boven</i>, <i>Oben</i>, <i>Superior</i> or <i>Haut</i>. In the case of the Low Countries / Netherlands the geographical location of the <i>lower</i> region has been more or less downstream and near the sea. The geographical location of the upper region, however, changed tremendously over time, depending on the location of the economic and military power governing the Low Countries area. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> made a distinction between the Roman provinces of downstream <a href="/wiki/Germania_Inferior" title="Germania Inferior">Germania Inferior</a> (nowadays part of Belgium and the Netherlands) and upstream <a href="/wiki/Germania_Superior" title="Germania Superior">Germania Superior</a> (nowadays part of Germany). The designation \'Low\' to refer to the region returns again in the 10th century Duchy of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Lorraine" title="Lower Lorraine">Lower Lorraine</a>, that covered much of the Low Countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Franks_(Columbia_Encyclopedia)_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Franks_(Columbia_Encyclopedia)-38">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[30]</a></sup> But this time the corresponding <i>Upper</i> region is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Lorraine" title="Upper Lorraine">Upper Lorraine</a>, in nowadays Northern France.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dukes_of_Burgundy" title="Dukes of Burgundy">Dukes of Burgundy</a>, who ruled the Low Countries in the 15th century, used the term <i>les pays de par de&#231;&#224;</i> (~ the lands over here) for the Low Countries as opposed to <i>les pays de par del&#224;</i> (~ the lands over there) for their original homeland: <a href="/wiki/Burgundy" title="Burgundy">Burgundy</a> in present-day east-central France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlockmansPrevenier2010_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-BlockmansPrevenier2010-40">[31]</a></sup> Under <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Netherlands" title="Habsburg Netherlands">Habsburg rule</a>, <i>Les pays de par de&#231;&#224;</i> developed in <i>pays d\'embas</i> (lands down-here),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[32]</a></sup> a deictic expression in relation to other Habsburg possessions like Hungary and Austria. This was translated as <i>Neder-landen</i> in contemporary Dutch official documents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lem_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lem-42">[33]</a></sup> From a regional point of view, <i>Niderlant</i> was also the area between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meuse_(river)" title="Meuse (river)">Meuse</a> and the lower <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> in the late Middle Ages. The area known as <i>Oberland</i> (High country) was in this deictic context considered to begin approximately at the nearby higher located <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>.\n</p><p>From the mid-sixteenth century on, the "Low Countries" and the "Netherlands" lost their original deictic meaning. They were probably the most commonly used names, besides <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a>, another pars pro toto for the Low Countries, especially in Romance language speaking Europe. The <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years\' War">Eighty Years\' War</a> (1568&#8211;1648) divided the Low Countries into an independent northern <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Latinisation_of_names" title="Latinisation of names">Latinised</a> <i>Belgica Foederata</i>, "Federated Netherlands", the precursor state of the Netherlands) and a Spanish controlled <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Southern Netherlands</a> (Latinised <i>Belgica Regia</i>, "Royal Netherlands", the precursor state of Belgium). The Low Countries today is a designation that includes the countries the Netherlands, Belgium and Luxembourg, although in most <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>, the term "Low Countries" is used as the name for the Netherlands specifically. It is used synonymous with the more neutral and geopolitical term <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Netherlands" title="History of the Netherlands">History of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<h3><span id="Prehistory_.28before_800_BC.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_(before_800_BC)">Prehistory (before 800 BC)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory (before 800 BC)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic_Europe" title="Paleolithic Europe">Paleolithic Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Europe" title="Neolithic Europe">Neolithic Europe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age_Europe" title="Bronze Age Europe">Bronze Age Europe</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1104" data-file-width="620" decoding="async" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg/150px-Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg/225px-Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg/300px-Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mannetje_van_Willemstad.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oak figurine found in <a href="/wiki/Willemstad,_North_Brabant" title="Willemstad, North Brabant">Willemstad</a> (4500 BCE)</div></div></div>\n<p>The prehistory of the area that is now the Netherlands was largely shaped by the sea and the rivers that constantly shifted the low-lying geography. The oldest human (<a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a>) traces were found in higher soils, near <a href="/wiki/Maastricht" title="Maastricht">Maastricht</a>, from what is believed to be about 250,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[34]</a></sup> At the end of the <a href="/wiki/Weichselian_glaciation" title="Weichselian glaciation">Ice Age</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nomadic" title="Nomadic">nomadic</a> late <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">Upper Paleolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_culture" title="Hamburg culture">Hamburg culture</a> (c. 13.000&#8211;10.000 BC) hunted <a href="/wiki/Reindeer" title="Reindeer">reindeer</a> in the area, using spears, but the later <a href="/wiki/Ahrensburg_culture" title="Ahrensburg culture">Ahrensburg culture</a> (c. 11.200&#8211;9500 BC) used <a href="/wiki/Bow_and_arrow" title="Bow and arrow">bow and arrow</a>. From <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesolithic_Europe" title="Mesolithic Europe">Mesolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Maglemosian_culture" title="Maglemosian culture">Maglemosian-like tribes</a> (c. 8000 BC) the <a href="/wiki/Pesse_canoe" title="Pesse canoe">oldest canoe</a> in the world was found in <a href="/wiki/Drenthe" title="Drenthe">Drenthe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;max-width:342px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:137px;max-width:137px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:163px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:5500vc_ex_leg.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="616" data-file-width="510" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/5500vc_ex_leg.jpg/135px-5500vc_ex_leg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/5500vc_ex_leg.jpg/203px-5500vc_ex_leg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/5500vc_ex_leg.jpg/270px-5500vc_ex_leg.jpg 2x" width="135"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The Netherlands in 5500 BCE.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:201px;max-width:201px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:163px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BronzAgeElp.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="497" data-file-width="606" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/BronzAgeElp.png/199px-BronzAgeElp.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/BronzAgeElp.png/299px-BronzAgeElp.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/BronzAgeElp.png/398px-BronzAgeElp.png 2x" width="199"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Bronze Age cultures in the Netherlands.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Indigenous late Mesolithic <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Swifterbant_culture" title="Swifterbant culture">Swifterbant culture</a> (c. 5600 BC) were related to the southern Scandinavian <a href="/wiki/Erteb%C3%B8lle_culture" title="Erteb&#248;lle culture">Erteb&#248;lle culture</a> and were strongly linked to rivers and open water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kooijmans1998_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kooijmans1998-45">[36]</a></sup> Between 4800 and 4500 BC, the Swifterbant people started to copy from the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Linear_Pottery_culture" title="Linear Pottery culture">Linear Pottery culture</a> the practise of <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a>, and between 4300 and 4000 BC the practise of <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[37]</a></sup> To Swifterbant related <a href="/wiki/Funnelbeaker_culture" title="Funnelbeaker culture">Funnelbeaker culture</a> (c. 4300&#8211;2800 BC) erected the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dolmens" title="Dolmens">dolmens</a>, large stone grave monuments found in Drenthe. There was a quick and smooth transition from the Funnelbeaker farming culture to the pan-European <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corded_Ware" title="Corded Ware">Corded Ware</a> <a href="/wiki/Pastoralism" title="Pastoralism">pastoralist</a> culture (c. 2950 BC). Although in the southwest, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seine-Oise-Marne_culture" title="Seine-Oise-Marne culture">Seine-Oise-Marne culture</a> related <a href="/wiki/Vlaardingen_culture" title="Vlaardingen culture">Vlaardingen culture</a> (c. 2600 BC), an apparently more primitive culture of hunter-gatherers, survived well into the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> period, until it was finally succeeded by the Corded Ware culture as well.\n</p><p>Of the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Beaker_culture" title="Beaker culture">Bell Beaker culture</a> (2700&#8211;2100 BC) several regions of origin have been postulated, notably the Iberian peninsula, the Netherlands and Central Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[38]</a></sup> They introduced metalwork in copper, gold and later bronze and opened international trade routes not seen before, reflected in the discoveries of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copper_Age_Europe" title="Copper Age Europe">copper artifacts</a>, as the metal is not normally found in Dutch soil. The many finds in <a href="/wiki/Drenthe" title="Drenthe">Drenthe</a> of rare bronze objects, suggest that it was even a trading centre in the Bronze Age (2000&#8211;800 BC). The Bell Beaker culture developed locally into the Barbed-Wire Beaker culture (2100&#8211;1800 BC) and later the <a href="/wiki/Elp_culture" title="Elp culture">Elp culture</a> (c. 1800&#8211;800 BC),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[39]</a></sup> a Middle Bronze Age archaeological culture having <a href="/wiki/Earthenware" title="Earthenware">earthenware</a> pottery of low quality as a marker. The initial phase of the Elp culture was characterised by <a href="/wiki/Tumulus" title="Tumulus">tumuli</a> (1800&#8211;1200 BC) that were strongly tied to contemporary tumuli in northern Germany and Scandinavia, and were apparently related to the <a href="/wiki/Tumulus_culture" title="Tumulus culture">Tumulus culture</a> in central Europe. The subsequent phase was that of cremating the dead and placing their ashes in urns which were then buried in fields, following the customs of the <a href="/wiki/Urnfield_culture" title="Urnfield culture">Urnfield culture</a> (1200&#8211;800 BC). The southern region became dominated by the related <a href="/wiki/Hilversum_culture" title="Hilversum culture">Hilversum culture</a> (1800&#8211;800 BC), which apparently inherited cultural ties with Britain of the previous Barbed-Wire Beaker culture.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Celts.2C_Germanic_tribes_and_Romans_.28800_BC.E2.80.93410_AD.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Celts,_Germanic_tribes_and_Romans_(800_BC&#8211;410_AD)">Celts, Germanic tribes and Romans (800 BC&#8211;410 AD)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Celts, Germanic tribes and Romans (800 BC&#8211;410 AD)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age_Europe" title="Iron Age Europe">Iron Age Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romans_in_the_Netherlands" title="Romans in the Netherlands">Romans in the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="314" data-file-width="450" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png/220px-Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png/330px-Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png/440px-Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Celtic_expansion_in_Europe.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFFF43; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diachronic_linguistics" title="Diachronic linguistics">Diachronic</a> distribution of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celtic_people" title="Celtic people">Celtic people</a> from 500 BC.</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #97FFB6; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Expansion into the southern <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> by 270 BC.</div></div></div></div>\n<p>From 800 BC onwards, the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age_Europe" title="Iron Age Europe">Iron Age</a> Celtic <a href="/wiki/Hallstatt_culture" title="Hallstatt culture">Hallstatt culture</a> became influential, replacing the <a href="/wiki/Hilversum_culture" title="Hilversum culture">Hilversum culture</a>. Iron ore brought a measure of prosperity, and was available throughout the country, including <a href="/wiki/Bog_iron" title="Bog iron">bog iron</a>. <a href="/wiki/Blacksmith" title="Blacksmith">Smiths</a> travelled from settlement to settlement with bronze and iron, fabricating tools on demand. The <a href="/wiki/Vorstengraf_(Oss)" title="Vorstengraf (Oss)">King\'s grave of Oss</a> (700 BC) was found in a burial mound, the largest of its kind in western Europe and containing an iron sword with an inlay of gold and coral.\n</p><p>The deteriorating climate in Scandinavia around 850 BC, that further deteriorated around 650 BC, might have triggered migration of <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> tribes from the North. By the time this migration was complete, around 250 BC, a few general cultural and linguistic groups had emerged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verhaal_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-50">[41]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_Germanic" title="North Sea Germanic">North Sea Germanic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ingvaeones" title="Ingvaeones">Ingvaeones</a> inhabited the northern part of the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>. They would later develop into the <a href="/wiki/Frisii" title="Frisii">Frisii</a> and the early <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verhaal_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-50">[41]</a></sup> A second grouping, the <a href="/wiki/Weser-Rhine_Germanic" title="Weser-Rhine Germanic">Weser-Rhine Germanic</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Istvaeones" title="Istvaeones">Istvaeones</a>), extended along the middle Rhine and <a href="/wiki/Weser" title="Weser">Weser</a> and inhabited the Low Countries south of the great rivers. This group consisted of tribes that would eventually develop into the <a href="/wiki/Salian_Franks" title="Salian Franks">Salian Franks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verhaal_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-50">[41]</a></sup> Also the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> <a href="/wiki/La_T%C3%A8ne_culture" title="La T&#232;ne culture">La T&#232;ne culture</a> (c. 450 BC up to the Roman conquest) had expanded over a wide range, including the southern area of the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>. Some scholars have speculated that even a third ethnic identity and language, neither Germanic nor Celtic, survived in the Netherlands until the Roman period, the Iron Age <a href="/wiki/Nordwestblock" title="Nordwestblock">Nordwestblock</a> culture,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lendering_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lendering-52">[43]</a></sup> that eventually was being absorbed by the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> to the south and the Germanic peoples from the east.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Germania_70.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="780" data-file-width="972" decoding="async" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Germania_70.svg/220px-Germania_70.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Germania_70.svg/330px-Germania_70.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Germania_70.svg/440px-Germania_70.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Germania_70.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rhine frontier of around 70 AD</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Gallic_Wars" title="Gallic Wars">Gallic Wars</a>, the area south and west of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> was conquered by <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman forces</a> under <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a> from 57 BC to 53 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lendering_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lendering-52">[43]</a></sup> Caesar describes two main Celtic tribes living in what is now the southern Netherlands: the <a href="/wiki/Menapii" title="Menapii">Menapii</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eburones" title="Eburones">Eburones</a>. The Rhine became fixed as Rome\'s northern frontier around 12 AD. Notable towns would arise along the <a href="/wiki/Limes_Germanicus" title="Limes Germanicus">Limes Germanicus</a>: <a href="/wiki/Nijmegen" title="Nijmegen">Nijmegen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Voorburg" title="Voorburg">Voorburg</a>. At first part of <a href="/wiki/Gallia_Belgica" title="Gallia Belgica">Gallia Belgica</a>, the area south of the Limes became part of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Germania_Inferior" title="Germania Inferior">Germania Inferior</a>. The area to the north of the Rhine, inhabited by the Frisii, remained outside Roman rule (but not its presence and control), while the Germanic border tribes of the <a href="/wiki/Batavi_(Germanic_tribe)" title="Batavi (Germanic tribe)">Batavi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cananefates" title="Cananefates">Cananefates</a> served in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ala_(Roman_military)" title="Ala (Roman military)">Roman cavalry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[44]</a></sup> The Batavi rose against the Romans in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batavian_rebellion" title="Batavian rebellion">Batavian rebellion</a> of 69 AD, but were eventually defeated. The Batavi later merged with other tribes into the confederation of the Salian Franks, whose identity emerged at the first half of the third century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Previt&#233;-Orton_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Previt&#233;-Orton-54">[45]</a></sup> Salian Franks appear in Roman texts as both allies and enemies. They were forced by the confederation of the Saxons from the east to move over the Rhine into Roman territory in the fourth century. From their new base in <a href="/wiki/West_Flanders" title="West Flanders">West Flanders</a> and the Southwest Netherlands, they were raiding the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a>. Roman forces pacified the region, but did not expel the Franks, who continued to be feared at least until the time of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate" title="Julian the Apostate">Julian the Apostate</a> (358), when Salian Franks were allowed to settle as <i><a href="/wiki/Foederati" title="Foederati">foederati</a></i> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toxandria" title="Toxandria">Toxandria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Previt&#233;-Orton_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Previt&#233;-Orton-54">[45]</a></sup> It has been postulated that after deteriorating climate conditions and the Romans withdrawal, the <a href="/wiki/Frisii" title="Frisii">Frisii</a> disappeared as <i><a href="/wiki/Laeti" title="Laeti">laeti</a></i> in c. 296, leaving the coastal lands largely unpopulated for the next two centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[46]</a></sup> However, recent excavations in <a href="/wiki/Kennemerland" title="Kennemerland">Kennemerland</a> show clear indication of a permanent habituation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[48]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Early_Middle_Ages_.28411.E2.80.931000.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Middle_Ages_(411&#8211;1000)">Early Middle Ages (411&#8211;1000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early Middle Ages (411&#8211;1000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankish_Kingdom" title="Frankish Kingdom">Frankish Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frisian_Kingdom" title="Frisian Kingdom">Frisian Kingdom</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frisia_716-la.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="602" data-file-width="583" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Frisia_716-la.svg/170px-Frisia_716-la.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Frisia_716-la.svg/255px-Frisia_716-la.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Frisia_716-la.svg/340px-Frisia_716-la.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frisia_716-la.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Franks, Frisians and Saxons (710s AD)</div></div></div>\n<p>After <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> government in the area collapsed, the Franks expanded their territories in numerous kingdoms. By the 490s, <a href="/wiki/Clovis_I" title="Clovis I">Clovis I</a> had conquered and united all these territories in the southern Netherlands in one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankish_kingdom" title="Frankish kingdom">Frankish kingdom</a>, and from there continued his conquests into <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a>. During this expansion, Franks migrating to the south eventually adopted the <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a> of the local population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verhaal_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-50">[41]</a></sup> A widening cultural divide grew with the Franks remaining in their original homeland in the north (i.e. southern Netherlands and Flanders), who kept on speaking <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Frankish" title="Old Frankish">Old Frankish</a>, which by the ninth century had evolved into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Low_Franconian" title="Old Low Franconian">Old Low Franconian</a> or <a href="/wiki/Old_Dutch" title="Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verhaal_50-4"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-50">[41]</a></sup> A Dutch-French language boundary came into existence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verhaal_50-5"><a href="#cite_note-Verhaal-50">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[49]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Franks_expansion.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="505" data-file-width="790" decoding="async" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Franks_expansion.gif/170px-Franks_expansion.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Franks_expansion.gif/255px-Franks_expansion.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Franks_expansion.gif/340px-Franks_expansion.gif 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Franks_expansion.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Frankish expansion (481 to 870 AD)</div></div></div>\n<p>To the north of the Franks, climatic conditions on the coast improved, and during the <a href="/wiki/Migration_Period" title="Migration Period">Migration Period</a> the abandoned land was resettled again, mostly by <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a>, but also by the closely related <a href="/wiki/Angles" title="Angles">Angles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jutes" title="Jutes">Jutes</a> and ancient <a href="/wiki/Frisii" title="Frisii">Frisii</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity-59">[50]</a></sup> Many moved on to <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and came to be known as <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxons</a>, but those who stayed would be referred to as <a href="/wiki/Frisians" title="Frisians">Frisians</a> and their language as <a href="/wiki/Frisian_languages" title="Frisian languages">Frisian</a>, named after the land that was once inhabited by Frisii.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity-59">[50]</a></sup> Frisian was spoken along the entire southern North Sea coast, and it is still the language most closely related to English among the living languages of continental Europe. By the seventh century a <a href="/wiki/Frisian_Kingdom" title="Frisian Kingdom">Frisian Kingdom</a> (650&#8211;734) under King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aldegisel" title="Aldegisel">Aldegisel</a> and King <a href="/wiki/Redbad,_King_of_the_Frisians" title="Redbad, King of the Frisians">Redbad</a> emerged with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utrecht_(city)" title="Utrecht (city)">Utrecht</a> as its centre of power,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnic_Constructs_in_Antiquity-59">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[51]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Dorestad" title="Dorestad">Dorestad</a> was a flourishing trading place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atlas_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Atlas-62">[53]</a></sup> Between 600 and around 719 the cities were often fought over between the Frisians and the Franks. In 734, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Boarn" title="Battle of the Boarn">Battle of the Boarn</a>, the Frisians were defeated after a <a href="/wiki/Frisian%E2%80%93Frankish_wars" title="Frisian&#8211;Frankish wars">series of wars</a>. With the approval of the Franks, the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_mission" title="Anglo-Saxon mission">Anglo-Saxon</a> missionary <a href="/wiki/Willibrord" title="Willibrord">Willibrord</a> converted the Frisian people to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>. He established the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Utrecht_(695%E2%80%931580)" title="Archdiocese of Utrecht (695&#8211;1580)">Archdiocese of Utrecht</a> and became bishop of the Frisians. However, his successor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boniface" title="Boniface">Boniface</a> was murdered by the Frisians in <a href="/wiki/Dokkum" title="Dokkum">Dokkum</a>, in 754.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="843" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="309" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg/220px-Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg/330px-Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg/440px-Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rorik_by_H._W._Koekkoek.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rorik_of_Dorestad" title="Rorik of Dorestad">Rorik of Dorestad</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viking" title="Viking">Viking</a> ruler of <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a> (romantic 1912 depiction)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lotharingia-959.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4174" data-file-width="3161" decoding="async" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Lotharingia-959.svg/220px-Lotharingia-959.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Lotharingia-959.svg/330px-Lotharingia-959.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Lotharingia-959.svg/440px-Lotharingia-959.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lotharingia-959.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lotharingia after 959 with the language border dotted in red</div></div></div>\n<p>The Frankish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carolingian_empire" title="Carolingian empire">Carolingian empire</a> modeled itself after the Roman Empire and controlled much of Western Europe. However, as of 843, it was divided into three parts&#8212;<a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_Francia" title="Middle Francia">Middle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Francia" title="West Francia">West Francia</a>. Most of present-day Netherlands became part of <a href="/wiki/Middle_Francia" title="Middle Francia">Middle Francia</a>, which was a weak kingdom and subject of numerous partitions and annexation attempts by its stronger neighbours. It comprised territories from <a href="/wiki/Frisia" title="Frisia">Frisia</a> in the north to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(medieval)" title="Kingdom of Italy (medieval)">Kingdom of Italy</a> in the south. Around 850, <a href="/wiki/Lothair_I" title="Lothair I">Lothair I</a> of Middle Francia acknowledged the Viking <a href="/wiki/Rorik_of_Dorestad" title="Rorik of Dorestad">Rorik of Dorestad</a> as ruler of most of Frisia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[54]</a></sup> When the kingdom of Middle Francia was partitioned in 855, the lands north of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> passed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lothair_II_of_Lotharingia" title="Lothair II of Lotharingia">Lothair II</a> and consecutively were named <a href="/wiki/Lotharingia" title="Lotharingia">Lotharingia</a>. After he died in 869, Lotharingia was partitioned, into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Lotharingia" title="Upper Lotharingia">Upper</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_Lotharingia" title="Lower Lotharingia">Lower Lotharingia</a>, the latter part comprising the Low Countries that technically became part of <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East Francia</a> in 870, although it was effectively under the control of Vikings, who raided the largely defenceless <a href="/wiki/Frisians" title="Frisians">Frisian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> towns lying on the Frisian coast and along the rivers. Around 879, another Viking raided the Frisian lands, <a href="/wiki/Godfrid,_Duke_of_Frisia" title="Godfrid, Duke of Frisia">Godfrid, Duke of Frisia</a>. The Viking raids made the sway of French and German lords in the area weak. Resistance to the Vikings, if any, came from local nobles, who gained in stature as a result, and that laid the basis for the disintegration of Lower Lotharingia into semi-independent states. One of these local nobles was <a href="/wiki/Gerolf_of_Holland" title="Gerolf of Holland">Gerolf of Holland</a>, who assumed lordship in Frisia after he helped to assassinate Godfrid, and Viking rule came to an end.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="High_Middle_Ages_.281000.E2.80.931384.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="High_Middle_Ages_(1000&#8211;1384)">High Middle Ages (1000&#8211;1384)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: High Middle Ages (1000&#8211;1384)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_urban_centers_in_the_Low_Countries" title="History of urban centers in the Low Countries">History of urban centers in the Low Countries</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> (the successor state of East Francia and then Lotharingia) ruled much of the Low Countries in the 10th and 11th century, but was not able to maintain political unity. Powerful local nobles turned their cities, counties and duchies into private kingdoms, that felt little sense of obligation to the emperor. <a href="/wiki/County_of_Holland" title="County of Holland">Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Hainaut" title="County of Hainaut">Hainaut</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">Flanders</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Gelre" title="Duchy of Gelre">Gelre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brabant" title="Duchy of Brabant">Brabant</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Utrecht" title="Bishopric of Utrecht">Utrecht</a> were in a state of almost continual war or paradoxically formed personal unions. The language and culture of most of the people who lived in the County of Holland were originally <a href="/wiki/Frisia" title="Frisia">Frisian</a>. As Frankish settlement progressed from Flanders and Brabant, the area quickly became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Low_Franconian" title="Old Low Franconian">Old Low Franconian</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Old_Dutch" title="Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a>). The rest of <a href="/wiki/Frisia" title="Frisia">Frisia</a> in the north (now <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Groningen_(province)" title="Groningen (province)">Groningen</a>) continued to maintain its independence and had its own institutions (collectively called the "<a href="/wiki/Frisian_freedom" title="Frisian freedom">Frisian freedom</a>") and resented the imposition of the feudal system.\n</p><p>Around 1000 AD, due to several agricultural developments, the economy started to develop at a fast pace, and the higher productivity allowed workers to farm more land or to become tradesmen. Towns grew around <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monasteries" title="Monasteries">monasteries</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castles" title="Castles">castles</a>, and a mercantile middle class began to develop in these urban areas, especially in Flanders and later also Brabant. Wealthy cities started to buy certain <a href="/wiki/City_rights_in_the_Low_Countries" title="City rights in the Low Countries">privileges</a> for themselves from the <a href="/wiki/Monarch" title="Monarch">sovereign</a>. In practice, this meant that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brugge" title="Brugge">Brugge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> became quasi-independent republics in their own right and would later develop into some of the most important cities and ports in Europe.\n</p><p>Around 1100 AD, farmers from <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">Flanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Utrecht" title="Bishopric of Utrecht">Utrecht</a> began draining and cultivating uninhabited swampy land in the western Netherlands, and made the emergence of the County of Holland as centre of power possible. The title of <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Holland" title="Count of Holland">Count of Holland</a> were fought over in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hook_and_Cod_Wars" title="Hook and Cod Wars">Hook and Cod Wars</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Hoekse en Kabeljauwse twisten</i>) between 1350 and 1490. The Cod faction consisted of the more progressive cities, while the Hook faction consisted of the conservative noblemen. These noblemen invited the Duke <a href="/wiki/Philip_the_Good" title="Philip the Good">Philip the Good</a> of Burgundy &#8212; who was also Count of Flanders &#8212; to conquer Holland.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Burgundian_and_.28Spanish.29_Habsburg_Netherlands_.281384.E2.80.931581.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Burgundian_and_(Spanish)_Habsburg_Netherlands_(1384&#8211;1581)">Burgundian and (Spanish) Habsburg Netherlands (1384&#8211;1581)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Burgundian and (Spanish) Habsburg Netherlands (1384&#8211;1581)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Burgundian_Netherlands" title="Burgundian Netherlands">Burgundian Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Netherlands" title="Habsburg Netherlands">Habsburg Netherlands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Netherlands" title="Spanish Netherlands">Spanish Netherlands</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Spanish Netherlands</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:240px;max-width:240px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:175px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Van_Soest,_Four_Days_Battle.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="516" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg/238px-Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg/357px-Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg/476px-Van_Soest%2C_Four_Days_Battle.jpg 2x" width="238"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><i>The <a href="/wiki/Four_Days%27_Battle" title="Four Days\' Battle">Four Days\' Battle</a>, 1&#8211;4 June 1666</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Anglo%E2%80%93Dutch_War" title="Second Anglo&#8211;Dutch War">Second Anglo&#8211;Dutch War</a>) by <a href="/wiki/Pieter_Cornelisz_van_Soest" title="Pieter Cornelisz van Soest">Pieter Cornelisz van Soest</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:123px;max-width:123px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:155px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_(1350)-NL.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3608" data-file-width="2818" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg/121px-Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg/182px-Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg/242px-Political_map_of_the_Low_Countries_%281350%29-NL.svg.png 2x" width="121"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The Low Countries in the late 14th century.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:115px;max-width:115px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:155px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:William_I,_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="6728" data-file-width="4876" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg/113px-William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg/170px-William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg/226px-William_I%2C_Prince_of_Orange_by_Adriaen_Thomasz._Key_Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam_SK-A-3148.jpg 2x" width="113"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">William I, Prince of Orange (<a href="/wiki/William_the_Silent" title="William the Silent">William the Silent</a>), leader of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Revolt" title="Dutch Revolt">Dutch Revolt</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Most of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Imperial</a> and <a href="/wiki/France_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="France in the Middle Ages">French</a> fiefs in what is now the Netherlands and Belgium were united in a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> by Philip the Good, Duke of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Burgundy" title="Duchy of Burgundy">Burgundy</a> in 1433. The <a href="/wiki/House_of_Valois-Burgundy" title="House of Valois-Burgundy">House of Valois-Burgundy</a> and their <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Habsburg</a> heirs would rule the Low Countries in the period from 1384 to 1581. Before the Burgundian union, the Dutch identified themselves by the town they lived in or their local duchy or county. The Burgundian period is when the road to nationhood began. The new rulers defended Dutch trading interests, which then developed rapidly. The fleets of the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Holland" title="County of Holland">County of Holland</a> defeated the fleets of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a> several times. <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> grew and in the 15th century became the primary trading port in Europe for grain from the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_region" title="Baltic region">Baltic region</a>. Amsterdam distributed grain to the major cities of Belgium, Northern France and England. This trade was vital, because Holland could no longer produce enough grain to feed itself. Land drainage had caused the <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> of the former <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a> to reduce to a level that was too low for drainage to be maintained.\n</p><p>Under Habsburg <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a>, ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> and King of <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Spain" title="Habsburg Spain">Spain</a>, all fiefs in the current Netherlands region were united into the <a href="/wiki/Seventeen_Provinces" title="Seventeen Provinces">Seventeen Provinces</a>, which also included most of present-day Belgium, Luxembourg, and some adjacent land in what is now France and Germany. In 1568, the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years\' War">Eighty Years\' War</a> between the Provinces and their <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> ruler began. The level of ferocity exhibited by both sides can be gleaned from a Dutch chronicler\'s report:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[55]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<blockquote><p> On more than one occasion men were seen hanging their own brothers, who had been taken prisoners in the enemy\'s ranks.... A Spaniard had ceased to be human in their eyes. On one occasion, a surgeon at Veer cut the heart from a Spanish prisoner, nailed it on a vessel\'s prow, and invited the townsmen to come and fasten their teeth in it, which many did with savage satisfaction. </p></blockquote>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fernando_%C3%81lvarez_de_Toledo,_3rd_Duke_of_Alba" title="Fernando &#193;lvarez de Toledo, 3rd Duke of Alba">Duke of Alba</a> ruthlessly attempted to suppress the Protestant movement in the Netherlands. Netherlanders were &#8220;burned, strangled, beheaded, or buried alive&#8221; by his &#8220;<a href="/wiki/Council_of_Troubles" title="Council of Troubles">Blood Council</a>&#8221; and his Spanish soldiers. Severed heads and decapitated corpses were displayed along streets and roads to terrorize the population into submission. Alba boasted of having executed 18,600,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[56]</a></sup> but this figure does not include those who perished by war and famine.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Habsburg_Map_1547.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1029" data-file-width="1654" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Habsburg_Map_1547.jpg/220px-Habsburg_Map_1547.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Habsburg_Map_1547.jpg/330px-Habsburg_Map_1547.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Habsburg_Map_1547.jpg/440px-Habsburg_Map_1547.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Habsburg_Map_1547.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of the dominion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">Habsburgs</a>. From 1556 the dynasty\'s lands in the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> were retained by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Habsburgs" title="Spanish Habsburgs">Spanish Habsburgs</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beleg_van_Maastricht_(1579),_Johann_Jakob_Wick_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="382" data-file-width="565" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Beleg_van_Maastricht_%281579%29%2C_Johann_Jakob_Wick_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Beleg_van_Maastricht_%281579%29%2C_Johann_Jakob_Wick_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Beleg_van_Maastricht_%281579%29%2C_Johann_Jakob_Wick_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Beleg_van_Maastricht_%281579%29%2C_Johann_Jakob_Wick_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Beleg_van_Maastricht_%281579%29%2C_Johann_Jakob_Wick_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Beleg_van_Maastricht_%281579%29%2C_Johann_Jakob_Wick_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beleg_van_Maastricht_(1579),_Johann_Jakob_Wick_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Fury" title="Spanish Fury">Spanish Fury</a> at <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Maastricht_(1579)" title="Siege of Maastricht (1579)">Maastricht</a> in 1579</div></div></div>\n<p>The first great siege was Alba\'s effort to capture <a href="/wiki/Haarlem" title="Haarlem">Haarlem</a> and thereby cut Holland in half. It dragged on from December 1572 to the next summer, when Haarlemers finally surrendered on 13 July upon promise that the city would be spared from being sacked. It was a stipulation <a href="/wiki/Fadrique_%C3%81lvarez_de_Toledo,_4th_Duke_of_Alba" title="Fadrique &#193;lvarez de Toledo, 4th Duke of Alba">Don Fadrique</a> was unable to honor, when his soldiers mutinied, angered over pay owed and the miserable conditions they endured during the long, cold months of the campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[57]</a></sup> On 4 November 1576, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Tercio" title="Tercio">tercios</a> seized <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> and subjected it to the worst pillage in the Netherlands\' history. The citizens resisted, but were overcome; seven thousand of them were mowed down; a thousand buildings were torched; men, women, and children were slaughtered in a delirium of blood by soldiers crying, "Santiago! Espa&#241;a! A sangre, a carne, a fuego, a sacco!" (Saint James! Spain! To blood, to the flesh, to fire, to sack!)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[58]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Antwerp" title="Sack of Antwerp">sack of Antwerp</a>, delegates from Catholic Brabant and Protestant Holland and Zeeland agreed, at Ghent, to join Utrecht and William the Silent in driving out all Spanish troops and forming a new government for the Netherlands. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Don_Juan_of_Austria" title="Don Juan of Austria">Don Juan of Austria</a>, the new Spanish governor, was forced to concede initially, but within months returned to active hostilities. As the fighting restarted, the Dutch began to look for help from the Queen of England, but she initially stood by her commitments to the Spanish in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Bristol" title="Treaty of Bristol">Treaty of Bristol</a> of 1574. The result was that when the next large-scale battle did occur at <a href="/wiki/Gembloux" title="Gembloux">Gembloux</a> in 1578, the Spanish forces easily won the day, killing at least 10,000 rebels, with the Spanish suffering few losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[59]</a></sup> In light of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gembloux_(1578)" title="Battle of Gembloux (1578)">defeat at Gembloux</a>, the southern states of the Seventeen Provinces (today in northern France and Belgium) distanced themselves from the rebels in the north with the 1579 <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Arras" title="Union of Arras">Union of Arras</a>, which expressed their loyalty to <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a>. Opposing them, the northern half of the Seventeen Provinces forged the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Utrecht" title="Union of Utrecht">Union of Utrecht</a> (also of 1579) in which they committed to support each other in their defence against the Spanish army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[60]</a></sup> The Union of Utrecht is seen as the foundation of the modern Netherlands.\n</p><p>Spanish troops sacked <a href="/wiki/Maastricht" title="Maastricht">Maastricht</a> in 1579, killing over 10,000 civilians and thereby ensuring the rebellion continued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[61]</a></sup> In 1581, the northern provinces adopted the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Abjuration" title="Act of Abjuration">Act of Abjuration</a>, the declaration of independence in which the provinces officially deposed Philip II as reigning monarch in the northern provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[62]</a></sup> Against the rebels Philip could draw on the resources of Spain, Spanish America, Spanish Italy and the Spanish Netherlands. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I of England</a> sympathised with the Dutch struggle against the Spanish, and sent an army of 7,600 soldiers to aid the Dutch in their war with the Catholic Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[63]</a></sup> English forces under the Earl of Leicester and then Lord Willoughby faced the Spanish in the Netherlands under the <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Farnese,_Duke_of_Parma" title="Alexander Farnese, Duke of Parma">Duke of Parma</a> in a series of largely indecisive actions that tied down significant numbers of Spanish troops and bought time for the Dutch to reorganise their defenses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[64]</a></sup> The war continued until 1648, when Spain under King <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_Spain" title="Philip IV of Spain">Philip IV</a> finally recognised the independence of the seven north-western provinces in the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_M%C3%BCnster" title="Peace of M&#252;nster">Peace of M&#252;nster</a>. Parts of the southern provinces became <i>de facto</i> colonies of the new republican-mercantile empire.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Dutch_Republic_.281581.E2.80.931795.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_Republic_(1581&#8211;1795)">Dutch Republic (1581&#8211;1795)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Dutch Republic (1581&#8211;1795)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_the_Dutch_Empire" title="Evolution of the Dutch Empire">Evolution of the Dutch Empire</a></div>\n<p>After declaring their independence, the provinces of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Holland" title="County of Holland">Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Zeeland" title="County of Zeeland">Zeeland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Groningen" title="Lordship of Groningen">Groningen</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Friesland" title="Lordship of Friesland">Friesland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Utrecht" title="Lordship of Utrecht">Utrecht</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Overijssel" title="Lordship of Overijssel">Overijssel</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Gelderland" title="Duchy of Gelderland">Gelderland</a> formed a <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederation</a>. All these duchies, lordships and counties were autonomous and had their own government, the <a href="/wiki/States-Provincial" title="States-Provincial">States-Provincial</a>. The <a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">States General</a>, the confederal government, were seated in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> and consisted of representatives from each of the seven provinces. The sparsely populated region of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Drenthe" title="Lordship of Drenthe">Drenthe</a> was part of the republic too, although it was not considered one of the provinces. Moreover, the Republic had come to occupy during the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years\' War">Eighty Years\' War</a> a number of so-called <a href="/wiki/Generality_Lands" title="Generality Lands">Generality Lands</a> in <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">Flanders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brabant" title="Duchy of Brabant">Brabant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Limburg" title="Duchy of Limburg">Limburg</a>. Their population was mainly Roman Catholic, and these areas did not have a governmental structure of their own, and were used as a buffer zone between the Republic and the Spanish-controlled <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Southern Netherlands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[65]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1232" data-file-width="2303" decoding="async" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg/220px-Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg/330px-Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg/440px-Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hendrick_Avercamp_-_Winterlandschap_met_schaatsers_bij_de_stad_Kampen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Winter landscape with skaters near the city of <a href="/wiki/Kampen,_Overijssel" title="Kampen, Overijssel">Kampen</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_Avercamp" title="Hendrick Avercamp">Hendrick Avercamp</a> (1620s)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1475" data-file-width="2505" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg/220px-Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg"
