srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg/330px-Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg/440px-Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Johannes_Lingelbach_001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Dam_Square" title="Dam Square">Dam Square</a> in 1656</div></div></div>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a>, spanning much of the 17th century, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a> grew to become one of the major seafaring and economic powers, alongside Portugal, Spain, France and England. Science, military, and art (especially <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age_painting" title="Dutch Golden Age painting">painting</a>) were among the most acclaimed in the world. By 1650, the Dutch-owned 16,000 merchant ships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[66]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a> established <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">colonies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading posts</a> all over the world, including ruling the northern parts of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_under_Dutch_rule" title="Taiwan under Dutch rule">1624&#8211;1662 and 1664&#8211;1667</a>. The <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">Dutch settlement in North America</a> began with the founding of <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a> on the southern part of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> in 1614. In South Africa, the Dutch settled the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a> in 1652. <a href="/wiki/Dutch_colonisation_of_the_Guianas" title="Dutch colonisation of the Guianas">Dutch colonies in South America</a> were established along the many rivers in the fertile <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> plains, among them <a href="/wiki/Surinam_(Dutch_colony)" title="Surinam (Dutch colony)">Colony of Surinam</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>). In Asia, the Dutch established the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>), and the only western trading post in Japan, <a href="/wiki/Dejima" title="Dejima">Dejima</a>.\n</p><p>Many economic historians regard the Netherlands as the first thoroughly <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> country in the world. In early modern Europe it had the wealthiest trading city (<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>) and the first full-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">stock exchange</a>. The inventiveness of the traders led to insurance and retirement funds as well as phenomena such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boom_and_bust" title="Boom and bust">boom-bust cycle</a>, the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Asset_price_inflation" title="Asset price inflation">asset-inflation bubble</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tulip_mania" title="Tulip mania">tulip mania</a> of 1636&#8211;1637, and the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Bear_raid" title="Bear raid">bear raider</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isaac_le_Maire" title="Isaac le Maire">Isaac le Maire</a>, who forced prices down by dumping stock and then buying it back at a discount.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[67]</a></sup> In 1672 &#8211; known in Dutch history as the <a href="/wiki/Rampjaar" title="Rampjaar">Rampjaar</a> (Disaster Year) &#8211; the Dutch Republic was at war with France, England and three German Bishoprics simultaneously. At sea it could successfully prevent the English and French navy entering the western shores. On land, however, it was almost taken over internally by the advancing French and German armies coming from the east. It managed to turn the tide by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hollandic_Water_Line" title="Hollandic Water Line">inundating parts of Holland</a>, but could never recover to its former glory again and went into a state of general decline in the 18th century, with economic competition from England and long-standing rivalries between the two main factions in Dutch society, the republican <a href="/wiki/Dutch_States_Party" title="Dutch States Party"><i>Staatsgezinden</i></a> and the supporters of the <a href="/wiki/Stadtholder" title="Stadtholder">stadtholder</a> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orangism_(Netherlands)" title="Orangism (Netherlands)"><i>Prinsgezinden</i></a>, as main <a href="/wiki/Political_faction" title="Political faction">political factions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[68]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Batavian_Republic_and_Kingdom_.281795.E2.80.931890.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Batavian_Republic_and_Kingdom_(1795&#8211;1890)">Batavian Republic and Kingdom (1795&#8211;1890)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Batavian Republic and Kingdom (1795&#8211;1890)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Batavian_Republic" title="Batavian Republic">Batavian Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Holland" title="Kingdom of Holland">Kingdom of Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Principality_of_the_United_Netherlands" title="Sovereign Principality of the United Netherlands">Sovereign Principality of the United Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">United Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<p>With the armed support of <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">revolutionary France</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patriots_(Dutch_Republic)" title="Patriots (Dutch Republic)">Dutch republicans</a> proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Batavian_Republic" title="Batavian Republic">Batavian Republic</a>, modelled after the <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">French Republic</a> and rendering the Netherlands a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a> on 19 January 1795. The <a href="/wiki/Stadtholder" title="Stadtholder">stadtholder</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_V_of_Orange" title="William V of Orange">William V of Orange</a> had fled to England. But from 1806 to 1810, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Holland" title="Kingdom of Holland">Kingdom of Holland</a> was set up by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> as a puppet kingdom governed by his brother <a href="/wiki/Louis_Bonaparte" title="Louis Bonaparte">Louis Bonaparte</a> to control the Netherlands more effectively. However, King Louis Bonaparte tried to serve Dutch interests instead of his brother\'s, and he was forced to abdicate on 1 July 1810. The Emperor sent in an army and the Netherlands became part of the French Empire until the autumn of 1813, when Napoleon was defeated in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leipzig" title="Battle of Leipzig">Battle of Leipzig</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dutch_Empire35.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="893" data-file-width="1678" decoding="async" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Dutch_Empire35.PNG/220px-Dutch_Empire35.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Dutch_Empire35.PNG/330px-Dutch_Empire35.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Dutch_Empire35.PNG/440px-Dutch_Empire35.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dutch_Empire35.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch colonial empire</a>. Light green: territories administered by or originating from territories administered by the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a>; dark green: the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a>. In yellow are the territories occupied later, during the 19th century.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/William_I_of_the_Netherlands" title="William I of the Netherlands">William Frederick</a>, son of the last stadtholder, returned to the Netherlands in 1813 and proclaimed himself <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Principality_of_the_United_Netherlands" title="Sovereign Principality of the United Netherlands">Sovereign Prince of the Netherlands</a>. Two years later, the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> added the southern Netherlands to the north to create a strong country on the northern border of France. William Frederick raised this <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">United Netherlands</a> to the status of a kingdom and proclaimed himself <a href="/wiki/William_I_of_the_Netherlands" title="William I of the Netherlands">King William I</a> in 1815. In addition, William became hereditary <a href="/wiki/Grand_Ducal_Family_of_Luxembourg" title="Grand Ducal Family of Luxembourg">Grand Duke of Luxembourg</a> in exchange for his German possessions. However, the Southern Netherlands had been culturally separate from the north since 1581, and <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Revolution" title="Belgian Revolution">rebelled</a>. The south gained independence in 1830 as Belgium (recognised by the Northern Netherlands in 1839 as the Kingdom of the Netherlands was created by decree), while the <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> between Luxembourg and the Netherlands was severed in 1890, when <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_the_Netherlands" title="William III of the Netherlands">William III</a> died with no surviving male heirs. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salic_Law" title="Salic Law">Ascendancy laws</a> prevented his daughter <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmina_of_the_Netherlands" title="Wilhelmina of the Netherlands">Queen Wilhelmina</a> from becoming the next Grand Duchess.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4608" data-file-width="6124" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg/220px-Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg/330px-Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg/440px-Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The submission of <a href="/wiki/Diponegoro" title="Diponegoro">Diponegoro</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Merkus_de_Kock" title="Hendrik Merkus de Kock">General De Kock</a> at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Java_War" title="Java War">Java War</a> in 1830; <a href="/wiki/The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock" title="The Submission of Prince Dipo Negoro to General De Kock">painting</a> by <a href="/wiki/Nicolaas_Pieneman" title="Nicolaas Pieneman">Nicolaas Pieneman</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Belgian Revolution at home and the <a href="/wiki/Java_War" title="Java War">Java War</a> in the Dutch East Indies brought the Netherlands to the brink of bankruptcy. However, the <a href="/wiki/Cultivation_System" title="Cultivation System">Cultivation System</a> was introduced in 1830; in the Dutch East Indies, 20% of village land had to be devoted to government crops for export. The policy brought the Dutch enormous wealth and made the colony self-sufficient. \n</p><p>The Netherlands abolished slavery in 1863,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[69]</a></sup> as the last country in Europe to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[70]</a></sup> Furthermore, slaves in <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> would be fully free only in 1873, since the law stipulated that there was to be a mandatory 10-year transition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[71]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Dutch were also one of the last European countries to <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">industrialise</a>, in the second half of the 19th century.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="World_wars_and_beyond_.281890.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_wars_and_beyond_(1890&#8211;present)">World wars and beyond (1890&#8211;present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: World wars and beyond (1890&#8211;present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Netherlands_(1900%E2%80%93present)" title="History of the Netherlands (1900&#8211;present)">History of the Netherlands (1900&#8211;present)</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Netherlands_in_World_War_I" title="The Netherlands in World War I">The Netherlands in World War I</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_in_World_War_II" title="Netherlands in World War II">Netherlands in World War II</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rotterdam,_Laurenskerk,_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2269" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg/220px-Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg/330px-Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg/440px-Rotterdam%2C_Laurenskerk%2C_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rotterdam,_Laurenskerk,_na_bombardement_van_mei_1940.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rotterdam_Blitz" title="Rotterdam Blitz">German air raids</a> in 1940</div></div></div>\n<p>The Netherlands were able to remain neutral during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, in part because the import of goods through the Netherlands proved essential to German survival, until the blockade by the British Royal Navy in 1916.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abbenhuis_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Abbenhuis-81">[72]</a></sup> That changed in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Netherlands" title="Battle of the Netherlands">invaded the Netherlands</a> on 10 May 1940. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rotterdam_Blitz" title="Rotterdam Blitz">Rotterdam Blitz</a> forced the main element of the Dutch army to surrender four days later. During the occupation, over 100,000 <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Netherlands" title="History of the Jews in the Netherlands">Dutch Jews</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[73]</a></sup> were rounded up and transported to Nazi <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">extermination camps</a>; only a few of them survived. Dutch workers were conscripted for forced labour in Germany, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_resistance" title="Dutch resistance">civilians who resisted</a> were killed in reprisal for attacks on German soldiers, and the countryside was plundered for food. Although there were thousands of Dutch who risked their lives by hiding Jews from the Germans, over 20,000 Dutch fascists <a href="/wiki/23rd_SS_Volunteer_Panzer_Grenadier_Division_Nederland" title="23rd SS Volunteer Panzer Grenadier Division Nederland">joined the Waffen SS</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[74]</a></sup> fighting on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[75]</a></sup> Political <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collaboration_with_the_Axis_Powers_during_World_War_II" title="Collaboration with the Axis Powers during World War II">collaborators</a> were members of the <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Movement_in_the_Netherlands" title="National Socialist Movement in the Netherlands">NSB</a>, the only legal political party in the occupied Netherlands. On 8 December 1941, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_government-in-exile" title="Dutch government-in-exile">Dutch government-in-exile</a> in London declared war on Japan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[76]</a></sup> but could not prevent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_Indonesia" title="Japanese occupation of Indonesia">the Japanese occupation of the Dutch East Indies (Indonesia)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[77]</a></sup> In 1944&#8211;45, the <a href="/wiki/First_Canadian_Army" title="First Canadian Army">First Canadian Army</a>, which included Canadian, <a href="/wiki/I_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="I Corps (United Kingdom)">British</a> and <a href="/wiki/1st_Armoured_Division_(Poland)" title="1st Armoured Division (Poland)">Polish</a> troops, was responsible for liberating much of the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[78]</a></sup> Soon after <a href="/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">VE Day</a>, the Dutch fought a <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">colonial war against the new Republic of Indonesia</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kok_VanAgt_DeJong_Rutte_Lubbers_Balkenende.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2608" data-file-width="3712" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Kok_VanAgt_DeJong_Rutte_Lubbers_Balkenende.jpg/220px-Kok_VanAgt_DeJong_Rutte_Lubbers_Balkenende.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Kok_VanAgt_DeJong_Rutte_Lubbers_Balkenende.jpg/330px-Kok_VanAgt_DeJong_Rutte_Lubbers_Balkenende.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Kok_VanAgt_DeJong_Rutte_Lubbers_Balkenende.jpg/440px-Kok_VanAgt_DeJong_Rutte_Lubbers_Balkenende.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kok_VanAgt_DeJong_Rutte_Lubbers_Balkenende.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former Prime Ministers <a href="/wiki/Wim_Kok" title="Wim Kok">Wim Kok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dries_van_Agt" title="Dries van Agt">Dries van Agt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piet_de_Jong" title="Piet de Jong">Piet de Jong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Lubbers" title="Ruud Lubbers">Ruud Lubbers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jan_Peter_Balkenende" title="Jan Peter Balkenende">Jan Peter Balkenende</a> with Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Mark_Rutte" title="Mark Rutte">Mark Rutte</a>, in 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1954, the <a href="/wiki/Charter_for_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Charter for the Kingdom of the Netherlands">Charter for the Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> reformed the political structure of the Netherlands, which was a result of international pressure to carry out <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonisation" title="Decolonisation">decolonisation</a>. The Dutch colonies of <a href="/wiki/Surinam_(Dutch_colony)" title="Surinam (Dutch colony)">Surinam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_and_Dependencies" title="Cura&#231;ao and Dependencies">Cura&#231;ao and Dependencies</a> and the European country all became countries within the Kingdom, on a basis of equality. Indonesia had declared its independence in August 1945 (recognised in 1949), and thus was never part of the reformed Kingdom. <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> followed in 1975. After the war the Netherlands left behind an era of neutrality and gained closer ties with neighboring states. The Netherlands was one of the founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euratom" title="Euratom">Euratom</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a>, which would evolve into the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">EEC</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_Market" title="Common Market">Common Market</a>) and later the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.\n</p><p>Government-encouraged emigration efforts to reduce <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> prompted some 500,000 <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch people</a> to leave the country after the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[79]</a></sup> The 1960s and 1970s were a time of great social and cultural change, such as rapid <i>ontzuiling</i> (end of <a href="/wiki/Pillarisation" title="Pillarisation">pillarisation</a>), a term that describes the decay of the old divisions along political and religious lines. Youths, and students in particular, rejected traditional mores and pushed for change in matters such as <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women\'s rights">women\'s rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_sexuality" title="Human sexuality">sexuality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disarmament" title="Disarmament">disarmament</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_issues" title="Environmental issues">environmental issues</a>. In 2002, the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> was introduced as <a href="/wiki/Fiat_money" title="Fiat money">fiat money</a> and in 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a> was <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Netherlands_Antilles" title="Dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles">dissolved</a>. Referendums were held on each island to determine their future status. As a result, the islands of <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a> (the BES islands) were to obtain closer ties with the Netherlands. This led to the incorporation of these three islands into the country of the Netherlands as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_municipality_(Netherlands)" title="Special municipality (Netherlands)">special municipalities</a></i> upon the dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles. The special municipalities are collectively known as the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Netherlands" title="Geography of the Netherlands">Geography of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3440" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg/220px-2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg/330px-2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg/440px-2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2012-NL-prov-relief-3000.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A relief map of the European Netherlands</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the Central Bureau of Statistics, the European Netherlands has a total land area of 41,528&#160;km<sup>2</sup>, including non-tidal water bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[80]</a></sup> It lies between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latitudes" title="Latitudes">latitudes</a> <a href="/wiki/50th_parallel_north" title="50th parallel north">50&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/54th_parallel_north" title="54th parallel north">54&#176; N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/3rd_meridian_east" title="3rd meridian east">3&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/8th_meridian_east" title="8th meridian east">8&#176; E</a>.\n</p><p>The Netherlands is geographically a very low and flat country, with about 26% of its area<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[81]</a></sup> and 21% of its population<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milrek_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-milrek-91">[82]</a></sup> located below sea level, and only about 50% of its land exceeding one metre <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eupedia_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Eupedia-25">[17]</a></sup> The European part of the country is for the most part flat, with the exception of foothills in the far southeast, up to a height of no more than 321 metres, and some low hill ranges in the central parts. Most of the areas below sea level are man-made, caused by <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> extraction or achieved through <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a>. Since the late 16th century, large <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">polder</a> areas are preserved through elaborate drainage systems that include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dike_(construction)" title="Dike (construction)">dikes</a>, canals and pumping stations. Nearly 17% of the country\'s land area is reclaimed from the sea and from lakes.\n</p><p>Much of the country was originally formed by the <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuaries</a> of three large European rivers: the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> (<i>Rijn</i>), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meuse_River" title="Meuse River">Meuse</a> (<i>Maas</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a> (<i>Schelde</i>), as well as their <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributaries</a>. The south-western part of the Netherlands is to this day a <a href="/wiki/River_delta" title="River delta">river delta</a> of these three rivers, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhine-Meuse-Scheldt_delta" title="Rhine-Meuse-Scheldt delta">Rhine-Meuse-Scheldt delta</a>.\n</p><p>The European Netherlands is divided into north and south parts by the Rhine, the <a href="/wiki/Waal_(river)" title="Waal (river)">Waal</a>, its main tributary branch, and the Meuse. In the past these rivers functioned as a natural barrier between <a href="/wiki/Fief" title="Fief">fiefdoms</a> and hence historically created a cultural divide, as is evident in some phonetic traits that are recognisable on either side of what the Dutch call their "Great Rivers" (<i>de Grote Rivieren</i>). Another significant branch of the Rhine, the <a href="/wiki/IJssel" title="IJssel">IJssel</a> river, discharges into <a href="/wiki/IJsselmeer" title="IJsselmeer">Lake IJssel</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/Zuiderzee" title="Zuiderzee">Zuiderzee</a> (\'southern sea\'). Just like the previous, this river forms a linguistic divide: people to the northeast of this river speak <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Low_Saxon" title="Dutch Low Saxon">Dutch Low Saxon</a> dialects (except for the province of <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a>, which has its own language).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-international2000_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-international2000-92">[83]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Floods">Floods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Floods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Flood_control_in_the_Netherlands" title="Flood control in the Netherlands">Flood control in the Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Floods_in_the_Netherlands" title="Floods in the Netherlands">Floods in the Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_flood_of_1953" title="North Sea flood of 1953">North Sea flood of 1953</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Storm_tides_of_the_North_Sea" title="Storm tides of the North Sea">Storm tides of the North Sea</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Christmas_flood_1717.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2370" data-file-width="3863" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Christmas_flood_1717.jpg/220px-Christmas_flood_1717.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Christmas_flood_1717.jpg/330px-Christmas_flood_1717.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Christmas_flood_1717.jpg/440px-Christmas_flood_1717.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Christmas_flood_1717.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christmas_flood_of_1717" title="Christmas flood of 1717">Christmas flood of 1717</a> was the result of a northwesterly storm that resulted in the death of thousands.</div></div></div>\n<p>Over the centuries, the Dutch coastline has changed considerably as a result of natural disasters and human intervention. Most notable in terms of land loss was the storm of 1134<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, which created the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> of <a href="/wiki/Zeeland" title="Zeeland">Zeeland</a> in the south-west.\n</p><p>On 14 December 1287, <a href="/wiki/St._Lucia%27s_flood" title="St. Lucia\'s flood">St. Lucia\'s flood</a> affected the Netherlands and Germany, killing more than 50,000 people in one of the most destructive floods in recorded history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[84]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/St._Elizabeth%27s_flood_(1421)" title="St. Elizabeth\'s flood (1421)">St. Elizabeth flood</a> of 1421 and the mismanagement in its aftermath destroyed a newly reclaimed <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">polder</a>, replacing it with the 72-square-kilometre (28&#160;sq&#160;mi) <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biesbosch" title="Biesbosch">Biesbosch</a></i> tidal floodplains in the south-centre. The huge <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_flood_of_1953" title="North Sea flood of 1953">North Sea flood of early February 1953</a> caused the collapse of several dikes in the south-west of the Netherlands; more than 1,800 people drowned in the flood. The Dutch government subsequently instituted a large-scale programme, the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deltawerken" title="Deltawerken">Delta Works</a>", to protect the country against future flooding, which was completed over a period of more than thirty years.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1003" data-file-width="962" decoding="async" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png/220px-The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png/330px-The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png/440px-The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Netherlands_compared_to_sealevel.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map illustrating European areas of the Netherlands below sea level</div></div></div>\n<p>The impact of disasters was to an extent increased through human activity. Relatively high-lying <a href="/wiki/Swamp" title="Swamp">swampland</a> was drained to be used as farmland. The drainage caused the fertile <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> to contract and ground levels to drop, upon which groundwater levels were lowered to compensate for the drop in ground level, causing the underlying peat to contract further. Additionally, until the 19th century peat was mined, dried, and used for fuel, further exacerbating the problem. Centuries of extensive and poorly controlled <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> extraction lowered an already low land surface by several metres. Even in flooded areas, peat extraction continued through turf dredging.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NL-zaanse-schans-wohnhaeuser.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/NL-zaanse-schans-wohnhaeuser.jpg/220px-NL-zaanse-schans-wohnhaeuser.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/NL-zaanse-schans-wohnhaeuser.jpg/330px-NL-zaanse-schans-wohnhaeuser.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/NL-zaanse-schans-wohnhaeuser.jpg/440px-NL-zaanse-schans-wohnhaeuser.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NL-zaanse-schans-wohnhaeuser.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Zaanse_Schans" title="Zaanse Schans">Zaanse Schans</a>, a touristic Dutch village built in an aquatic area</div></div></div>\n<p>Because of the flooding, farming was difficult, which encouraged foreign trade, the result of which was that the Dutch were involved in world affairs since the early 14th/15th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[85]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Netherlands,_Zoetermeer,_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_(1).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1140" data-file-width="1716" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG/220px-Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG/330px-Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG/440px-Netherlands%2C_Zoetermeer%2C_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_%281%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Netherlands,_Zoetermeer,_Zoetermeerse_Meerpolder_(1).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A polder at 5.53 metres below sea level</div></div></div>\n<p>To guard against floods, a series of defences against the water were contrived. In the first millennium <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AD" title="AD">AD</a>, villages and farmhouses were built on man-made hills called <i>terps</i>. Later, these terps were connected by dikes. In the 12th century, local government agencies called <i>"<a href="/wiki/Water_board_(Netherlands)" title="Water board (Netherlands)">waterschappen</a>"</i> ("water boards") or <i>"<a href="/wiki/Water_board_(Netherlands)" title="Water board (Netherlands)">hoogheemraadschappen</a>"</i> ("high home councils") started to appear, whose job it was to maintain the water level and to protect a region from floods; these agencies continue to exist. As the ground level dropped, the dikes by necessity grew and merged into an integrated system. By the 13th century <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">windmills</a> had come into use to pump water out of areas below sea level. The windmills were later used to drain lakes, creating the famous <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">polders</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[86]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1932 the <i><a href="/wiki/Afsluitdijk" title="Afsluitdijk">Afsluitdijk</a></i> ("Closure Dike") was completed, blocking the former <i><a href="/wiki/Zuiderzee" title="Zuiderzee">Zuiderzee</a></i> (Southern Sea) from the North Sea and thus creating the <a href="/wiki/IJsselmeer" title="IJsselmeer">IJsselmeer</a> (<a href="/wiki/IJssel" title="IJssel">IJssel</a> Lake). It became part of the larger <a href="/wiki/Zuiderzee_Works" title="Zuiderzee Works">Zuiderzee Works</a> in which four polders totalling 2,500 square kilometres (965&#160;sq&#160;mi) were reclaimed from the sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[88]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Netherlands is one of the countries that may suffer most from <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>. Not only is the rising sea a problem, but erratic weather patterns may cause the rivers to overflow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[91]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Delta_Works">Delta Works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Delta Works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Delta_Works" title="Delta Works">Delta Works</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flood_control_in_the_Netherlands" title="Flood control in the Netherlands">Flood control in the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Deltawerken_na.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1532" data-file-width="1622" decoding="async" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Deltawerken_na.png/220px-Deltawerken_na.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Deltawerken_na.png/330px-Deltawerken_na.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Deltawerken_na.png/440px-Deltawerken_na.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Deltawerken_na.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Delta_Works" title="Delta Works">Delta Works</a> are located in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/South_Holland" title="South Holland">South Holland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zeeland" title="Zeeland">Zeeland</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Sea_Flood_of_1953" title="North Sea Flood of 1953">1953 disaster</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Delta_Works" title="Delta Works">Delta Works</a> was constructed, a comprehensive set of civil works throughout the Dutch coast. The project started in 1958 and was largely completed in 1997 with the completion of the <a href="/wiki/Maeslantkering" title="Maeslantkering">Maeslantkering</a>. New projects have been periodically started since to renovate and renew the Delta Works. A main goal of the Delta project was to reduce the risk of flooding in South Holland and Zeeland to once per 10,000 years (compared to 1 per 4000 years for the rest of the country). This was achieved by raising 3,000 kilometres (1,864&#160;mi) of outer sea-dikes and 10,000 kilometres (6,214&#160;mi) of inner, canal, and river dikes, and by closing off the sea <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuaries</a> of the Zeeland province. New risk assessments occasionally show problems requiring additional Delta project dike reinforcements. The Delta project is considered by the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Civil_Engineers" title="American Society of Civil Engineers">American Society of Civil Engineers</a> as one of the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Civil_Engineers#World_wonders" title="American Society of Civil Engineers">seven wonders of the modern world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[92]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haringvlietdam-01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1188" data-file-width="1783" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Haringvlietdam-01.jpg/220px-Haringvlietdam-01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Haringvlietdam-01.jpg/330px-Haringvlietdam-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Haringvlietdam-01.jpg/440px-Haringvlietdam-01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haringvlietdam-01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Haringvlietdam" title="Haringvlietdam">Haringvlietdam</a>, completed in 1971</div></div></div>\n<p>It is anticipated that <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> in the 21st century will result in a rise in <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>. The Netherlands is actively preparing for a sea level rise. A politically neutral Delta Commission has formulated an action plan to cope with a sea level rise of 1.10 metres (3.6&#160;ft) and a simultaneous land height decline of 10 centimetres (3.9&#160;in). The plan encompasses the reinforcement of the existing coastal defences like <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">dikes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dune" title="Dune">dunes</a> with 1.30 metres (4.3&#160;ft) of additional flood protection. Climate change will not only threaten the Netherlands from the sea side, but could also alter rainfall patterns and river run-off. To protect the country from river flooding, another program is already being executed. The <a href="/wiki/Room_for_the_River_(Netherlands)" title="Room for the River (Netherlands)">Room for the River plan</a> grants more flow space to rivers, protects the major populated areas and allows for periodic flooding of indefensible lands. The few residents who lived in these so-called "overflow areas" have been moved to higher ground, with some of that ground having been raised above anticipated flood levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT021313_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT021313-102">[93]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The predominant wind direction in the European Netherlands is southwest, which causes a mild <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime climate</a>, with moderately warm summers and cool winters, and typically high humidity. This is especially true close to the Dutch coastline, where the difference in temperature between summer and winter, as well as between day and night is noticeably smaller than it is in the southeast of the country.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:240px;max-width:240px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:178px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2654" data-file-width="3539" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg/238px-Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg/357px-Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg/476px-Nijl%C3%A2nnermolen_Workum.jpg 2x" width="238"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Workum" title="Workum">Workum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:240px;max-width:240px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:158px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Floroj_en_Lisse.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4896" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Floroj_en_Lisse.jpg/238px-Floroj_en_Lisse.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Floroj_en_Lisse.jpg/357px-Floroj_en_Lisse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Floroj_en_Lisse.jpg/476px-Floroj_en_Lisse.jpg 2x" width="238"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Lisse" title="Lisse">Lisse</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Holland" title="South Holland">South Holland</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Ice days&#8212;maximum temperature below 0&#160;&#176;C (32&#160;&#176;F)&#8212;usually occur from December until February, with the occasional rare ice day prior to or after that period. Freezing days&#8212;minimum temperature below 0&#160;&#176;C (32&#160;&#176;F)&#8212;occur much more often, usually ranging from mid-November to late March, but not rarely measured as early as mid-October and as late as mid-May. If one chooses the height of measurement to be 10&#160;cm (4&#160;in) above ground instead of 150&#160;cm (59&#160;in), one may even find such temperatures in the middle of the summer. On average, snow can occur from November to April, but sometimes occurs in May or October too.\n</p><p>Warm days&#8212;maximum temperature above 20&#160;&#176;C (68&#160;&#176;F)&#8212;are usually found in April to October, but in some parts of the country these warm days can also occur in March, or even sometimes in November or February (usually not in De Bilt, however). Summer days&#8212;maximum temperature above 25&#160;&#176;C (77&#160;&#176;F)&#8212;are usually measured in De Bilt from May until September, tropical days&#8212;maximum temperature above 30&#160;&#176;C (86&#160;&#176;F)&#8212;are rare and usually occur only in June to August.\n</p><p>Precipitation throughout the year is distributed relatively equally each month. Summer and autumn months tend to gather a little more precipitation than the other months, mainly because of the intensity of the rainfall rather than the frequency of rain days (this is especially the case in summer, when lightning is also much more frequent).\n</p><p>The number of sunshine hours is affected by the fact that because of the geographical latitude, the length of the days varies between barely eight hours in December and nearly 17 hours in June.\n</p><p>The following tables are based on mean measurements by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KNMI_(institute)" title="KNMI (institute)">KNMI</a> weather station in <a href="/wiki/De_Bilt" title="De Bilt">De Bilt</a> between 1981 and 2010:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="width:100%; color:#FFFFFF;">62.3\n</td>\n<td style="background: #AAAAA7; color:#000000;">85.7\n</td>\n<td style="background: #B7B75B; color:#000000;">121.6\n</td>\n<td style="background: #D1D100; color:#000000;">173.6\n</td>\n<td style="background: #D9D900;
