color:#000000;">138.3\n</td>\n<td style="background: #B3B373; color:#000000;">112.9\n</td>\n<td style="background: #767676; color:#FFFFFF;">63.0\n</td>\n<td style="background: #5A5A5A; color:#FFFFFF;">49.3\n</td>\n<td style="background: #BDBD34; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">1,601.5\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: KNMI.nl<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-knmi_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-knmi-103">[94]</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nature">Nature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Nature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_the_Netherlands" title="List of national parks of the Netherlands">List of national parks of the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_extinct_animals_of_the_Netherlands" title="List of extinct animals of the Netherlands">List of extinct animals of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<p>The Netherlands has 20 national parks and hundreds of other nature reserves, that include <a href="/wiki/Lake" title="Lake">lakes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heathland" title="Heathland">heathland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodland" title="Woodland">woods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dune" title="Dune">dunes</a> and other habitats. Most of these are owned by <a href="/wiki/Staatsbosbeheer" title="Staatsbosbeheer">Staatsbosbeheer</a>, the national department for <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habitat_conservation" title="Habitat conservation">nature conservation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vereniging_Natuurmonumenten" title="Vereniging Natuurmonumenten">Natuurmonumenten</a> (literally \'Natures monuments\'), a private organisation that buys, protects and manages nature reserves. The Dutch part of the <a href="/wiki/Wadden_Sea" title="Wadden Sea">Wadden Sea</a> in the north, with its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidal_flat" title="Tidal flat">tidal flats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a>, is rich in <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biological diversity</a>, and was declared a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Nature Site</a> in 2009.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1707" data-file-width="2856" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg/220px-Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg/330px-Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg/440px-Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phoca_vitulina_Terschelling.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Harbor_seal" title="Harbor seal">Common seals</a> on <a href="/wiki/Terschelling" title="Terschelling">Terschelling</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Wadden_Sea" title="Wadden Sea">Wadden Sea</a> island</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oosterschelde" title="Oosterschelde">Oosterschelde</a>, formerly the northeast <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuary</a> of the river <a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a> was designated a national park in 2002, thereby making it the largest national park in the Netherlands at an area of 370 square kilometres (140&#160;sq&#160;mi). It consists primarily of the salt waters of the Oosterschelde, but also includes mud flats, meadows, and shoals. Because of the large variety of sea life, including unique regional species, the park is popular with <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">Scuba divers</a>. Other activities include sailing, fishing, cycling, and bird watching.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, the European Netherlands is shared between the Atlantic European and Central European provinces of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wide Fund for Nature</a>, the European territory of the Netherlands belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> of Atlantic mixed forests. In 1871, the last old original natural woods were cut down, and most woods today are planted monocultures of trees like <a href="/wiki/Scots_pine" title="Scots pine">Scots pine</a> and trees that are not native to the Netherlands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These woods were planted on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heath_(habitat)#Anthropogenic_heaths" title="Heath (habitat)">anthropogenic heaths</a> and sand-drifts (overgrazed heaths) (<a href="/wiki/Veluwe" title="Veluwe">Veluwe</a>).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Caribbean_islands">Caribbean islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Caribbean islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a></div>\n<p>While <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Cura&#231;ao">Cura&#231;ao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a> have a <a href="/wiki/Constituent_state" title="Constituent state">constituent country</a> status, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a> are three islands designated as special municipalities of the Netherlands. The islands are part of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> and have land and maritime borders with <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (<a href="/wiki/Collectivity_of_Saint_Martin" title="Collectivity of Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>), maritime borders with France (<a href="/wiki/Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint Barth&#233;lemy">Saint Barth&#233;lemy</a>), the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (<a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>), <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (<a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[95]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kleine_Bonaire-Underwater_life(js).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4636" data-file-width="10000" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Kleine_Bonaire-Underwater_life%28js%29.jpg/280px-Kleine_Bonaire-Underwater_life%28js%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Kleine_Bonaire-Underwater_life%28js%29.jpg/420px-Kleine_Bonaire-Underwater_life%28js%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Kleine_Bonaire-Underwater_life%28js%29.jpg/560px-Kleine_Bonaire-Underwater_life%28js%29.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kleine_Bonaire-Underwater_life(js).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Underwater life of <a href="/wiki/Klein_Bonaire" title="Klein Bonaire">Klein Bonaire</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Within this island group:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a> is part of the <a href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">ABC islands</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Antilles" title="Leeward Antilles">Leeward Antilles</a> island chain off the <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuelan</a> coast. The Leeward Antilles have a mixed volcanic and coral origin.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> are part of the <a href="/wiki/SSS_islands" title="SSS islands">SSS islands</a>. They are located east of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a>. Although in the English language they are considered part of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>, French, Spanish, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> and the English spoken locally consider them part of the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a>. The Windward Islands are all of volcanic origin and hilly, leaving little ground suitable for <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Scenery" title="Mount Scenery">Mount Scenery</a>, 887 metres (2,910&#160;ft), on <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>. This is the highest point in the country, and is also the highest point of the entire <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>The islands of the Caribbean Netherlands enjoy a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical" title="Tropical">tropical</a> <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> with warm weather all year round. The Leeward Antilles are warmer and drier than the Windward islands. In summer, the Windward Islands can be subject to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricanes" title="Hurricanes">hurricanes</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Den_Haag_-_panoramio_-_Nikolai_Karaneschev.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Den_Haag_-_panoramio_-_Nikolai_Karaneschev.jpg/220px-Den_Haag_-_panoramio_-_Nikolai_Karaneschev.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Den_Haag_-_panoramio_-_Nikolai_Karaneschev.jpg/330px-Den_Haag_-_panoramio_-_Nikolai_Karaneschev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Den_Haag_-_panoramio_-_Nikolai_Karaneschev.jpg/440px-Den_Haag_-_panoramio_-_Nikolai_Karaneschev.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Den_Haag_-_panoramio_-_Nikolai_Karaneschev.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Binnenhof" title="Binnenhof">Binnenhof</a>, where the lower and upper houses of the States General meet</div></div></div>\n<p>The Netherlands has been a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> since 1815, and due to the efforts of <a href="/wiki/Johan_Rudolph_Thorbecke" title="Johan Rudolph Thorbecke">Johan Rudolph Thorbecke</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRC_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-NRC-105">[96]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democracy</a> since 1848. The Netherlands is described as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consociational_state" title="Consociational state">consociational state</a>. Dutch politics and governance are characterised by an effort to achieve broad consensus on important issues, within both the political community and society as a whole. In 2017, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> ranked the Netherlands as the 11th <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">most democratic country in the world</a>.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_monarchy" title="Dutch monarchy">monarch</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, at present King <a href="/wiki/Willem-Alexander_of_the_Netherlands" title="Willem-Alexander of the Netherlands">Willem-Alexander of the Netherlands</a>. Constitutionally, the position is equipped with limited powers. By law, the King has the right to be periodically briefed and consulted on government affairs. Depending on the personalities and relationships of the King and the ministers, the monarch might have influence beyond the power granted by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Netherlands" title="Constitution of the Netherlands">Constitution of the Netherlands</a>.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:360px;max-width:360px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:174px;max-width:174px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Willem-Alexander_(Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm,_2010)_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1152" data-file-width="789" decoding="async" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg/172px-Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg/258px-Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg/344px-Willem-Alexander_%28Royal_Wedding_in_Stockholm%2C_2010%29_cropped.jpg 2x" width="172"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Willem-Alexander_of_the_Netherlands" title="Willem-Alexander of the Netherlands">Willem-Alexander</a><br/><small><a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Monarchy of the Netherlands">King of the Netherlands</a><br/>since 30 April 2013</small></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mark_Rutte-4.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="4724" data-file-width="3394" decoding="async" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mark_Rutte-4.jpg/180px-Mark_Rutte-4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mark_Rutte-4.jpg/270px-Mark_Rutte-4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mark_Rutte-4.jpg/360px-Mark_Rutte-4.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Mark_Rutte" title="Mark Rutte">Mark Rutte</a><br/><small><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Netherlands" title="Prime Minister of the Netherlands">Prime Minister of the Netherlands</a><br/>since 14 October 2010</small></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a> is formed by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_(Netherlands)" title="Council of Ministers (Netherlands)">Council of Ministers</a>, the deliberative organ of the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_Netherlands" title="Cabinet of the Netherlands">Dutch cabinet</a>. The cabinet usually consists of 13 to 16 ministers and a varying number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Secretary_(Netherlands)" title="State Secretary (Netherlands)">state secretaries</a>. One to three ministers are <a href="/wiki/Minister_without_portfolio" title="Minister without portfolio">ministers without portfolio</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Netherlands" title="Prime Minister of the Netherlands">Prime Minister of the Netherlands</a>, who often is the leader of the largest party of the coalition. The Prime Minister is a <i><a href="/wiki/Primus_inter_pares" title="Primus inter pares">primus inter pares</a></i>, with no explicit powers beyond those of the other ministers. <a href="/wiki/Mark_Rutte" title="Mark Rutte">Mark Rutte</a> has been Prime Minister since October 2010; the Prime Minister had been the leader of the largest party continuously since 1973.\n</p><p>The cabinet is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministerial_responsibility" title="Ministerial responsibility">responsible</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>, the <a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">States General</a>, which also has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative" title="Legislative">legislative powers</a>. The 150 members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_(Netherlands)" title="House of Representatives (Netherlands)">House of Representatives</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a>, are elected in <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">direct elections</a> on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Party-list_proportional_representation" title="Party-list proportional representation">party-list proportional representation</a>. These are held every four years, or sooner in case the cabinet falls (for example: when one of the chambers carries a <a href="/wiki/Motion_of_no_confidence" title="Motion of no confidence">motion of no confidence</a>, the cabinet offers its resignation to the monarch). The <a href="/wiki/States-Provincial" title="States-Provincial">States-Provincial</a> are directly elected every four years as well. The members of the provincial assemblies elect the 75 members of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_(Netherlands)" title="Senate (Netherlands)">Senate</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a>, which has the power to reject laws, but not propose or amend them. Both houses send members to the <a href="/wiki/Benelux_Parliament" title="Benelux Parliament">Benelux Parliament</a>, a consultative council.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2811" data-file-width="4280" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG/250px-Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG/375px-Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG/500px-Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/De_Wallen" title="De Wallen">De Wallen</a>, Amsterdam\'s <a href="/wiki/Red-light_district" title="Red-light district">Red-light district</a>, offers activities such as legal <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_the_Netherlands" title="Prostitution in the Netherlands">prostitution</a> and a number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coffee_shops" title="Coffee shops">coffee shops</a> that sell <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marijuana" title="Marijuana">marijuana</a>, symbolising the Dutch political culture and tradition of tolerance.</div></div></div>\n<p>Both trade unions and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Employers_organisation" title="Employers organisation">employers organisations</a> are consulted beforehand in policymaking in the financial, economic and social areas. They meet regularly with the government in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social-Economic_Council" title="Social-Economic Council">Social-Economic Council</a>. This body advises government and its advice cannot be put aside easily.\n</p><p>The Netherlands has a long tradition of <a href="/wiki/Toleration" title="Toleration">social tolerance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Singh2010_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Singh2010-106">[97]</a></sup> In the 18th century, while the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed Church</a> was the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_Netherlands" title="Roman Catholicism in the Netherlands">Catholicism</a>, other forms of Protestantism, such as Baptists and Lutherans, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Netherlands" title="History of the Jews in the Netherlands">Judaism</a> were tolerated but discriminated against.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Singh2010_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-Singh2010-106">[97]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the late 19th century this Dutch tradition of religious tolerance transformed into a system of <a href="/wiki/Pillarisation" title="Pillarisation">pillarisation</a>, in which religious groups coexisted separately and only interacted at the level of government. This tradition of tolerance influences Dutch <a href="/wiki/Criminal_justice_system_of_the_Netherlands" title="Criminal justice system of the Netherlands">criminal justice</a> policies on <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Drug policy of the Netherlands">recreational drugs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_the_Netherlands" title="Prostitution in the Netherlands">prostitution</a>, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_Netherlands" title="LGBT rights in the Netherlands">LGBT rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanasia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_the_Netherlands" title="Abortion in the Netherlands">abortion</a>, which are among the most liberal in the world.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_parties">Political parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Political parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_parties_of_the_Netherlands" title="Political parties of the Netherlands">Political parties of the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Netherlands" title="Politics of the Netherlands">Politics of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ineke_van_Gent,_Han_ten_Broeke_en_Kees_Verhoeven,_Lancering_Europese_Mobiliteitsweek_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Ineke_van_Gent%2C_Han_ten_Broeke_en_Kees_Verhoeven%2C_Lancering_Europese_Mobiliteitsweek_2010.jpg/220px-Ineke_van_Gent%2C_Han_ten_Broeke_en_Kees_Verhoeven%2C_Lancering_Europese_Mobiliteitsweek_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Ineke_van_Gent%2C_Han_ten_Broeke_en_Kees_Verhoeven%2C_Lancering_Europese_Mobiliteitsweek_2010.jpg/330px-Ineke_van_Gent%2C_Han_ten_Broeke_en_Kees_Verhoeven%2C_Lancering_Europese_Mobiliteitsweek_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Ineke_van_Gent%2C_Han_ten_Broeke_en_Kees_Verhoeven%2C_Lancering_Europese_Mobiliteitsweek_2010.jpg/440px-Ineke_van_Gent%2C_Han_ten_Broeke_en_Kees_Verhoeven%2C_Lancering_Europese_Mobiliteitsweek_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ineke_van_Gent,_Han_ten_Broeke_en_Kees_Verhoeven,_Lancering_Europese_Mobiliteitsweek_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Netherlands has a culture of respectful and friendly debate; here (from left to right) are members of the House of Representatives <a href="/wiki/Sander_de_Rouwe" title="Sander de Rouwe">Sander de Rouwe</a> (CDA), <a href="/wiki/Ineke_van_Gent" title="Ineke van Gent">Ineke van Gent</a> (GL), <a href="/wiki/Han_ten_Broeke" title="Han ten Broeke">Han ten Broeke</a> (VVD), <a href="/wiki/Kees_Verhoeven" title="Kees Verhoeven">Kees Verhoeven</a> (D66) and <a href="/wiki/Farshad_Bashir" title="Farshad Bashir">Farshad Bashir</a> (SP), 2010.</div></div></div>\n<p>Because of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_parties_of_the_Netherlands" title="Political parties of the Netherlands">multi-party system</a>, no single party has held a majority in parliament since the 19th century, and <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition cabinets</a> had to be formed. Since suffrage became universal <a href="/wiki/Pacification_of_1917" title="Pacification of 1917">in 1917</a>, the Dutch political system has been dominated by three families of political parties: the strongest of which were the <a href="/wiki/Christian_democracy" title="Christian democracy">Christian Democrats</a>, currently represented by the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Appeal" title="Christian Democratic Appeal">Christian Democratic Appeal</a> (CDA); second were the <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">Social Democrats</a>, represented by the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Netherlands)" title="Labour Party (Netherlands)">Labour Party</a> (PvdA); and third were the <a href="/wiki/Liberalism_in_the_Netherlands" title="Liberalism in the Netherlands">Liberals</a>, of which the right-wing <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_for_Freedom_and_Democracy" title="People\'s Party for Freedom and Democracy">People\'s Party for Freedom and Democracy</a> (VVD) is the main representative.\n</p><p>These parties co-operated in coalition cabinets in which the Christian Democrats had always been a partner: so either a centre-left coalition of the Christian Democrats and Social Democrats was ruling or a centre-right coalition of Christian Democrats and Liberals. In the 1970s, the <a href="/wiki/Party_system" title="Party system">party system</a> became more volatile: the Christian Democratic parties lost seats, while new parties became successful, such as the <a href="/wiki/Radicalism_(historical)" title="Radicalism (historical)">radical democrat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">progressive</a> liberal <a href="/wiki/Democrats_66" title="Democrats 66">Democrats 66</a> (D66) or the <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecologist</a> party <a href="/wiki/GroenLinks" title="GroenLinks">GroenLinks</a> (GL).\n</p><p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_1994" title="Dutch general election, 1994">1994 election</a>, the CDA lost its dominant position. A "<a href="/wiki/Purple_(government)" title="Purple (government)">purple</a>" cabinet was formed by the VVD, D66, and PvdA. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_2002" title="Dutch general election, 2002">2002 elections</a>, this cabinet lost its majority, because of an increased support for the CDA and the rise of the right <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lijst_Pim_Fortuyn" title="Lijst Pim Fortuyn">LPF</a>, a new political party, around <a href="/wiki/Pim_Fortuyn" title="Pim Fortuyn">Pim Fortuyn</a>, who was assassinated a week before the elections. A short-lived <a href="/wiki/First_Balkenende_cabinet" title="First Balkenende cabinet">cabinet</a> was formed by CDA, VVD, and LPF, which was led by the CDA Leader <a href="/wiki/Jan_Peter_Balkenende" title="Jan Peter Balkenende">Jan Peter Balkenende</a>. After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_2003" title="Dutch general election, 2003">2003 elections</a>, in which the LPF lost most of its seats, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balkenende_II" title="Balkenende II">cabinet</a> was formed by the CDA, VVD, and D66. The cabinet initiated an ambitious programme of reforming the <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_the_Netherlands" title="Healthcare in the Netherlands">healthcare system</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Border_control#Immigration_policy" title="Border control">immigration policy</a>.\n</p><p>In June 2006, the cabinet fell after D66 voted in favour of a motion of no confidence against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Justice_and_Security_(Netherlands)" title="Ministry of Justice and Security (Netherlands)">Minister of Immigration and Integration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rita_Verdonk" title="Rita Verdonk">Rita Verdonk</a>, who had instigated an investigation of the asylum procedure of <a href="/wiki/Ayaan_Hirsi_Ali" title="Ayaan Hirsi Ali">Ayaan Hirsi Ali</a>, a VVD <a href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament" title="Member of parliament">MP</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Third_Balkenende_cabinet" title="Third Balkenende cabinet">caretaker cabinet</a> was formed by the CDA and VVD, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_2006" title="Dutch general election, 2006">general elections</a> were held on 22 November 2006. In these elections, the CDA remained the largest party and the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(Netherlands)" title="Socialist Party (Netherlands)">Socialist Party</a> made the largest gains. The <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Dutch_cabinet_formation" title="2006&#8211;07 Dutch cabinet formation">formation of a new cabinet</a> took three months, resulting in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Netherlands_cabinet_Balkenende-4" title="Netherlands cabinet Balkenende-4">coalition</a> of CDA, PvdA, and <a href="/wiki/Christian_Union_(Netherlands)" title="Christian Union (Netherlands)">Christian Union</a>.\n</p><p>On 20 February 2010, the cabinet fell when the PvdA refused to prolong the involvement of the Dutch Army in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uruzgan" title="Uruzgan">Uruzgan</a>, Afghanistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[98]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Snap_election" title="Snap election">Snap elections</a> were held on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_2010" title="Dutch general election, 2010">9 June 2010</a>, with devastating results for the previously largest party, the CDA, which lost about half of its seats, resulting in 21 seats. The VVD became the largest party with 31 seats, closely followed by the PvdA with 30 seats. The big winner of the 2010 elections was <a href="/wiki/Geert_Wilders" title="Geert Wilders">Geert Wilders</a>, whose right wing <a href="/wiki/Party_for_Freedom" title="Party for Freedom">PVV</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[100]</a></sup> the ideological successor to the <a href="/wiki/Pim_Fortuyn_List" title="Pim Fortuyn List">LPF</a>, more than doubled its number of seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[101]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2010_Dutch_cabinet_formation" title="2010 Dutch cabinet formation">Negotiation talks for a new government</a> resulted in a <a href="/wiki/Minority_government" title="Minority government">minority government</a>, led by VVD (a first) in coalition with CDA, which was sworn in on 14 October 2010. This unprecedented minority government was supported by PVV, but proved ultimately to be unstable,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[102]</a></sup> when on 21 April 2012, Wilders, leader of PVV, unexpectedly \'torpedoed seven weeks of austerity talks\' on new austerity measures, paving the way for early elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[105]</a></sup>\n</p><p>VVD and PvdA won a majority in the House of Representatives during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_2012" title="Dutch general election, 2012">2012 general election</a>. On 5 November 2012 they formed the <a href="/wiki/Second_Rutte_cabinet" title="Second Rutte cabinet">second Rutte cabinet</a>.\n</p><p>After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_general_election,_2017" title="Dutch general election, 2017">2017 general election</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VVD" title="VVD">VVD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Appeal" title="Christian Democratic Appeal">Christian Democratic Appeal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democrats_66" title="Democrats 66">Democrats 66</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ChristenUnie" title="ChristenUnie">ChristenUnie</a> formed the <a href="/wiki/Third_Rutte_cabinet" title="Third Rutte cabinet">third Rutte cabinet</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Netherlands" title="Government of the Netherlands">Government of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Netherlands" title="Provinces of the Netherlands">Provinces of the Netherlands</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_the_Netherlands" title="Municipalities of the Netherlands">Municipalities of the Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_board_(Netherlands)" title="Water board (Netherlands)">Water board (Netherlands)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Public_body_(Netherlands)" title="Public body (Netherlands)">Public body (Netherlands)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="881" data-file-width="743" decoding="async" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg/200px-Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg/300px-Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg/400px-Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_provinces_Netherlands-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Netherlands" title="Provinces of the Netherlands">Provinces</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_municipality_(Netherlands)" title="Special municipality (Netherlands)">special municipalities</a> of the Netherlands.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Netherlands is divided into twelve provinces, each under a <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Commissioner" title="King\'s Commissioner">King\'s Commissioner</a> (<i>Commissaris van de Koning</i>), except for <a href="/wiki/Limburg_(Netherlands)" title="Limburg (Netherlands)">Limburg province</a> where the position is named Governor (<i>Gouverneur</i>) but has the same tasks. All provinces are divided into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_the_Netherlands" title="Municipalities of the Netherlands">municipalities</a> (<i>gemeenten</i>), of which there are 380 (2018).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MUNICPS_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-MUNICPS-115">[106]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The country is also subdivided into 24 water districts, governed by a <a href="/wiki/Water_board_(Netherlands)" title="Water board (Netherlands)">water board</a> (<i>waterschap</i> or <i>hoogheemraadschap</i>), each having authority in matters concerning water management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WATER_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-WATER-116">[107]</a></sup> The creation of water boards actually pre-dates that of the nation itself, the first appearing in 1196. The Dutch water boards are among the oldest democratic entities in the world still in existence. Direct elections of the water boards take place every 4 years.\n</p><p>The administrative structure on the 3 BES islands, collectively known as the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a>, is different. These islands have the status of <i>openbare lichamen (<a href="/wiki/Public_body_(Netherlands)" title="Public body (Netherlands)">public bodies</a>)</i> rather than municipalities and as administrative units are generally referred to as <i>special municipalities</i>. They are not part of a province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOLBES_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-WOLBES-117">[108]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Netherlands has several Belgian <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">exclaves</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[109]</a></sup> and within those even several enclaves which are still part of the province of <a href="/wiki/North_Brabant" title="North Brabant">North Brabant</a>. Because the Netherlands and Belgium are both in the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, citizens of respective countries can travel through these enclaves.\n</p>\n<table cellspacing="2" style="background:none;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>\n<table class="sortable wikitable" style="text-align:left;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th class="unsortable"
