class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Netherlands" title="Foreign relations of the Netherlands">Foreign relations of the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_the_Netherlands" title="List of diplomatic missions of the Netherlands">List of diplomatic missions of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:International_Court_of_Justice.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="597" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/International_Court_of_Justice.jpg/220px-International_Court_of_Justice.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/International_Court_of_Justice.jpg/330px-International_Court_of_Justice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/International_Court_of_Justice.jpg/440px-International_Court_of_Justice.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:International_Court_of_Justice.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Peace_Palace" title="Peace Palace">Peace Palace</a> (<i>Vredespaleis</i>), in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The history of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Netherlands" title="Foreign relations of the Netherlands">Dutch foreign policy</a> has been characterised by its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutral_state" title="Neutral state">neutrality</a>. Since World War II, the Netherlands has become a member of a large number of international organisations, most prominently the UN, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and the EU. The Dutch economy is very open and relies strongly on <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">international trade</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a> of the Netherlands is based on four basic commitments: to <a href="/wiki/Atlanticism" title="Atlanticism">Atlantic co-operation</a>, to <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>, to <a href="/wiki/International_development" title="International development">international development</a> and to <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>. One of the more controversial international issues surrounding the Netherlands is its <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Drug policy of the Netherlands">liberal policy towards soft drugs</a>.\n</p><p>During and after the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a>, the Dutch people built up a commercial and colonial empire. The most important colonies were present-day <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. Indonesia became independent after the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">Indonesian National Revolution</a> in the 1940s following a war of independence, international pressure and several <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_resolution" title="United Nations Security Council resolution">United Nations Security Council resolutions</a>. Suriname became independent in 1975. The historical ties inherited from its colonial past still influence the foreign relations of the Netherlands. In addition, many people from these countries are living permanently in the Netherlands.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces_of_the_Netherlands" title="Armed forces of the Netherlands">Armed forces of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rob_Bauer.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2214" data-file-width="3321" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Rob_Bauer.jpg/220px-Rob_Bauer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Rob_Bauer.jpg/330px-Rob_Bauer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Rob_Bauer.jpg/440px-Rob_Bauer.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rob_Bauer.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lieutenant admiral <a href="/wiki/Rob_Bauer" title="Rob Bauer">Rob Bauer</a> is the current <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Defence_(Netherlands)" title="Chief of Defence (Netherlands)">Chief of Defence</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Netherlands has one of the oldest standing armies in Europe; it was first established as such by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maurice_of_Nassau" title="Maurice of Nassau">Maurice of Nassau</a> in the late 1500s. The Dutch army was used throughout the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a>. After the defeat of Napoleon, the Dutch army was transformed into a <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> army. The army was unsuccessfully deployed during the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Revolution" title="Belgian Revolution">Belgian Revolution</a> in 1830. After 1830, it was deployed mainly in the Dutch colonies, as the Netherlands remained neutral in European wars (including the First World War), until the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Netherlands" title="Battle of the Netherlands">Netherlands was invaded in World War II</a> and defeated by the Wehrmacht in May 1940.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HNLMS_Holland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/HNLMS_Holland.jpg/220px-HNLMS_Holland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/HNLMS_Holland.jpg/330px-HNLMS_Holland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/HNLMS_Holland.jpg/440px-HNLMS_Holland.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HNLMS_Holland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Zr. Ms. Holland</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Navy" title="Royal Netherlands Navy">Royal Netherlands Navy</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Offshore_patrol_vessel" title="Offshore patrol vessel">offshore patrol vessel</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Netherlands abandoned its neutrality in 1948 when it signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brussels" title="Treaty of Brussels">Treaty of Brussels</a>, and became a founding member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in 1949. The Dutch military was therefore part of the NATO strength in <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> Europe, deploying its army to several bases in Germany. More than 3,000 Dutch soldiers were assigned to the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" title="2nd Infantry Division (United States)">2nd Infantry Division</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>. In 1996 conscription was suspended, and the Dutch army was once again transformed into a professional army. Since the 1990s the Dutch army has been involved in the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>, it held a province in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> after the defeat of <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a>, and it was engaged in <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001&#8211;present)">Afghanistan</a>.\n</p><p>The military is composed of four branches, all of which carry the prefix <i>Koninklijke</i> (Royal):\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Koninklijke Landmacht</i> (KL), the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Army" title="Royal Netherlands Army">Royal Netherlands Army</a>;</li>\n<li><i>Koninklijke Marine</i> (KM), the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Navy" title="Royal Netherlands Navy">Royal Netherlands Navy</a>, including the Naval Air Service and Marine Corps;</li>\n<li><i>Koninklijke Luchtmacht</i> (KLu), the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Air_Force" title="Royal Netherlands Air Force">Royal Netherlands Air Force</a>;</li>\n<li><i>Koninklijke Marechaussee</i> (KMar), the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marechaussee" title="Royal Marechaussee">Royal Marechaussee</a> (Military Police), tasks include military police and border control.</li></ul>\n<p>The submarine service is open to women as of 1 January 2017. The <a href="/wiki/Korps_Commandotroepen" title="Korps Commandotroepen">Korps Commandotroepen</a>, the Special Operations Force of the Netherlands Army, is open to women, but because of the extremely high physical demands for initial training, it is almost impossible for a woman to become a commando.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[114]</a></sup> The Dutch Ministry of Defence employs more than 70,000 personnel, including over 20,000 civilians and over 50,000 military personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[115]</a></sup> In April 2011 the government announced a major reduction in its military because of a cut in government expenditure, including a decrease in the number of tanks, fighter aircraft, naval ships and senior officials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[116]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Economy of the Netherlands">Economy of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Smile_29Aug07_5,_at_the_Amazone_harbour,_Port_of_Rotterdam,_Holland_29-Aug-2007.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2616" data-file-width="3488" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Smile_29Aug07_5%2C_at_the_Amazone_harbour%2C_Port_of_Rotterdam%2C_Holland_29-Aug-2007.jpg/220px-Smile_29Aug07_5%2C_at_the_Amazone_harbour%2C_Port_of_Rotterdam%2C_Holland_29-Aug-2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Smile_29Aug07_5%2C_at_the_Amazone_harbour%2C_Port_of_Rotterdam%2C_Holland_29-Aug-2007.jpg/330px-Smile_29Aug07_5%2C_at_the_Amazone_harbour%2C_Port_of_Rotterdam%2C_Holland_29-Aug-2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Smile_29Aug07_5%2C_at_the_Amazone_harbour%2C_Port_of_Rotterdam%2C_Holland_29-Aug-2007.jpg/440px-Smile_29Aug07_5%2C_at_the_Amazone_harbour%2C_Port_of_Rotterdam%2C_Holland_29-Aug-2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Smile_29Aug07_5,_at_the_Amazone_harbour,_Port_of_Rotterdam,_Holland_29-Aug-2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rotterdam" title="Port of Rotterdam">Port of Rotterdam</a> is Europe\'s largest port.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Netherlands has a developed economy and has been playing a special role in the European economy for many centuries. Since the 16th century, shipping, fishing, agriculture, trade, and banking have been leading sectors of the Dutch economy. The Netherlands has <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_economic_freedom" title="List of countries by economic freedom">a high level of economic freedom</a>. The Netherlands is one of the top countries in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Enabling_Trade_Report" title="Global Enabling Trade Report">Global Enabling Trade Report</a> (2nd in 2016), and was ranked the fifth most competitive economy in the world by the Swiss <a href="/wiki/International_Institute_for_Management_Development" title="International Institute for Management Development">International Institute for Management Development</a> in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[117]</a></sup> In addition, the country was ranked the second most innovative in the world in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index" title="Global Innovation Index">Global Innovation Index</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[118]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the key trading partners of the Netherlands were Germany, Belgium, the United Kingdom, the United States, France, Italy, China and Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[119]</a></sup> The Netherlands is one of the world\'s 10 leading exporting countries. Foodstuffs form the largest industrial sector. Other major industries include chemicals, metallurgy, machinery, electrical goods, trade, services and tourism. Examples of international Dutch companies operating in Netherlands include <a href="/wiki/Randstad_Holding" title="Randstad Holding">Randstad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">Unilever</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heineken_International" title="Heineken International">Heineken</a>, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a>, financial services (<a href="/wiki/ING_Group" title="ING Group">ING</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABN_AMRO" title="ABN AMRO">ABN AMRO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabobank" title="Rabobank">Rabobank</a>), chemicals (<a href="/wiki/DSM_(company)" title="DSM (company)">DSM</a>, <a href="/wiki/AkzoNobel" title="AkzoNobel">AKZO</a>), petroleum refining (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a>), electronical machinery (<a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a>, <a href="/wiki/ASML_Holding" title="ASML Holding">ASML</a>), and satellite navigation (<a href="/wiki/TomTom" title="TomTom">TomTom</a>).\n</p><p>The Netherlands has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">17th-largest economy in the world</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">ranks 10th in GDP (nominal) per capita</a>. Between 1997 and 2000 annual economic growth (GDP) averaged nearly 4%, well above the European average. Growth slowed considerably from 2001 to 2005 with the global economic slowdown, but accelerated to 4.1% in the third quarter of 2007. In May 2013, inflation was at 2.8% per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[120]</a></sup> In April 2013, unemployment was at 8.2% (or 6.7% following the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">ILO</a> definition) of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labour_force" title="Labour force">labour force</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[121]</a></sup> In October 2018, this was reduced to 3.7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[122]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Q3 and Q4 2011, the Dutch economy contracted by 0.4% and 0.7%, respectively, because of European Debt Crisis, while in Q4 the Eurozone economy shrunk by 0.3%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[123]</a></sup> The Netherlands also has a relatively low <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">GINI coefficient</a> of 0.326. Despite ranking 7th in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> ranked the Netherlands 1st in child well-being in rich countries, both in 2007 and in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[126]</a></sup> On the <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a> Netherlands is the 13th most <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a> capitalist economy out of 157 surveyed countries.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> is the financial and business capital of the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ez_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-ez-136">[127]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a> (AEX), part of <a href="/wiki/Euronext" title="Euronext">Euronext</a>, is the world\'s oldest stock exchange and is one of Europe\'s largest bourses. It is situated near <a href="/wiki/Dam_Square" title="Dam Square">Dam Square</a> in the city\'s centre. As a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>, the Netherlands replaced (for accounting purposes) its former currency, the "gulden" (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_guilder" title="Dutch guilder">guilder</a>), on 1 January 1999, along with 15 other adopters of the euro. Actual <a href="/wiki/Euro_coins" title="Euro coins">euro coins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euro_banknotes" title="Euro banknotes">banknotes</a> followed on 1 January 2002. One euro was equivalent to 2.20371 Dutch guilders. In the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a> is used instead of the euro.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="645" decoding="async" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/220px-BlueEurozone.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/330px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/440px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Netherlands is part of a monetary union, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> (dark blue), and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_Market_(European_Union)" title="Internal Market (European Union)">EU single market</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Dutch location gives it prime access to markets in the UK and Germany, with the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rotterdam" title="Port of Rotterdam">Port of Rotterdam</a> being the largest port in Europe. Other important parts of the economy are <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">international trade</a> (Dutch colonialism started with co-operative private enterprises such as the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a>), banking and transport. The Netherlands successfully addressed the issue of public finances and stagnating job growth long before its European partners. Amsterdam is the 5th-busiest tourist destination in Europe with more than 4.2&#160;million international visitors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42milvisitors_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-42milvisitors-137">[128]</a></sup> Since the enlargement of the EU large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Migrant_worker" title="Migrant worker">migrant workers</a> have arrived in the Netherlands from <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[129]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also of economic importance is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BrabantStad" title="BrabantStad">BrabantStad</a>, a partnership between the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Breda" title="Breda">Breda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven" title="Eindhoven">Eindhoven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helmond" title="Helmond">Helmond</a>, <a href="/wiki/%27s-Hertogenbosch" title="\'s-Hertogenbosch">\'s-Hertogenbosch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tilburg" title="Tilburg">Tilburg</a> and the province of <a href="/wiki/North_Brabant" title="North Brabant">North Brabant</a>. BrabantStad is the fastest growing economic region in the Netherlands, with the <a href="/wiki/Brabantse_Stedenrij" title="Brabantse Stedenrij">Brabantse Stedenrij</a> (polycentric city region) as one of the national top regions, behind the <a href="/wiki/Randstad" title="Randstad">Randstad</a> <a href="/wiki/Megalopolis" title="Megalopolis">megalopolis</a> (<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> and <a href="/wiki/Utrecht" title="Utrecht">Utrecht</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref608454752_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-ref608454752-139">[130]</a></sup> The partnership in North Brabant aims to form an urban network and to make the province explicitly known as a leading knowledge region within Europe. With a total of 1.5&#160;million people and 20% of the industrial production in the Netherlands is BrabantStad one of the major economical important, metropolitan regions of the Netherlands. Of all the money that goes to research and development in the Netherlands, one third is spent in Eindhoven. A quarter of the jobs in the region are in technology and ICT.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref-213874478_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-ref-213874478-140">[131]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Of all European patent applications in the field of physics and electronics about eight per cent is from North Brabant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref-601915138_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-ref-601915138-141">[132]</a></sup> In the extended region, BrabantStad is part of the Eindhoven-Leuven-Aachen Triangle (ELAT). This economic cooperation agreement between three cities in three countries has created one of the most innovative regions in the European Union (measured in terms of money invested in <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_economy" title="Knowledge economy">knowledge economy</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref1983490620_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-ref1983490620-142">[133]</a></sup> The economic success of this region is important for the international competitiveness of the Netherlands; Amsterdam, Rotterdam, and Eindhoven form together the foundation of the Dutch economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref1367203750_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-ref1367203750-143">[134]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Netherlands continues to be one of the leading European nations for attracting foreign direct investment and is one of the five largest investors in the United States. The economy experienced a slowdown in 2005, but in 2006 recovered to the fastest pace in six years on the back of increased exports and strong investment. The pace of job growth reached 10-year highs in 2007. The Netherlands is the fourth-most competitive economy in the world, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wefcomp_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-wefcomp-144">[135]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_gas">Natural gas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Natural gas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Natural_gas_NL.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1032" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Natural_gas_NL.png/220px-Natural_gas_NL.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Natural_gas_NL.png/330px-Natural_gas_NL.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Natural_gas_NL.png/440px-Natural_gas_NL.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Natural_gas_NL.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Natural gas concessions in the Netherlands. Today the Netherlands accounts for more than 25% of all natural gas reserves in the EU.</div></div></div>\n<p>Beginning in the 1950s, the Netherlands discovered huge natural gas resources. The sale of natural gas generated enormous revenues for the Netherlands for decades, adding hundreds of billions of euros to the government\'s budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vorige.nrc.nl_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-vorige.nrc.nl-145">[136]</a></sup> However, the unforeseen consequences of the country\'s huge energy wealth impacted the competitiveness of other sectors of the economy, leading to the theory of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_disease" title="Dutch disease">Dutch disease</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vorige.nrc.nl_145-1"><a href="#cite_note-vorige.nrc.nl-145">[136]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Apart from coal and gas, the country has no mining resources. The last coal mine was closed in 1974. The <a href="/wiki/Groningen_gas_field" title="Groningen gas field">Groningen gas field</a>, one of the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_gas_field" title="Natural gas field">natural gas fields</a> in the world, is situated near <a href="/wiki/Slochteren" title="Slochteren">Slochteren</a>. Exploitation of this field has resulted in &#8364;159&#160;billion in revenue since the mid-1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geo_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-geo-146">[137]</a></sup> The field is operated by government-owned Gasunie and output is jointly exploited by the government, Royal Dutch Shell, and Exxon Mobil through NAM (Nederlandse Aardolie Maatschappij). "Gas extraction has resulted in increasingly strong earth tremors, some measuring as much as 3.6 on the Richter magnitude scale. The cost of damage repairs, structural improvements to buildings, and compensation for home value decreases has been estimated at 6.5 billion euros. Around 35,000 homes are said to be affected."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[138]</a></sup> The Netherlands have an estimated 25% of natural gas reserves in the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[139]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dutch_belted_cows_at_Park_Sonsbeek_meadows_in_the_centre_of_the_city_of_Arnhem_(look_the_background)_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Dutch_belted_cows_at_Park_Sonsbeek_meadows_in_the_centre_of_the_city_of_Arnhem_%28look_the_background%29_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Dutch_belted_cows_at_Park_Sonsbeek_meadows_in_the_centre_of_the_city_of_Arnhem_%28look_the_background%29_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Dutch_belted_cows_at_Park_Sonsbeek_meadows_in_the_centre_of_the_city_of_Arnhem_%28look_the_background%29_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Dutch_belted_cows_at_Park_Sonsbeek_meadows_in_the_centre_of_the_city_of_Arnhem_%28look_the_background%29_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Dutch_belted_cows_at_Park_Sonsbeek_meadows_in_the_centre_of_the_city_of_Arnhem_%28look_the_background%29_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Dutch_belted_cows_at_Park_Sonsbeek_meadows_in_the_centre_of_the_city_of_Arnhem_%28look_the_background%29_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dutch_belted_cows_at_Park_Sonsbeek_meadows_in_the_centre_of_the_city_of_Arnhem_(look_the_background)_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cows near the city of <a href="/wiki/Arnhem" title="Arnhem">Arnhem</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Dutch agricultural sector is highly mechanised, and has a strong focus on international exports. It employs about 4% of the Dutch labour force but produces large surpluses for the food-processing industry and accounts for 21 percent of the Dutch total export value.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[140]</a></sup> The Dutch rank first in the European Union and second worldwide in value of agricultural exports, behind only the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[141]</a></sup> with agricultural exports earning &#8364;80.7&#160;billion in 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-government.nl_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-government.nl-151">[142]</a></sup> up from &#8364;75.4&#160;billion in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hollandtrade.com_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-hollandtrade.com-27">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Netherlands has, at some time in recent history, supplied one quarter of all of the world\'s exported tomatoes, and trade of one-third of the world\'s exports of <a href="/wiki/Capsicum" title="Capsicum">chilis</a>, tomatoes and cucumbers goes through the country. The Netherlands also exports one-fifteenth of the world\'s apples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDA_Foreign_Agriculture_Service_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-USDA_Foreign_Agriculture_Service-152">[143]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Aside from that, a significant portion of Dutch agricultural exports consists of fresh-cut plants, flowers, and flower bulbs, with the Netherlands exporting two-thirds of the world\'s total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDA_Foreign_Agriculture_Service_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-USDA_Foreign_Agriculture_Service-152">[143]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Netherlands" title="Transport in the Netherlands">Transport in the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A1-Hoog_Buurlo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/A1-Hoog_Buurlo.jpg/220px-A1-Hoog_Buurlo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/A1-Hoog_Buurlo.jpg/330px-A1-Hoog_Buurlo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/A1-Hoog_Buurlo.jpg/440px-A1-Hoog_Buurlo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A1-Hoog_Buurlo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/A1_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A1 motorway (Netherlands)">A1 motorway</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Gelderland" title="Gelderland">Gelderland</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bike_entrance_Rotterdam_Central_Station.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3064" data-file-width="4555" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Bike_entrance_Rotterdam_Central_Station.jpg/220px-Bike_entrance_Rotterdam_Central_Station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Bike_entrance_Rotterdam_Central_Station.jpg/330px-Bike_entrance_Rotterdam_Central_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Bike_entrance_Rotterdam_Central_Station.jpg/440px-Bike_entrance_Rotterdam_Central_Station.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bike_entrance_Rotterdam_Central_Station.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bike passage at <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam_Centraal_station" title="Rotterdam Centraal station">Rotterdam Centraal station</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Mobility on Dutch roads has grown continuously since the 1950s and now exceeds 200 billion km travelled per year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[144]</a></sup> three quarters of which are done by car.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECD-ITF_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-ITF-154">[145]</a></sup> Around half of all trips in the Netherlands are made by car, 25% by bicycle, 20% walking, and 5% by public transport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECD-ITF_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-ITF-154">[145]</a></sup> With a total <a href="/wiki/Roads_in_the_Netherlands" title="Roads in the Netherlands">road network</a> of 139,295&#160;km, which includes 2,758&#160;km of expressways,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[146]</a></sup> the Netherlands has one of the densest road networks in the world&#8212;much denser than Germany and France, but still not as dense as Belgium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[147]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NSR_-_Sprinter_Lighttrain_(SLT)_-_Wieldrechtse_Zeedijk_-_Dordrecht_(22087244596).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/NSR_-_Sprinter_Lighttrain_%28SLT%29_-_Wieldrechtse_Zeedijk_-_Dordrecht_%2822087244596%29.jpg/220px-NSR_-_Sprinter_Lighttrain_%28SLT%29_-_Wieldrechtse_Zeedijk_-_Dordrecht_%2822087244596%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/NSR_-_Sprinter_Lighttrain_%28SLT%29_-_Wieldrechtse_Zeedijk_-_Dordrecht_%2822087244596%29.jpg/330px-NSR_-_Sprinter_Lighttrain_%28SLT%29_-_Wieldrechtse_Zeedijk_-_Dordrecht_%2822087244596%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/NSR_-_Sprinter_Lighttrain_%28SLT%29_-_Wieldrechtse_Zeedijk_-_Dordrecht_%2822087244596%29.jpg/440px-NSR_-_Sprinter_Lighttrain_%28SLT%29_-_Wieldrechtse_Zeedijk_-_Dordrecht_%2822087244596%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NSR_-_Sprinter_Lighttrain_(SLT)_-_Wieldrechtse_Zeedijk_-_Dordrecht_(22087244596).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A regional train operated by <a href="/wiki/Nederlandse_Spoorwegen" title="Nederlandse Spoorwegen">Nederlandse Spoorwegen</a> (NS)</div></div></div>\n<p>About 13% of all distance is travelled by public transport, the majority of which by train.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECD-ITF_154-2"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-ITF-154">[145]</a></sup> Like in <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_rail_transport_network_size" title="List of countries by rail transport network size">many other European countries</a>, the Dutch rail network of 3,013 route&#160;km is also rather dense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[148]</a></sup> The network is mostly focused on passenger rail services and connects all major towns and cities, with over 400 stations. Trains are frequent, with two trains per hour on lesser lines,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[j]</a></sup> two to four trains per hour on average, and up to eight trains an hour on the busiest lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[149]</a></sup> The Dutch national train network, which is free of charge for students, also includes the <a href="/wiki/HSL-Zuid" title="HSL-Zuid">HSL-Zuid</a>, a high-speed line between the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_metropolitan_area" title="Amsterdam metropolitan area">Amsterdam metropolitan area</a> and the Belgian border for trains running from Paris and London to the Netherlands.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cycling_in_the_Netherlands" title="Cycling in the Netherlands">Cycling</a> is a ubiquitous mode of transport in the Netherlands. Almost as many kilometres are covered by bicycle as by train.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECD-ITF_154-3"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-ITF-154">[145]</a></sup> The Dutch are estimated to have at least 18 million bicycles,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[151]</a></sup> which makes more than one per capita, and twice as many as the circa 9 million motor vehicles on the road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[152]</a></sup> In 2013, the <a href="/wiki/European_Cyclists%27_Federation" title="European Cyclists\' Federation">European Cyclists\' Federation</a> ranked both the Netherlands and <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> as the most bike-friendly countries in Europe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[153]</a></sup> but more of the Dutch (36%) than of the Danes (23%) list the bike as their most frequent mode of transport on a typical day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[k]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cycling_infrastructure" title="Cycling infrastructure">Cycling infrastructure</a> is comprehensive. Busy roads have received some 35,000&#160;km of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Segregated_cycle_facilities" title="Segregated cycle facilities">dedicated cycle tracks</a>, physically segregated from motorised traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[157]</a></sup> Busy junctions are often equipped with bicycle-specific traffic lights. There are large bicycle parking facilities, particularly in city centres and at train stations.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rotterdam" title="Port of Rotterdam">Port of Rotterdam</a> is the largest port in Europe, with the rivers Meuse and Rhine providing excellent access to the <a href="/wiki/Hinterland" title="Hinterland">hinterland</a> upstream reaching to <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a>, Switzerland, and into Germany and France. As of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Rotterdam was the world\'s eighth largest <a href="/wiki/Container_port" title="Container port">container port</a> handling 440.5 million metric tonnes of cargo annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[158]</a></sup> The port\'s main activities are <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">petrochemical</a> industries and general cargo handling and <a href="/wiki/Transshipment" title="Transshipment">transshipment</a>. The harbour functions as an important transit point for <a href="/wiki/Bulk_material_handling" title="Bulk material handling">bulk materials</a> and between the European continent and overseas. From Rotterdam goods are transported by ship, river barge, train or road. In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Betuweroute" title="Betuweroute">Betuweroute</a>, a new fast freight railway from Rotterdam to Germany, was completed.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Schiphol Airport</a>, just southwest of Amsterdam, is the main <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in the Netherlands, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">third busiest airport in Europe</a> in terms of passengers. In 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Group" title="Schiphol Group">Royal Schiphol Group</a> airports handled 70 million passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOS_Schiphol64_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOS_Schiphol64-170">[159]</a></sup> As part of its commitment to environmental sustainability, the Government of the Netherlands initiated a plan to establish over 200 recharging stations for electric vehicles across the country. The rollout will be undertaken by Switzerland-based power and automation company <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABB_(company)" title="ABB (company)">ABB</a> and Dutch startup Fastned, and will aim to provide at least one station within a 50-kilometre radius (30 miles) from every home in the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[160]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Netherlands" title="Demographics of the Netherlands">Demographics of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="313" data-file-width="416" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2c/Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png/220px-Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2c/Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png/330px-Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/2c/Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Population_of_the_Netherlands_1900-2000.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The population of the Netherlands from 1900 to 2000</div></div></div>\n<p>The Netherlands had an estimated population of 17,093,000 as of January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbs-counter_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbs-counter-172">[161]</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/Area_and_population_of_European_countries" title="Area and population of European countries">most densely populated country in Europe</a>, except for very small states like <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>. It is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" title="List of countries by population">63rd most populous country</a> in the world. Between 1900 and 1950, the country\'s population almost doubled from 5.1 to 10 million. From 1950 to 2000, the population further increased, to 15.9&#160;million, though this represented a lower rate of <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[162]</a></sup> The estimated growth rate in 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> is 0.44%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-worldfactbook-nl_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-cia-worldfactbook-nl-174">[163]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> in the Netherlands is 1.78 children per woman (2013 estimate),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-worldfactbook-nl_174-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia-worldfactbook-nl-174">[163]</a></sup> which is high compared with many other European countries, but <a href="/wiki/Sub-replacement_fertility" title="Sub-replacement fertility">below the rate of 2.1 children per woman required for natural population replacement</a>. <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> is high in the Netherlands: 83.2 years for newborn girls and 78.9 for boys (2013 estimate).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-worldfactbook-nl_174-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia-worldfactbook-nl-174">[163]</a></sup> The country has a <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migration</a> rate of 2.0 migrants per 1,000 inhabitants per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-worldfactbook-nl_174-3"><a href="#cite_note-cia-worldfactbook-nl-174">[163]</a></sup> The majority of the population of the Netherlands is ethnically <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>. According to a 2005 estimate, the population was 80.9% Dutch, 2.4% <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a>, 2.4% <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a>, 2.2% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkish-Dutch" title="Turkish-Dutch">Turkish</a>, 2.0% <a href="/wiki/Surinamese_people" title="Surinamese people">Surinamese</a>, 1.9% <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Moroccan</a>, 0.8% <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Antillean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruban</a>, and 7.4% others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[164]</a></sup> Some 150,000 to 200,000 people living in the Netherlands are <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriates</a>, mostly concentrated in and around <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, now constituting almost 10% of the population of these cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[166]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Dutch are the tallest people in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Science_2015-04-07_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Science_2015-04-07-178">[167]</a></sup> with an average height of 1.81 metres (5&#160;ft 11.3&#160;in) for adult males and 1.67 metres (5&#160;ft 5.7&#160;in) for adult females in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[168]</a></sup> People in the south are on average about 2&#160;cm (0.8 inches) shorter than those in the north.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grote_drukte_zomercarnaval_Rotterdam.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2727" data-file-width="4090" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Grote_drukte_zomercarnaval_Rotterdam.jpg/220px-Grote_drukte_zomercarnaval_Rotterdam.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Grote_drukte_zomercarnaval_Rotterdam.jpg/330px-Grote_drukte_zomercarnaval_Rotterdam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Grote_drukte_zomercarnaval_Rotterdam.jpg/440px-Grote_drukte_zomercarnaval_Rotterdam.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grote_drukte_zomercarnaval_Rotterdam.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> almost half the population has an immigrant background.</div></div></div>\n<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, in 2010 there were 1.8 million <a href="/wiki/Foreign_born" title="Foreign born">foreign-born residents</a> in the Netherlands, corresponding to 11.1% of the total population. Of these, 1.4 million (8.5%) were born outside the EU and 0.43 million (2.6%) were born in another EU Member State.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[169]</a></sup> On 21 November 2016, there were 3.8 million residents in the Netherlands with at least one foreign-born parent ("migration background").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[170]</a></sup> Over half the young people in Amsterdam and Rotterdam have a non-western background.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[171]</a></sup> Dutch people, or <a href="/wiki/Dutch_diaspora" title="Dutch diaspora">descendants of Dutch people</a>, are also found in migrant communities worldwide, notably in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> (2006), more than 5&#160;million Americans claim total or partial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_American" title="Dutch American">Dutch</a> ancestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[172]</a></sup> There are close to 3&#160;million Dutch-descended <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afrikaner" title="Afrikaner">Afrikaners</a> living in South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[173]</a></sup> In 1940, there were 290,000 Europeans and Eurasians in Indonesia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[174]</a></sup> but most have since left the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[175]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Netherlands is the 24th <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_population_density" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by population density">most densely populated</a> country in the world, with 408.53 inhabitants per square kilometre (1,060/sq&#160;mi) or &#8211; if only the land area is counted (33,883&#160;km<sup>2</sup>, 13,082&#160;sq&#160;mi) &#8211; 500.89 inhabitants per square kilometre (1,300/sq&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[176]</a></sup> When the land area of the provinces only is counted (33,718&#160;km<sup>2</sup>, 13,019&#160;sq&#160;mi), a number of 500 inhabitants per square kilometre (1,290/sq&#160;mi) was reached in the first half of 2014. The <a href="/wiki/Randstad" title="Randstad">Randstad</a> is the country\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbation</a> located in the west of the country and contains the four largest cities: Amsterdam in the province <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> in the province <a href="/wiki/South_Holland" title="South Holland">South Holland</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utrecht_(city)" title="Utrecht (city)">Utrecht</a> in the province <a href="/wiki/Utrecht_(province)" title="Utrecht (province)">Utrecht</a>. The Randstad has a population of 7&#160;million inhabitants and is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Europe_by_population" title="List of metropolitan areas in Europe by population">5th largest</a> <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> in Europe. According to Dutch Central Statistics Bureau, in 2015, 28 percent of Dutch population had a spendable income above 40,000 euros (which does not include spendings on health care or education).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[177]</a></sup>\n</p><p><br/>\n</p>\n<table class="navbox">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th class="navbox-title" colspan="10"><div style="float:right; title="Template:Largest cities of the Netherlands"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Largest_cities_of_the_Netherlands" title="Template style="height:2.6em;line-height:1.3em;"><span style="font-size:110%;">Largest municipalities in the Netherlands</span><br/><div style="display:inline;font-weight:normal;"><a style="text-align:right;">124,719\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Functional_urban_areas">Functional urban areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Functional urban areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Density_Netherlands_2007.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2644" data-file-width="2333" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Density_Netherlands_2007.png/220px-Density_Netherlands_2007.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Density_Netherlands_2007.png/330px-Density_Netherlands_2007.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Density_Netherlands_2007.png/440px-Density_Netherlands_2007.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Density_Netherlands_2007.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population density in the Netherlands</div></div></div>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left;">\n<tbody><tr style="font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n<th align="center"><a href="/wiki/Larger_urban_zone" title="Larger urban zone">Functional urban areas</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[179]</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th align="center">Population<br/>(2011)\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" align="right">1,419,000\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>\n</td>\n<td align="right">850,000\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Utrecht" align="right">695,000\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Groningen" title="Groningen">Groningen</a>\n</td>\n<td align="right">482,000\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Enschede" title="Enschede">Enschede</a>\n</td>\n<td align="right">402,000\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Netherlands" title="Languages of the Netherlands">Languages of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Foreign_languages_Netherlands,_2005.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="424" data-file-width="712" decoding="async" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png/350px-Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png/525px-Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png/700px-Foreign_languages_Netherlands%2C_2005.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Foreign_languages_Netherlands,_2005.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Knowledge of foreign languages in the Netherlands, in percent of the population over 15, 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[180]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The official language is <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, which is spoken by the vast majority of the inhabitants. Besides Dutch, <a href="/wiki/West_Frisian_language" title="West Frisian language">West Frisian</a> is recognised as a second official language in the northern province of <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a> (<i>Frysl&#226;n</i> in West Frisian).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[181]</a></sup> West Frisian has a formal status for government correspondence in that province. In the European part of the kingdom two other regional languages are recognised under the <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[182]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first of these recognised regional languages is <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Low_Saxon" title="Dutch Low Saxon">Low Saxon</a> (<i>Nedersaksisch</i> in Dutch). Low Saxon consists of several dialects spoken in the north and east, like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twents" title="Twents">Twents</a> in the region of <a href="/wiki/Twente" title="Twente">Twente</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drents" title="Drents">Drents</a> in the province of <a href="/wiki/Drenthe" title="Drenthe">Drenthe</a>. Secondly, <a href="/wiki/Limburgish" title="Limburgish">Limburgish</a> is also recognised as a regional language. It consists of Dutch varieties of <a href="/wiki/Meuse-Rhenish" title="Meuse-Rhenish">Meuse-Rhenish</a> <a href="/wiki/Franconian_languages" title="Franconian languages">Franconian languages</a> and is spoken in the south-eastern province of <a href="/wiki/Limburg_(Netherlands)" title="Limburg (Netherlands)">Limburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-international2000_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-international2000-92">[83]</a></sup> The dialects most spoken in the Netherlands are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brabantian" title="Brabantian">Brabantian</a>-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hollandic" title="Hollandic">Hollandic</a> dialects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[183]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ripuarian_language" title="Ripuarian language">Ripuarian language</a>, which is spoken in <a href="/wiki/Kerkrade" title="Kerkrade">Kerkrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vaals" title="Vaals">Vaals</a> in the form of, respectively, the <a href="/wiki/Kerkrade_dialect" title="Kerkrade dialect">Kerkrade dialect</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vaals_dialect" title="Vaals dialect">Vaals dialect</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[185]</a></sup> is not recognised as a regional language of the Netherlands. These dialects are however sometimes considered to be a part of or related to <a href="/wiki/Limburgish" title="Limburgish">Limburgish</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/English_in_the_Netherlands" title="English in the Netherlands">English</a> has a formal status in the special municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a>. It is widely spoken on these islands. <a href="/wiki/Papiamento" title="Papiamento">Papiamento</a> has a formal status in the special municipality of <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>. <a href="/wiki/Yiddish" title="Yiddish">Yiddish</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani language</a> were recognised in 1996 as non-territorial languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[186]</a></sup> The Netherlands has a tradition of learning foreign languages, formalised in Dutch education laws. Some 90% of the total population indicate <a href="/wiki/English_in_the_Netherlands" title="English in the Netherlands">they are able to converse in English</a>, 70% in German, and 29% in French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[187]</a></sup> English is a mandatory course in all secondary schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xyz_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-xyz-199">[188]</a></sup> In most lower level secondary school educations (<i><a href="/wiki/Voorbereidend_middelbaar_beroepsonderwijs" title="Voorbereidend middelbaar beroepsonderwijs">vmbo</a></i>), one additional modern foreign language is mandatory during the first two years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schedule_of_the_Central_Exams_of_2009_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schedule_of_the_Central_Exams_of_2009-200">[189]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In higher level secondary schools (<a href="/wiki/Hoger_algemeen_voortgezet_onderwijs" title="Hoger algemeen voortgezet onderwijs">HAVO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Voorbereidend_wetenschappelijk_onderwijs" title="Voorbereidend wetenschappelijk onderwijs">VWO</a>), two additional modern foreign languages are mandatory during the first three years. Only during the last three years in VWO one foreign language is mandatory. Besides English, the standard modern languages are <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, although schools can replace one of these modern languages with <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> or <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Examenblad_talen_vwo_2019_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-Examenblad_talen_vwo_2019-201">[190]</a></sup> Additionally, schools in Friesland teach and have exams in <a href="/wiki/West_Frisian_language" title="West Frisian language">West Frisian</a>, and schools across the country teach and have exams in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for secondary school (called <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">Gymnasium</a> or VWO+).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Netherlands" title="Religion in the Netherlands">Religion in the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">\n<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">\n<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 15915.284869156px; border-left-color:Brown"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Brown"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Brown"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 1323.776965281px; border-left-color:Green"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Green"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 248.00703903114px; border-left-color:Cyan"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Cyan"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Cyan"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 125.62719357843px; border-left-color:Blue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Blue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Blue"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:99.715890026061px 7.5326805527929px 0 0; border-top-color:DarkBlue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DarkBlue"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:0.62831439655591px 99.998026085614px 0 0; border-top-color:Honeydew"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Honeydew"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>Religious identification in the Netherlands (2015)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbs2016_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-cbs2016-10">[6]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Honeydew; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irreligious" title="Irreligious">Irreligious</a> (50.1%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> (23.7%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Protestant_Church_in_the_Netherlands" title="Protestant Church in the Netherlands">Protestant Church in the Netherlands</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[l]</a></sup> (15.5%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Cyan; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[m]</a></sup> (4.6%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Netherlands" title="Islam in the Netherlands">Muslim</a> (4.9%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Brown; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other (1.1%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>The Dutch are one of the least religious people in the world. Religion in the Netherlands was predominantly <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> until late into the 20th century. Although religious diversity remains, there has been a decline of religious adherence.\n</p><p>In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Statistics_Netherlands" title="Statistics Netherlands">Statistics Netherlands</a>, the Dutch governmental institution that gathers statistical information about the Netherlands, found that 50.1% of the total population declared to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-religious" title="Non-religious">non-religious</a>. Groups that represent the non-religious in the Netherlands include <a href="/wiki/Humanistisch_Verbond" title="Humanistisch Verbond">Humanistisch Verbond</a>. Christians comprised the 43.8% of the total population and were divided in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholics" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> with 23.7%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">Protestants</a> with a membership in the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Church_in_the_Netherlands" title="Protestant Church in the Netherlands">Protestant Church in the Netherlands</a> with 15.5% and other Christians (including Protestants without a membership in the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Church_in_the_Netherlands" title="Protestant Church in the Netherlands">Protestant Church in the Netherlands</a>) with 4.6%. <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> comprised the 4.9% of the total population and other religions (like <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>) comprised the remaining 1.1%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbs2016_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-cbs2016-10">[6]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to an independent in-depth interviewing by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radboud_University" title="Radboud University">Radboud University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vrije_Universiteit_Amsterdam" title="Vrije Universiteit Amsterdam">Vrije Universiteit Amsterdam</a> in 2006, 34% of the Dutch population identified as a Christian,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nos.nl_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-nos.nl-205">[192]</a></sup> decreasing till in 2015 almost 25% of the population adhered to one of the Christian faiths (11.7% Roman Catholic, 8.6% PKN, 4.2% other small Christian denominations), 5 percent is Muslim and 2 percent adheres to Hinduism or Buddhism, approximately 67.8% of the population in 2015 has <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">no religious affiliation</a>, up from 61% in 2006, 53% in 1996, 43% 1979 and 33% in 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BerntsA_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-BerntsA-206">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[194]</a></sup> The Sociaal en Cultureel Planbureau (Social and Cultural Planning Agency, SCP) expects the number of non-affiliated Dutch to be at 72% in 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[195]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Constitution of the Netherlands guarantees freedom of education, which means that all schools that adhere to general quality criteria receive the same government funding. This includes schools based on religious principles by religious groups (especially Roman Catholic and various Protestant). Three political parties in the Dutch parliament, (<a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Appeal" title="Christian Democratic Appeal">CDA</a>, and two small parties, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ChristianUnion" title="ChristianUnion">ChristianUnion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Political_Party" title="Reformed Political Party">SGP</a>) are based upon the Christian belief. Several Christian religious holidays are national holidays (Christmas, Easter, <a href="/wiki/Pentecost" title="Pentecost">Pentecost</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ascension_of_Jesus" title="Ascension of Jesus">Ascension of Jesus</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[196]</a></sup> In the late 19th century atheism began to rise as secularism, <a href="/wiki/Pillarisation" title="Pillarisation">liberalism and socialism</a> grew. By 1960, Protestantism shrunk demographically to equal Roman Catholicism, and going onwards, both Christian branches began to decline. There is one major exception: Islam which grew considerably as the result of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Netherlands#Im-_and_Emigration" title="Demographics of the Netherlands">immigration</a>. Since the year 2000 there has been raised awareness of religion, mainly due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_extremism" title="Muslim extremism">Muslim extremism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[197]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Monarchy of the Netherlands">Dutch royal family</a> has been traditionally associated with <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a>, specifically the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">1795 disestablished</a> and now non-existent <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed Church</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed Church</a> has been the only major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> church in the Netherlands from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> up until the 19th century. It encompassed the vast majority of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">Protestants</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformed_tradition" title="Reformed tradition">Reformed tradition</a> until a series of splits <a href="/wiki/1834_Dutch_Reformed_Church_split" title="1834 Dutch Reformed Church split">in 1834</a> and <a href="/wiki/1886_Dutch_Reformed_Church_split" title="1886 Dutch Reformed Church split">in 1886</a> diversified Dutch Calvinism. In 2013, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> became <a href="/wiki/Queen_consort" title="Queen consort">Queen consort</a>.\n</p><p>From a December 2014 survey by the VU University Amsterdam it was concluded that for the first time there are more atheists (25%) than theists (17%) in the Netherlands. The majority of the population being agnostic (31%) or <a href="/wiki/Ietsism" title="Ietsism">ietsistic</a> (27%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trouw.nl_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-trouw.nl-211">[198]</a></sup> In 2015, a vast majority of the inhabitants of the Netherlands (82%) said they had never or almost never visited a church, and 59% stated that they had never been to a church of any kind. Of all the people questioned, 24% saw themselves as atheist, an increase of 11% compared to the previous study done in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BerntsA_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-BerntsA-206">[193]</a></sup> The expected rise of spirituality (ietsism) has come to a halt according to research in 2015. In 2006 40% of respondents considered themselves spiritual, in 2015 this has dropped to 31%. The number who believed in the existence of a higher power fell from 36% to 28% over the same period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nos.nl_205-1"><a href="#cite_note-nos.nl-205">[192]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is currently the largest religion in the Netherlands. The provinces of <a href="/wiki/North_Brabant" title="North Brabant">North Brabant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limburg_(Netherlands)" title="Limburg (Netherlands)">Limburg</a> have historically been strongly Roman Catholic, and some of their people might still consider the Catholic Church as a base for their <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Christian" title="Cultural Christian">cultural identity</a>. Protestantism in the Netherlands consists of a number of churches within various traditions. The largest of these is the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Church_in_the_Netherlands" title="Protestant Church in the Netherlands">Protestant Church in the Netherlands</a> (PKN), a <a href="/wiki/United_and_uniting_churches" title="United and uniting churches">United</a> church which is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformed" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a> in orientation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS_2009_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBS_2009-212">[199]</a></sup> It was formed in 2004 as a merger of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Churches_in_the_Netherlands" title="Reformed Churches in the Netherlands">Reformed Churches in the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in the Kingdom of the Netherlands">a smaller Lutheran Church</a>. Several orthodox Reformed and liberal churches did not merge into the PKN. Although in the Netherlands as a whole Christianity has become a minority, the Netherlands contains a <a href="/wiki/Bible_Belt_(Netherlands)" title="Bible Belt (Netherlands)">Bible Belt</a> from <a href="/wiki/Zeeland" title="Zeeland">Zeeland</a> to the northern parts of the province <a href="/wiki/Overijssel" title="Overijssel">Overijssel</a>, in which Protestant (particularly Reformed) beliefs remain strong, and even has majorities in municipal councils.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is the second largest religion in the state.
