In 2012, there were about 825,000 <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Netherlands" title="Islam in the Netherlands">Muslims</a> in the Netherlands (5% of the population).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS2_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBS2-213">[200]</a></sup> Muslim numbers increased from the 1960 as a consequence of large numbers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Netherlands#Im-_and_Emigration" title="Demographics of the Netherlands">migrant workers</a>. This included migrants from former <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch colonies</a>, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surinam" title="Surinam">Surinam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, but mainly migrant workers from <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>. During the 1990s, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_refugees" title="Muslim refugees">Muslim refugees</a> arrived from countries like <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[201]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other religions account for some 6% of the Dutch people. Hinduism is a minority religion in the Netherlands, with around 215,000 adherents (slightly over 1% of the population). Most of these are <a href="/wiki/Indo-Surinamese" title="Indo-Surinamese">Indo-Surinamese</a>. There are also sizable populations of Hindu immigrants from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, and some Western adherents of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_the_West" title="Hinduism in the West">Hinduism-oriented new religious movements</a> such as <a href="/wiki/International_Society_for_Krishna_Consciousness" title="International Society for Krishna Consciousness">Hare Krishnas</a>. The Netherlands has an estimated 250,000 <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_the_Netherlands" title="Buddhism in the Netherlands">Buddhists</a> or people strongly attracted to this religion, mainly ethnic Dutch people. There are about 45,000 <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Netherlands" title="History of the Jews in the Netherlands">Jews</a> in the Netherlands.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Netherlands" title="Education in the Netherlands">Education in the Netherlands</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universities_in_the_Netherlands" title="Universities in the Netherlands">Universities in the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BSN_Junior_School_Vlaskamp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2326" data-file-width="3500" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/BSN_Junior_School_Vlaskamp.jpg/220px-BSN_Junior_School_Vlaskamp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/BSN_Junior_School_Vlaskamp.jpg/330px-BSN_Junior_School_Vlaskamp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/BSN_Junior_School_Vlaskamp.jpg/440px-BSN_Junior_School_Vlaskamp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BSN_Junior_School_Vlaskamp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A primary school in The Hague</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ACTA_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2935" data-file-width="4402" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/ACTA_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-ACTA_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/ACTA_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-ACTA_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/ACTA_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-ACTA_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ACTA_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/University_of_Amsterdam" title="University of Amsterdam">University of Amsterdam</a> building</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Utrecht-Uithof,_from_CambridgeLaan_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Utrecht-Uithof%2C_from_CambridgeLaan_01.jpg/220px-Utrecht-Uithof%2C_from_CambridgeLaan_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Utrecht-Uithof%2C_from_CambridgeLaan_01.jpg/330px-Utrecht-Uithof%2C_from_CambridgeLaan_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Utrecht-Uithof%2C_from_CambridgeLaan_01.jpg/440px-Utrecht-Uithof%2C_from_CambridgeLaan_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Utrecht-Uithof,_from_CambridgeLaan_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View on the Utrecht Science Park of <a href="/wiki/Utrecht_University" title="Utrecht University">Utrecht University</a>. The building in the centre is the library</div></div></div>\n<p>Education in the Netherlands is compulsory between the ages of 5 and 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[202]</a></sup> If a child does not have a "startqualification" (HAVO, VWO or MBO 2+ degree) they are still forced to follow classes until they achieve such a qualification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[203]</a></sup>\n</p><p>All children in the Netherlands usually attend elementary school from (on average) ages 4 to 12. It comprises eight grades, the first of which is facultative. Based on an aptitude test, the eighth grade teacher\'s recommendation and the opinion of the pupil\'s parents or caretakers, a choice is made for one of the three main streams of secondary education. After completing a particular stream, a pupil may still continue in the penultimate year of the next stream.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Voorbereidend_middelbaar_beroepsonderwijs" title="Voorbereidend middelbaar beroepsonderwijs">VMBO</a> has 4 grades and is subdivided over several levels. Successfully completing the vmbo results in a low-level vocational degree that grants access to the MBO. The MBO (middle-level applied education) is a form of education primarily focuses on teaching a practical trade, or a vocational degree. With the MBO certification, a student can apply for the HBO. The <a href="/wiki/Hoger_algemeen_voortgezet_onderwijs" title="Hoger algemeen voortgezet onderwijs">HAVO</a> has 5 grades and allows for admission to the HBO. The HBO (higher professional education) are <a href="/wiki/Vocational_university" title="Vocational university">universities of professional education</a> (applied sciences) that award professional bachelor\'s degrees; similar to polytechnic degrees. A HBO degree gives access to the university system. The <a href="/wiki/Voorbereidend_wetenschappelijk_onderwijs" title="Voorbereidend wetenschappelijk onderwijs">VWO</a> (comprising <a href="/wiki/Atheneum_(school)" title="Atheneum (school)">atheneum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">gymnasium</a>) has 6 grades and prepares for studying at a research university. Universities offer of a three-year bachelor\'s degree, followed by a one or two year master\'s degree, which in turn can be followed by a four or five-year <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doctoral_degree" title="Doctoral degree">doctoral degree</a> program.\n</p><p>Doctoral candidates in the Netherlands are generally non-tenured employees of a university. All Dutch schools and universities are publicly funded and managed with the exception of religious schools that are publicly funded but not managed by the state even though requirements are necessary for the funding to be authorised. Dutch universities have a tuition fee of about 2,000 euros a year for students from the Netherlands and the European Union. The amount is about 10,000 euros for non-EU students.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_the_Netherlands" title="Healthcare in the Netherlands">Healthcare in the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_(1632-1723)._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2547" data-file-width="2148" decoding="async" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg/220px-Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg/330px-Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg/440px-Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_%281632-1723%29._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anthonie_van_Leeuwenhoek_(1632-1723)._Natuurkundige_te_Delft_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-957.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portrait of <a href="/wiki/Antonie_van_Leeuwenhoek" title="Antonie van Leeuwenhoek">Antonie van Leeuwenhoek</a> (1632&#8211;1723), known as "the father of microbiology"</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meander_MC_noordzijde_1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Meander_MC_noordzijde_1.JPG/220px-Meander_MC_noordzijde_1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Meander_MC_noordzijde_1.JPG/330px-Meander_MC_noordzijde_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Meander_MC_noordzijde_1.JPG/440px-Meander_MC_noordzijde_1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meander_MC_noordzijde_1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A public hospital in <a href="/wiki/Amersfoort" title="Amersfoort">Amersfoort</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 2016, the Netherlands has maintained its number one position at the top of the annual <a href="/wiki/Euro_health_consumer_index" title="Euro health consumer index">Euro health consumer index</a> (EHCI), which compares healthcare systems in Europe, scoring 916 of a maximum 1,000 points. The Netherlands has been in the top three countries in each report published since 2005. On 48 indicators such as patient rights and information, accessibility, prevention and outcomes, the Netherlands secured its top position among 37 European countries for the sixth year in a row.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[204]</a></sup>\nThe Netherlands was ranked first in a study in 2009 comparing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_care_system" title="Health care system">health care systems</a> of the United States, Australia, Canada, Germany and New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[206]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ever since a major reform of the health care system in 2006, the Dutch system received more points in the Index each year. According to the HCP (<a href="/wiki/Health_Consumer_Powerhouse" title="Health Consumer Powerhouse">Health Consumer Powerhouse</a>), the Netherlands has \'a chaos system\', meaning patients have a great degree of freedom from where to buy their health insurance, to where they get their healthcare service. The difference between the Netherlands and other countries is that the chaos is managed. Healthcare decisions are being made in a dialogue between the patients and healthcare professionals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[207]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Health insurance in the Netherlands is mandatory. Healthcare in the Netherlands is covered by two statutory forms of insurance:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Zorgverzekeringswet (ZVW), often called "basic insurance", covers common medical care.</li>\n<li>Algemene Wet Bijzondere Ziektekosten (AWBZ) covers long-term nursing and care.</li></ul>\n<p>While Dutch residents are automatically insured by the government for AWBZ, everyone has to take out their own basic healthcare insurance (basisverzekering), except those under 18 who are automatically covered under their parents\' premium. If you don\'t take out insurance, you risk a fine. Insurers have to offer a universal package for everyone over the age of 18 years, regardless of age or state of health &#8211; it\'s illegal to refuse an application or impose special conditions. In contrast to many other European systems, the Dutch government is responsible for the accessibility and quality of the healthcare system in the Netherlands, but not in charge of its management.\n</p><p>Healthcare in the Netherlands can be divided in several ways: three echelons, in somatic and mental health care and in \'cure\' (short term) and \'care\' (long term). Home doctors (<i>huisartsen</i>, comparable to <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">general practitioners</a>) form the largest part of the first echelon. Being referenced by a member of the first echelon is mandatory for access to the second and third echelon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boot_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boot-221">[208]</a></sup> The health care system is in comparison to other Western countries quite effective but not the most cost-effective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BCG_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-BCG-222">[209]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Healthcare in the Netherlands is financed by a dual system that came into effect in January 2006. Long-term treatments, especially those that involve semi-permanent hospitalisation, and also disability costs such as wheelchairs, are covered by a state-controlled mandatory insurance. This is laid down in the <i><a href="/wiki/AWBZ" title="AWBZ">Algemene Wet Bijzondere Ziektekosten</a></i> ("General Law on Exceptional Healthcare Costs") which first came into effect in 1968. In 2009 this insurance covered 27% of all health care expenses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statline.cbs.nl_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-statline.cbs.nl-223">[210]</a></sup>\n</p><p>For all regular (short-term) medical treatment, there is a system of obligatory <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a>, with private health insurance companies. These insurance companies are obliged to provide a package with a defined set of insured treatments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-minvws.nl_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-minvws.nl-224">[211]</a></sup> This insurance covers 41% of all health care expenses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statline.cbs.nl_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-statline.cbs.nl-223">[210]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other sources of health care payment are taxes (14%), out of pocket payments (9%), additional optional health insurance packages (4%) and a range of other sources (4%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statline.cbs.nl_223-2"><a href="#cite_note-statline.cbs.nl-223">[210]</a></sup> Affordability is guaranteed through a system of income-related allowances and individual and employer-paid income-related premiums.\n</p><p>A key feature of the Dutch system is that premiums may not be related to health status or age. Risk variances between private health insurance companies due to the different risks presented by individual policy holders are compensated through <a href="/wiki/Risk_equalization" title="Risk equalization">risk equalisation</a> and a common <a href="/wiki/Risk_pool" title="Risk pool">risk pool</a>. Funding for all short-term health care is 50% from employers, 45% from the insured person and 5% by the government. Children under 18 are covered for free. Those on low incomes receive compensation to help them pay their insurance. Premiums paid by the insured are about &#8364;100 per month (about US$127 in August 2010 and in 2012 &#8364;150 or US$196,) with variation of about 5% between the various competing insurers, and deductible a year &#8364;220 (U.S. $288).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Netherlands" title="Culture of the Netherlands">Culture of the Netherlands</a></div>\n<h3><span id="Art.2C_philosophy_and_literature"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Art,_philosophy_and_literature">Art, philosophy and literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Art, philosophy and literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_art" title="Dutch art">Dutch art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_the_Netherlands" title="Architecture of the Netherlands">Architecture of the Netherlands</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_literature" title="Dutch literature">Dutch literature</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:146px;max-width:146px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:169px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meisje_met_de_parel.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="4794" data-file-width="4095" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Meisje_met_de_parel.jpg/144px-Meisje_met_de_parel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Meisje_met_de_parel.jpg/216px-Meisje_met_de_parel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Meisje_met_de_parel.jpg/288px-Meisje_met_de_parel.jpg 2x" width="144"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><i><a href="/wiki/Girl_with_a_Pearl_Earring" title="Girl with a Pearl Earring">Girl with a Pearl Earring</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Vermeer" title="Johannes Vermeer">Johannes Vermeer</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:142px;max-width:142px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:169px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vincent_van_Gogh_-_Self-portrait_with_grey_felt_hat_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3008" data-file-width="2481" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Vincent_van_Gogh_-_Self-portrait_with_grey_felt_hat_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/140px-Vincent_van_Gogh_-_Self-portrait_with_grey_felt_hat_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Vincent_van_Gogh_-_Self-portrait_with_grey_felt_hat_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/210px-Vincent_van_Gogh_-_Self-portrait_with_grey_felt_hat_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Vincent_van_Gogh_-_Self-portrait_with_grey_felt_hat_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/280px-Vincent_van_Gogh_-_Self-portrait_with_grey_felt_hat_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Self-portrait by <a href="/wiki/Vincent_van_Gogh" title="Vincent van Gogh">Vincent van Gogh</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:290px;max-width:290px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:161px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rijksmuseum_2022.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2577" data-file-width="4582" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Rijksmuseum_2022.jpg/288px-Rijksmuseum_2022.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Rijksmuseum_2022.jpg/432px-Rijksmuseum_2022.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Rijksmuseum_2022.jpg/576px-Rijksmuseum_2022.jpg 2x" width="288"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum" title="Rijksmuseum">Rijksmuseum</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:290px;max-width:290px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:91px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NEMO_and_area.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="944" data-file-width="2973" decoding="async" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/NEMO_and_area.jpg/288px-NEMO_and_area.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/NEMO_and_area.jpg/432px-NEMO_and_area.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/NEMO_and_area.jpg/576px-NEMO_and_area.jpg 2x" width="288"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The National <a href="/wiki/NEMO_(museum)" title="NEMO (museum)">NEMO Science Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nederlands_Scheepvaartmuseum" title="Nederlands Scheepvaartmuseum">Nederlands Scheepvaartmuseum</a> in second plan, in Amsterdam.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The Netherlands has had many well-known painters. The 17th century, in which the Dutch Republic was prosperous, was the age of the "Dutch Masters", such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rembrandt_Harmenszoon_van_Rijn" title="Rembrandt Harmenszoon van Rijn">Rembrandt van Rijn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Vermeer" title="Johannes Vermeer">Johannes Vermeer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Steen" title="Jan Steen">Jan Steen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacob_van_Ruisdael" title="Jacob van Ruisdael">Jacob van Ruisdael</a> and many others. Famous Dutch painters of the 19th and 20th century were <a href="/wiki/Vincent_van_Gogh" title="Vincent van Gogh">Vincent van Gogh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Piet_Mondrian" title="Piet Mondrian">Piet Mondriaan</a>. <a href="/wiki/M._C._Escher" title="M. C. Escher">M. C. Escher</a> is a well-known graphics artist. <a href="/wiki/Willem_de_Kooning" title="Willem de Kooning">Willem de Kooning</a> was born and trained in <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, although he is considered to have reached acclaim as an American artist.\n</p><p>The Netherlands is the country of philosophers <a href="/wiki/Erasmus" title="Erasmus">Erasmus of Rotterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baruch_Spinoza" title="Baruch Spinoza">Spinoza</a>. All of <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Descartes" title="Ren&#233; Descartes">Descartes</a>\' major work was done in the Netherlands since he studied at <a href="/wiki/Leiden_University" title="Leiden University">Leiden University</a> &#8212; as did throughout the centuries geologist <a href="/wiki/James_Hutton" title="James Hutton">James Hutton</a>, British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Stuart,_3rd_Earl_of_Bute" title="John Stuart, 3rd Earl of Bute">John Stuart</a>, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a>, Physics Nobel Prize laureate <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Lorentz" title="Hendrik Lorentz">Hendrik Lorentz</a> and Islam critic <a href="/wiki/Ayaan_Hirsi_Ali" title="Ayaan Hirsi Ali">Ayaan Hirsi Ali</a>. The Dutch scientist <a href="/wiki/Christiaan_Huygens" title="Christiaan Huygens">Christiaan Huygens</a> (1629&#8211;1695) discovered <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a>\'s moon <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">Titan</a>, argued that light travelled as waves, invented the <a href="/wiki/Pendulum_clock" title="Pendulum clock">pendulum clock</a> and was the first physicist to use mathematical formulae. <a href="/wiki/Antonie_van_Leeuwenhoek" title="Antonie van Leeuwenhoek">Antonie van Leeuwenhoek</a> was the first to observe and describe <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">single-celled organisms</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Microscope" title="Microscope">microscope</a>.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a>, literature flourished as well, with <a href="/wiki/Joost_van_den_Vondel" title="Joost van den Vondel">Joost van den Vondel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pieter_Corneliszoon_Hooft" title="Pieter Corneliszoon Hooft">P. C. Hooft</a> as the two most famous writers. In the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Multatuli" title="Multatuli">Multatuli</a> wrote about the poor treatment of the natives in the Dutch colony, the current Indonesia. Important 20th century authors include <a href="/wiki/Godfried_Bomans" title="Godfried Bomans">Godfried Bomans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Mulisch" title="Harry Mulisch">Harry Mulisch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Wolkers" title="Jan Wolkers">Jan Wolkers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Vestdijk" title="Simon Vestdijk">Simon Vestdijk</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hella_S._Haasse" title="Hella S. Haasse">Hella S. Haasse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cees_Nooteboom" title="Cees Nooteboom">Cees Nooteboom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerard_Reve" title="Gerard Reve">Gerard Reve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willem_Frederik_Hermans" title="Willem Frederik Hermans">Willem Frederik Hermans</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anne_Frank" title="Anne Frank">Anne Frank</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/The_Diary_of_a_Young_Girl" title="The Diary of a Young Girl"><i>Diary of a Young Girl</i></a> was published after she died in the Holocaust and translated from Dutch to all major languages.\n</p><p>The traditional Dutch architecture is especially valuated in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delft" title="Delft">Delft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leiden" title="Leiden">Leiden</a>, with 17 and 18th century buildings along the canals. Smaller village architecture with wooden houses is found in <a href="/wiki/Zaandam" title="Zaandam">Zaandam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marken" title="Marken">Marken</a>. Replicas of Dutch buildings can be found in <a href="/wiki/Huis_Ten_Bosch_(theme_park)" title="Huis Ten Bosch (theme park)">Huis Ten Bosch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>. A similar Holland Village is being built in <a href="/wiki/Shenyang" title="Shenyang">Shenyang</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">Windmills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tulip" title="Tulip">tulips</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clog_(shoe)" title="Clog (shoe)">wooden shoes</a>, cheese, <a href="/wiki/Delftware" title="Delftware">Delftware</a> pottery, and <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a> are among the items associated with the Netherlands by tourists.\n</p><p>The Netherlands has a long history of social tolerance and today is regarded as a liberal country, considering <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Drug policy of the Netherlands">its drug policy</a> and its legalisation of <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia_in_the_Netherlands" title="Euthanasia in the Netherlands">euthanasia</a>. On 1 April 2001, the Netherlands became the first nation to legalise <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_Netherlands" title="Same-sex marriage in the Netherlands">same-sex marriage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[212]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_value_system">Dutch value system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Dutch value system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_customs_and_etiquette" title="Dutch customs and etiquette">Dutch customs and etiquette</a></div>\n<p>Dutch society is <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">modern</a>. The Dutch have an aversion to the non-essential.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colin_White_1995_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_White_1995-226">[213]</a></sup> Ostentatious behaviour is to be avoided. The Dutch are proud of their <a href="/wiki/Cultural_heritage" title="Cultural heritage">cultural heritage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_art" title="Dutch art">rich history in art</a> and involvement in <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international affairs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colin_White_1995_226-1"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_White_1995-226">[213]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koningsdag_2017_Amstel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2132" data-file-width="3104" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Koningsdag_2017_Amstel.jpg/220px-Koningsdag_2017_Amstel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Koningsdag_2017_Amstel.jpg/330px-Koningsdag_2017_Amstel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Koningsdag_2017_Amstel.jpg/440px-Koningsdag_2017_Amstel.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koningsdag_2017_Amstel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dutch people in orange celebrating <a href="/wiki/Koningsdag" title="Koningsdag">King\'s Day</a> in Amsterdam, 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>Dutch manners are open and direct with a no-nonsense attitude; informality combined with adherence to basic behaviour. According to a humorous source on Dutch culture, "Their directness gives many the impression that they are rude and crude &#8212; attributes they prefer to call openness."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colin_White_1995_226-2"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_White_1995-226">[213]</a></sup> A well known more serious source on Dutch etiquette is "Dealing with the Dutch" from Jacob Vossestein: "Dutch egalitarianism is the idea that people are equal, especially from a moral point of view, and accordingly, causes the somewhat ambiguous stance the Dutch have towards hierarchy and status."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[214]</a></sup> As always, manners differ between groups. Asking about basic rules will not be considered impolite. "What may strike you as being blatantly blunt topics and comments are no more embarrassing or unusual to the Dutch than discussing the weather."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colin_White_1995_226-3"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_White_1995-226">[213]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Netherlands is one of the most secular countries of Europe, and religion is in the Netherlands generally considered as a personal matter which is not supposed to be propagated in public, although it often remains a discussion subject. For 17% of the population religion is important and 14% goes to church weekly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[215]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_people_and_ecology">Dutch people and ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Dutch people and ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Netherlands has the <a href="/wiki/Reputation" title="Reputation">reputation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Leadership" title="Leadership">leader</a> <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Environmental_science" title="Environmental science">environmental</a> and <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">population management</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[216]</a></sup> In 2015, Amsterdam and Rotterdam were, respectively, at the 4th and the 5th position on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arcadis_NV" title="Arcadis NV">Arcadis Sustainable Cities Index</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[218]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">Sustainability</a> is a concept important for the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>. The goal of the Dutch Government is to have a <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainable</a>, reliable and affordable energy system, by 2050, in which <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_in_Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Carbon dioxide in Earth\'s atmosphere">CO<sub>2</sub> emissions</a> have been halved and 40 percent of <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a> is derived from <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainable sources</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-232">[219]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a> is investing billions of euros in <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable energy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">CO<sub>2</sub> reduction</a>. The Kingdom also encourage Dutch <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Companies" title="Companies">companies</a> to build <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_business" title="Sustainable business">sustainable business</a>/<a href="/wiki/Project" title="Project">projects</a>/<a href="/wiki/Facility_management" title="Facility management">facilities</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Subsidy" title="Subsidy">financial aids</a> from the state to the companies or <a href="/wiki/Individual" title="Individual">individuals</a> who are active in making the <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> more <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainable</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-232">[219]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Netherlands" title="Music of the Netherlands">Music of the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_former_Netherlands_Antilles" title="Music of the former Netherlands Antilles">Music of the former Netherlands Antilles</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RUB9281213-111_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="5472" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RUB9281213-111_1.jpg/190px-RUB9281213-111_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RUB9281213-111_1.jpg/285px-RUB9281213-111_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RUB9281213-111_1.jpg/380px-RUB9281213-111_1.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RUB9281213-111_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Concertgebouw" title="Concertgebouw">Royal Concertgebouw</a> from the 19th century</div></div></div>\n<p>The Netherlands has multiple <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a> traditions. Traditional Dutch music is a genre known as "<a href="/wiki/Levenslied" title="Levenslied">Levenslied</a>", meaning <i>Song of life</i>, to an extent comparable to a French <a href="/wiki/Chanson" title="Chanson">Chanson</a> or a German <a href="/wiki/Schlager_music" title="Schlager music">Schlager</a>. These songs typically have a simple melody and rhythm, and a straightforward structure of couplets and choruses. Themes can be light, but are often sentimental and include <a href="/wiki/Love" title="Love">love</a>, <a href="/wiki/Death" title="Death">death</a> and <a href="/wiki/Loneliness" title="Loneliness">loneliness</a>. Traditional musical instruments such as the <a href="/wiki/Accordion" title="Accordion">accordion</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Barrel_organ" title="Barrel organ">barrel organ</a> are a staple of levenslied music, though in recent years many artists also use synthesisers and guitars. Artists in this genre include <a href="/wiki/Jan_Smit_(singer)" title="Jan Smit (singer)">Jan Smit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frans_Bauer" title="Frans Bauer">Frans Bauer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Hazes" title="Andr&#233; Hazes">Andr&#233; Hazes</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="284" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG/190px-Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG/285px-Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG/380px-Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG 2x" width="190"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anouk_at_fesival_mundial_2008.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pop singer <a href="/wiki/Anouk_(singer)" title="Anouk (singer)">Anouk</a> in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[220]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coldplay_perform_%22Up%26Up%22,_Amsterdam_Arena,_June_2016_(5).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1667" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Coldplay_perform_%22Up%26Up%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg/190px-Coldplay_perform_%22Up%26Up%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Coldplay_perform_%22Up%26Up%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg/285px-Coldplay_perform_%22Up%26Up%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Coldplay_perform_%22Up%26Up%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg/380px-Coldplay_perform_%22Up%26Up%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coldplay_perform_%22Up%26Up%22,_Amsterdam_Arena,_June_2016_(5).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff_Arena" title="Johan Cruyff Arena">Johan Cruyff Arena</a>, largest Dutch concert venue</div></div></div>\n<p>Contemporary Dutch <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop music</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nederpop" title="Nederpop">Nederpop</a>) originated in the 1960s, heavily influenced by popular music from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a>. In the 1960s and 1970s the lyrics were mostly in English, and some tracks were instrumental. Bands such as <a href="/wiki/Shocking_Blue" title="Shocking Blue">Shocking Blue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Earring" title="Golden Earring">Golden Earring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tee_Set" title="Tee Set">Tee Set</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Baker_Selection" title="George Baker Selection">George Baker Selection</a> and <a href="/wiki/Focus_(band)" title="Focus (band)">Focus</a> enjoyed international success. As of the 1980s, more and more pop musicians started working in the Dutch language, partly inspired by the huge success of the band <a href="/wiki/Doe_Maar" title="Doe Maar">Doe Maar</a>. Today Dutch rock and pop music thrives in both languages, with some artists recording in both.\n</p><p>Current <a href="/wiki/Symphonic_metal" title="Symphonic metal">symphonic metal</a> bands <a href="/wiki/Epica_(band)" title="Epica (band)">Epica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delain" title="Delain">Delain</a>, <a href="/wiki/ReVamp" title="ReVamp">ReVamp</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Gathering_(band)" title="The Gathering (band)">The Gathering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asrai" title="Asrai">Asrai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autumn" title="Autumn">Autumn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ayreon" title="Ayreon">Ayreon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Within_Temptation" title="Within Temptation">Within Temptation</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> and pop singer <a href="/wiki/Caro_Emerald" title="Caro Emerald">Caro Emerald</a> are having international success. Also, metal bands like <a href="/wiki/Hail_of_Bullets" title="Hail of Bullets">Hail of Bullets</a>, <a href="/wiki/God_Dethroned" title="God Dethroned">God Dethroned</a>, <a href="/wiki/Izegrim" title="Izegrim">Izegrim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asphyx" title="Asphyx">Asphyx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Textures_(band)" title="Textures (band)">Textures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Present_Danger" title="Present Danger">Present Danger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heidevolk" title="Heidevolk">Heidevolk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slechtvalk" title="Slechtvalk">Slechtvalk</a> are popular guests at the biggest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metal_festival" title="Metal festival">metal festivals</a> in Europe. Contemporary local stars include pop singer <a href="/wiki/Anouk_(singer)" title="Anouk (singer)">Anouk</a>, country pop singer <a href="/wiki/Ilse_DeLange" title="Ilse DeLange">Ilse DeLange</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Guelderish" title="South Guelderish">South Guelderish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limburgish" title="Limburgish">Limburgish</a> dialect singing folk band <a href="/wiki/Rowwen_H%C3%A8ze" title="Rowwen H&#232;ze">Rowwen H&#232;ze</a>, rock band <a href="/wiki/BL%C3%98F" title="BL&#216;F">BL&#216;F</a> and duo <a href="/wiki/Nick_%26_Simon" title="Nick &amp; Simon">Nick &amp; Simon</a>.\n</p><p>Early 1990s Dutch and <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgian</a> <a href="/wiki/House_music" title="House music">house music</a> came together in <a href="/wiki/Eurodance" title="Eurodance">Eurodance</a> project <a href="/wiki/2_Unlimited" title="2 Unlimited">2 Unlimited</a>. Selling 18 million records,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[221]</a></sup> the two singers in the band are the most successful Dutch music artists to this day. Tracks like "<a href="/wiki/Get_Ready_for_This" title="Get Ready for This">Get Ready for This</a>" are still popular themes of U.S. sports events, like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NHL" title="NHL">NHL</a>. In the mid 1990s Dutch language <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">rap and hip hop</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Dutch_hip_hop" title="Dutch hip hop">Nederhop</a></i>) also came to fruition and has become popular in the Netherlands and Belgium. Artists with North African, Caribbean or Middle Eastern origins have strongly influenced this genre.\n</p><p>Since the 1990s, Dutch <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">electronic dance music</a> (EDM) gained widespread popularity in the world in many forms, from <a href="/wiki/Trance" title="Trance">trance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Techno" title="Techno">techno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gabber" title="Gabber">gabber</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hardstyle" title="Hardstyle">hardstyle</a>. Some of the world\'s best known dance music DJs hail from the Netherlands, including <a href="/wiki/Armin_van_Buuren" title="Armin van Buuren">Armin van Buuren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ti%C3%ABsto" title="Ti&#235;sto">Ti&#235;sto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hardwell" title="Hardwell">Hardwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Garrix" title="Martin Garrix">Martin Garrix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dash_Berlin" title="Dash Berlin">Dash Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicky_Romero" title="Nicky Romero">Nicky Romero</a>, <a href="/wiki/W%26W" title="W&amp;W">W&amp;W</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Diablo" title="Don Diablo">Don Diablo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afrojack" title="Afrojack">Afrojack</a>; the first four of which have been ranked as best in the world by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DJ_Mag_Top_100_DJs" title="DJ Mag Top 100 DJs">DJ Mag Top 100 DJs</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Dance_Event" title="Amsterdam Dance Event">Amsterdam Dance Event</a> (ADE) is the world\'s leading electronic music conference and the biggest club festival for the many electronic subgenres on the planet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[223]</a></sup> These DJs also contribute to the world\'s mainstream pop music, as they frequently collaborate and produce for high-profile international artists.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jan_Sweelinck" title="Jan Sweelinck">Jan Sweelinck</a> ranks as the Dutch most famous composer, with <a href="/wiki/Louis_Andriessen" title="Louis Andriessen">Louis Andriessen</a> amongst the best known living Dutch classical composers. <a href="/wiki/Ton_Koopman" title="Ton Koopman">Ton Koopman</a> is a Dutch conductor, organist and harpsichordist. He is also professor at the Royal Conservatory of The Hague. Notable violinists are <a href="/wiki/Janine_Jansen" title="Janine Jansen">Janine Jansen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Rieu" title="Andr&#233; Rieu">Andr&#233; Rieu</a>. The latter, together with his <a href="/wiki/Johann_Strauss_Orchestra" title="Johann Strauss Orchestra">Johann Strauss Orchestra</a>, has taken classical and <a href="/wiki/Waltz_(music)" title="Waltz (music)">waltz music</a> on worldwide concert tours, the size and revenue of which are otherwise only seen from the world\'s biggest rock and pop music acts. The most famous Dutch classical composition is "<a href="/wiki/Canto_Ostinato" title="Canto Ostinato">Canto Ostinato</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Simeon_ten_Holt" title="Simeon ten Holt">Simeon ten Holt</a>, a minimalistic composition for multiple instruments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[226]</a></sup> Acclaimed harpist <a href="/wiki/Lavinia_Meijer" title="Lavinia Meijer">Lavinia Meijer</a> in 2012 released an album with works from <a href="/wiki/Philip_Glass" title="Philip Glass">Philip Glass</a> that she transcribed for harp, with approval of Glass himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[227]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Concertgebouw" title="Concertgebouw">Concertgebouw</a> (completed in 1888) in Amsterdam is home to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Concertgebouw_Orchestra" title="Royal Concertgebouw Orchestra">Royal Concertgebouw Orchestra</a>, considered one of the world\'s finest orchestras.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[228]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_television">Film and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Film and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_Netherlands" title="Cinema of the Netherlands">Cinema of the Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Television_in_the_Netherlands" title="Television in the Netherlands">Television in the Netherlands</a></div>\n<p>Some Dutch films &#8211; mainly by director <a href="/wiki/Paul_Verhoeven" title="Paul Verhoeven">Paul Verhoeven</a> &#8211; have received international distribution and recognition, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Turkish_Delight_(1973_film)" title="Turkish Delight (1973 film)">Turkish Delight</a></i> ("<i>Turks Fruit</i>", 1973), <i><a href="/wiki/Soldier_of_Orange" title="Soldier of Orange">Soldier of Orange</a></i> ("<i>Soldaat van Oranje</i>", 1977), <i><a href="/wiki/Spetters" title="Spetters">Spetters</a></i> (1980) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fourth_Man_(1983_film)" title="The Fourth Man (1983 film)">The Fourth Man</a></i> ("<i>De Vierde Man</i>", 1983). Verhoeven then went on to direct big <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">Hollywood</a> movies like <i><a href="/wiki/RoboCop" title="RoboCop">RoboCop</a></i> (1987), <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Recall_(1990_film)" title="Total Recall (1990 film)">Total Recall</a></i> (1990) and <i><a href="/wiki/Basic_Instinct" title="Basic Instinct">Basic Instinct</a></i> (1992), and returned with Dutch film <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Book_(film)" title="Black Book (film)">Black Book</a></i> ("<i>Zwartboek</i>", 2006).\n</p><p>Other well-known Dutch film directors are <a href="/wiki/Jan_de_Bont" title="Jan de Bont">Jan de Bont</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Speed_(1994_film)" title="Speed (1994 film)">Speed</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Anton_Corbijn" title="Anton Corbijn">Anton Corbijn</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/A_Most_Wanted_Man_(film)" title="A Most Wanted Man (film)">A Most wanted Man</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Dick_Maas" title="Dick Maas">Dick Maas</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/De_Lift" title="De Lift">De Lift</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Fons_Rademakers" title="Fons Rademakers">Fons Rademakers</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Assault_(film)" title="The Assault (film)">The Assault</a></i>), and documentary makers <a href="/wiki/Bert_Haanstra" title="Bert Haanstra">Bert Haanstra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joris_Ivens" title="Joris Ivens">Joris Ivens</a>. Film director <a href="/wiki/Theo_van_Gogh_(film_director)" title="Theo van Gogh (film director)">Theo van Gogh</a> achieved international notoriety in 2004 when he was murdered by <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Bouyeri" title="Mohammed Bouyeri">Mohammed Bouyeri</a> in the streets of Amsterdam after directing the short film <i><a href="/wiki/Submission_(2004_film)" title="Submission (2004 film)">Submission</a></i>.\n</p><p>Internationally successful directors of photography from the Netherlands are <a href="/wiki/Hoyte_van_Hoytema" title="Hoyte van Hoytema">Hoyte van Hoytema</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Interstellar_(film)" title="Interstellar (film)">Interstellar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Spectre_(2015_film)" title="Spectre (2015 film)">Spectre</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dunkirk_(2017_film)" title="Dunkirk (2017 film)">Dunkirk</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Theo_van_de_Sande" title="Theo van de Sande">Theo van de Sande</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Wayne%27s_World" title="Wayne\'s World">Wayne\'s World</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_(film)" title="Blade (film)">Blade</a></i>). Van Hoytema went to the <a href="/wiki/National_Film_School_in_%C5%81%C3%B3d%C5%BA" title="National Film School in &#321;&#243;d&#378;">National Film School in &#321;&#243;d&#378;</a> (<a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>) and Van de Sande went to the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Film_Academy" title="Netherlands Film Academy">Netherlands Film Academy</a>. Internationally successful Dutch actors include <a href="/wiki/Famke_Janssen" title="Famke Janssen">Famke Janssen</a> (<a href="/wiki/X-Men_(film_series)" title="X-Men (film series)"><i>X-Men</i></a>), <a href="/wiki/Carice_van_Houten" title="Carice van Houten">Carice van Houten</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Michiel_Huisman" title="Michiel Huisman">Michiel Huisman</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Rutger_Hauer" title="Rutger Hauer">Rutger Hauer</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Jeroen_Krabb%C3%A9" title="Jeroen Krabb&#233;">Jeroen Krabb&#233;</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Living_Daylights" title="The Living Daylights">The Living Daylights</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Derek_de_Lint" title="Derek de Lint">Derek de Lint</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Three_Men_and_a_Baby" title="Three Men and a Baby">Three Men and a Baby</a></i>).\n</p><p>The Netherlands has a well developed television market, with both multiple commercial and public broadcasters. Imported TV programmes, as well as interviews with responses in a foreign language, are virtually always shown with the original sound and subtitled. Only foreign shows for children are translated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HaGanahl2013_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-HaGanahl2013-242">[229]</a></sup>\n</p><p>TV exports from the Netherlands mostly take the form of specific formats and franchises, most notably through internationally active TV production conglomerate <a href="/wiki/Endemol" title="Endemol">Endemol</a>, founded by Dutch <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">media</a> <a href="/wiki/Business_magnate" title="Business magnate">tycoons</a> <a href="/wiki/John_de_Mol_Jr." title="John de Mol Jr.">John de Mol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joop_van_den_Ende" title="Joop van den Ende">Joop van den Ende</a>. Headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, Endemol has around 90 companies in over 30 countries. Endemol and its subsidiaries create and run reality, talent, and game show franchises worldwide, including <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Brother_(TV_series)" title="Big Brother (TV series)">Big Brother</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Deal_or_No_Deal" title="Deal or No Deal">Deal or No Deal</a></i>. John de Mol later started his own company <a href="/wiki/Tien_(TV_channel)" title="Tien (TV channel)">Talpa</a> which created show franchises like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Voice_(TV_series)" title="The Voice (TV series)"><i>The Voice</i></a> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utopia_(U.S._reality_TV_series)" title="Utopia (U.S. reality TV series)">Utopia</a></i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_in_the_Netherlands" title="Sports in the Netherlands">Sports in the Netherlands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NED-DEN_Euro_2012_(10).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="593" data-file-width="656" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg/220px-NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg/330px-NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg/440px-NED-DEN_Euro_2012_%2810%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NED-DEN_Euro_2012_(10).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dutch star football players <a href="/wiki/Arjen_Robben" title="Arjen Robben">Arjen Robben</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robin_van_Persie" title="Robin van Persie">Robin van Persie</a> during a game with the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands national football team</a> against <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark national football team</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2012" title="Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Approximately 4.5 million of the 16.8 million people in the Netherlands are registered to one of the 35,000 sports clubs in the country. About two-thirds of the population between 15 and 75 participates in sports weekly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[230]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular participant sport in the Netherlands, before <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> as the second and third most popular team sports. Tennis, gymnastics and golf are the three most widely engaged in individual sports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sport_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-sport-244">[231]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Organisation of sports began at the end of the 19th century and the beginning of the 20th century. Federations for sports were established (such as the speed skating federation in 1882), rules were unified and sports clubs came into existence. A <a href="/wiki/NOC*NSF" title="NOC*NSF">Dutch National Olympic Committee</a> was established in 1912. Thus far, the nation has won 266 medals at the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympic Games</a> and another 110 medals at the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympic Games</a>. In international competition, Dutch national teams and athletes are dominant in several fields of sport. The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_women%27s_national_field_hockey_team" title="Netherlands women\'s national field hockey team">Netherlands women\'s field hockey team</a> is the most successful team in <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Hockey_World_Cup" title="Women\'s Hockey World Cup">World Cup</a> history. The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_baseball_team" title="Netherlands national baseball team">Netherlands baseball team</a> have won the <a href="/wiki/European_Baseball_Championship" title="European Baseball Championship">European championship</a> 20 times out of 32 events. Dutch <a href="/wiki/K-1" title="K-1">K-1</a> <a href="/wiki/Kickboxing" title="Kickboxing">kickboxers</a> have won the <a href="/wiki/K-1_World_Grand_Prix" title="K-1 World Grand Prix">K-1 World Grand Prix</a> 15 times out of 19 tournaments.\n</p><p>The Dutch <a href="/wiki/Speed_skating" title="Speed skating">speed skaters\'</a> performance at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympics</a>, where they won 8 out of 12 events, 23 out of 36 medals, including 4 clean sweeps, is the most dominant performance in a single sport in Olympic history. Motorcycle racing at the TT Assen Circuit has a long history. Assen is the only venue to have held a round of the Motorcycle World Championship every year since its creation in 1949. The circuit was purpose built for the Dutch TT in 1954, with previous events having been held on public roads.\n</p><p>The Dutch have also had success in all three of cyclings Grand Tours with <a href="/wiki/Jan_Janssen" title="Jan Janssen">Jan Janssen</a> winning the <a href="/wiki/1968_Tour_de_France" title="1968 Tour de France">1968 Tour de France</a>, more recently with <a href="/wiki/Tom_Dumoulin" title="Tom Dumoulin">Tom Dumoulin</a> winning the <a href="/wiki/2017_Giro_d%27Italia" title="2017 Giro d\'Italia">2017 Giro d\'Italia</a> and legendary rider <a href="/wiki/Joop_Zoetemelk" title="Joop Zoetemelk">Joop Zoetemelk</a> was the 1985 UCI World Champion, the winner of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1979_Vuelta_a_Espana" title="1979 Vuelta a Espana">1979 Vuelta a Espana</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1980_Tour_de_France" title="1980 Tour de France">1980 Tour de France</a> and still holds or shares numerous <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a> records including most Tours finished and most kilometers ridden.\n</p><p>Limburger <a href="/wiki/Max_Verstappen" title="Max Verstappen">Max Verstappen</a> currently races in <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2016_Spanish_Grand_Prix" title="2016 Spanish Grand Prix">was the first Dutchman to win a Grand Prix</a>. The coastal resort of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Circuit_Park_Zandvoort" title="Circuit Park Zandvoort">Zandvoort</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Grand_Prix" title="Dutch Grand Prix">Dutch Grand Prix</a> from 1958 to 1985. The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_men%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Netherlands men\'s national volleyball team">volleyball national men\'s team</a> has also been successful, winning the silver medal at the <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_1992_Summer_Olympics" title="Volleyball at the 1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Summer Olympics</a> and the gold medal <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_1996_Summer_Olympics" title="Volleyball at the 1996 Summer Olympics">four years later</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>. The biggest success of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_women%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Netherlands women\'s national volleyball team">women\'s national team</a> was winning the <a href="/wiki/1995_Women%27s_European_Volleyball_Championship" title="1995 Women\'s European Volleyball Championship">European Championship in 1995</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2007_FIVB_Volleyball_World_Grand_Prix" title="2007 FIVB Volleyball World Grand Prix">World Grand Prix in 2007</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_cuisine" title="Dutch cuisine">Dutch cuisine</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:124px;max-width:124px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:121px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stroopwafels_01.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2500" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Stroopwafels_01.jpg/122px-Stroopwafels_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Stroopwafels_01.jpg/183px-Stroopwafels_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Stroopwafels_01.jpg/244px-Stroopwafels_01.jpg 2x" width="122"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><i><a href="/wiki/Stroopwafel" title="Stroopwafel">Stroopwafels</a></i> (syrup waffles) are a treat consisting of waffles with caramel-like syrup filling in the middle.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:164px;max-width:164px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:121px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oliebollen.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Oliebollen.jpg/162px-Oliebollen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Oliebollen.jpg/243px-Oliebollen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Oliebollen.jpg/324px-Oliebollen.jpg 2x" width="162"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oliebollen" title="Oliebollen">Oliebollen</a></i>, a Dutch pastry eaten on New Year\'s Eve.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:147px;max-width:147px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:92px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Poffertjes-Melkhuis_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3136" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="92" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Poffertjes-Melkhuis_%28cropped%29.jpg/145px-Poffertjes-Melkhuis_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Poffertjes-Melkhuis_%28cropped%29.jpg/218px-Poffertjes-Melkhuis_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Poffertjes-Melkhuis_%28cropped%29.jpg/290px-Poffertjes-Melkhuis_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="145"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><i><a href="/wiki/Poffertjes" title="Poffertjes">Poffertjes</a></i> are made in a special, so-called, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skillet" title="Skillet">poffertjespan</a></i>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:141px;max-width:141px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:92px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:13-06-27-gouda-by-RalfR-125.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="92" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/13-06-27-gouda-by-RalfR-125.jpg/139px-13-06-27-gouda-by-RalfR-125.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/13-06-27-gouda-by-RalfR-125.jpg/209px-13-06-27-gouda-by-RalfR-125.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/13-06-27-gouda-by-RalfR-125.jpg/278px-13-06-27-gouda-by-RalfR-125.jpg 2x" width="139"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">The <a href="/wiki/Gouda,_South_Holland" title="Gouda, South Holland">Gouda</a> cheese market.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:160px;max-width:160px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:126px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hutspot_met_stooflap_op_bord.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="591" data-file-width="739" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Hutspot_met_stooflap_op_bord.JPG/158px-Hutspot_met_stooflap_op_bord.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Hutspot_met_stooflap_op_bord.JPG/237px-Hutspot_met_stooflap_op_bord.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Hutspot_met_stooflap_op_bord.JPG/316px-Hutspot_met_stooflap_op_bord.JPG 2x" width="158"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><i><a href="/wiki/Hutspot" title="Hutspot">Hutspot</a></i> with klapstuk (beef).</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:128px;max-width:128px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:126px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bitterballen_mosterd_mayo.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bitterballen_mosterd_mayo.jpg/126px-Bitterballen_mosterd_mayo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bitterballen_mosterd_mayo.jpg/189px-Bitterballen_mosterd_mayo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bitterballen_mosterd_mayo.jpg/252px-Bitterballen_mosterd_mayo.jpg 2x" width="126"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><i><a href="/wiki/Bitterballen" title="Bitterballen">Bitterballen</a></i> are usually served with <a href="/wiki/Mustard_(condiment)" title="Mustard (condiment)">mustard</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Originally, the country\'s cuisine was shaped by the practices of <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farming" title="Farming">farming</a>, including the cultivation of the soil for growing crops and raising domesticated animals. Dutch cuisine is simple and straightforward, and contains many dairy products. Breakfast and lunch are typically bread with toppings, with cereal for breakfast as an alternative. Traditionally, dinner consists of potatoes, a portion of meat, and (seasonal) vegetables. The Dutch diet was relatively high in carbohydrates and fat, reflecting the dietary needs of the labourers whose culture moulded the country. Without many refinements, it is best described as rustic, though many holidays are still celebrated with special foods. In the course of the twentieth century this diet changed and became much more <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">cosmopolitan</a>, with most <a href="/wiki/Global_cuisine" title="Global cuisine">global cuisines</a> being represented in the major cities.\n</p><p>Modern culinary writers distinguish between three general regional forms of Dutch cuisine. The regions in the northeast of the Netherlands, roughly the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Groningen_(province)" title="Groningen (province)">Groningen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drenthe" title="Drenthe">Drenthe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Overijssel" title="Overijssel">Overijssel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gelderland" title="Gelderland">Gelderland</a> north of the <a href="/wiki/Grote_rivieren" title="Grote rivieren">great rivers</a> are the least populated area of the Netherlands. The late (18th century) introduction of large scale agriculture means that the cuisine is generally known for its many kinds of meats. The relative lack of farms allowed for an abundance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_(meat)" title="Game (meat)">game</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">husbandry</a>, though dishes near the coastal regions of Friesland, Groningen and the parts of Overijssel bordering the <a href="/wiki/IJsselmeer" title="IJsselmeer">IJsselmeer</a> also include a large amount of fish. The various dried sausages, belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Metworst" title="Metworst">metworst</a>-family of Dutch sausages are found throughout this region and are highly prized for their often very strong taste. Also smoked sausages are common, of which (<i>Gelderse</i>) <i><a href="/wiki/Rookworst" title="Rookworst">rookworst</a></i> is the most renowned. The sausage contains a lot of fat and is very juicy. Larger sausages are often eaten alongside <i><a href="/wiki/Stamppot" title="Stamppot">stamppot</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hutspot" title="Hutspot">hutspot</a></i> or <i>zuurkool</i> (<a href="/wiki/Sauerkraut" title="Sauerkraut">sauerkraut</a>); whereas smaller ones are often eaten as a <a href="/wiki/Street_food" title="Street food">street food</a>. The provinces are also home to hard textured <a href="/wiki/Rye_bread" title="Rye bread">rye bread</a>, pastries and cookies, the latter heavily spiced with <a href="/wiki/Ginger" title="Ginger">ginger</a> or <a href="/wiki/Succade" title="Succade">succade</a> or contain small bits of meat. Various kinds of <i>Kruidkoek</i> (such as <a class="extiw" href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Groninger_koek" title="nl:Groninger koek">Groninger koek</a>), <i><a class="extiw" href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fryske_d%C3%BAmkes" title="nl:Fryske d&#250;mkes">Fryske d&#250;mkes</a></i> and <i><a class="extiw" href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/spekdik" title="nl:spekdik">spekdikken</a></i> (small savory pancakes cooked in a waffle iron) are considered typical. Notable characteristics of <i>Fries roggebrood</i> (Frisian rye bread) is its long baking time (up to 20 hours), resulting in a sweet taste and a deep dark colour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[232]</a></sup> In terms of alcoholic beverages, the region is renowned for its many <a href="/wiki/Bitters" title="Bitters">bitters</a> (such as <i><a href="/wiki/Beerenburg" title="Beerenburg">Beerenburg</a></i>) and other high-proof liquors rather than beer, which is, apart from <i><a href="/wiki/Jenever" title="Jenever">Jenever</a></i>, typical for the rest of the country. As a coastal region, Friesland is home to low-lying grasslands, and thus has a cheese production in common with the Western cuisine. <i>Friese Nagelkaas</i> (<a href="/wiki/Friesian_Clove" title="Friesian Clove">Friesian Clove</a>) is a notable example.\n</p><p>The provinces of <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Holland" title="South Holland">South Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zeeland" title="Zeeland">Zeeland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utrecht_(province)" title="Utrecht (province)">Utrecht</a> and the Gelderlandic region of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Betuwe" title="Betuwe">Betuwe</a> are the parts of the Netherlands which make up the region in which western Dutch cuisine is found. Because of the abundance of water and flat grass lands that are found here, the area is known for its many dairy products, which includes prominent cheeses such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gouda_(cheese)" title="Gouda (cheese)">Gouda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leyden_cheese" title="Leyden cheese">Leyden</a> (spiced cheese with cumin), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edam_(cheese)" title="Edam (cheese)">Edam</a> (traditionally in small spheres) as well as <a href="/wiki/Leerdammer" title="Leerdammer">Leerdammer</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beemster_Cheese" title="Beemster Cheese">Beemster</a>, while the adjacent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zaanstreek" title="Zaanstreek">Zaanstreek</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North Holland</a> is since the 16th century known for its <a href="/wiki/Mayonnaise" title="Mayonnaise">mayonnaise</a>, typical whole-grain <a href="/wiki/Mustard_(condiment)" title="Mustard (condiment)">mustards</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[233]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">chocolate</a> industry. Zeeland and South Holland produce a lot of butter, which contains a larger amount of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milkfat" title="Milkfat">milkfat</a> than most other European butter varieties. A by-product of the butter-making process, <i>karnemelk</i> (<a href="/wiki/Buttermilk" title="Buttermilk">buttermilk</a>), is also considered typical for this region. <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">Seafood</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Soused_herring" title="Soused herring">soused herring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_mussel" title="Blue mussel">mussels</a> (called <i>Zeeuwse Mossels</i>, since all Dutch mussels for consumption are cleaned in Zeeland\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oosterschelde" title="Oosterschelde">Oosterschelde</a>), <a href="/wiki/European_eel" title="European eel">eels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oyster" title="Oyster">oysters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shrimp" title="Shrimp">shrimps</a> are widely available and typical for the region. <i><a class="extiw" href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kibbeling" title="nl:Kibbeling">Kibbeling</a></i>, once a local delicacy consisting of small chunks of battered <a href="/wiki/Whitefish_(fisheries_term)" title="Whitefish (fisheries term)">white fish</a>, has become a national <a href="/wiki/Fast_food" title="Fast food">fast food</a>, just as <a class="extiw" href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lekkerbekje" title="nl:Lekkerbekje">lekkerbek</a>. Pastries in this area tend to be quite doughy, and often contain large amounts of sugar; either caramelised, powdered or crystallised. The <i><a href="/wiki/Oliebol" title="Oliebol">oliebol</a></i> (in its modern form) and <i><a href="/wiki/Zeeuwse_bolus" title="Zeeuwse bolus">Zeeuwse bolus</a></i> are good examples. Cookies are also produced in great number and tend to contain a lot of butter and sugar, like <i><a href="/wiki/Stroopwafel" title="Stroopwafel">stroopwafel</a></i>, as well as a filling of some kind, mostly almond, like <i><a class="extiw" href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gevulde_koek" title="nl:Gevulde koek">gevulde koek</a></i>. The traditional alcoholic beverages of this region are <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a> (strong pale lager) and <i><a href="/wiki/Jenever" title="Jenever">Jenever</a></i>, a high proof <a href="/wiki/Juniper" title="Juniper">juniper</a>-flavored spirit, that came to be known in England as <a href="/wiki/Gin" title="Gin">gin</a>. A noted exception within the traditional Dutch alcoholic landscape, <i><a href="/wiki/Advocaat" title="Advocaat">Advocaat</a></i>, a rich and creamy liqueur made from eggs, sugar and brandy, is also native to this region.\n</p><p>The Southern Dutch cuisine consists of the cuisines of the Dutch provinces of <a href="/wiki/North_Brabant" title="North Brabant">North Brabant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limburg_(Netherlands)" title="Limburg (Netherlands)">Limburg</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Region" title="Flemish Region">Flemish Region</a> in <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>. It is renowned for its many rich pastries, soups, stews and vegetable dishes and is often called Burgundian which is a Dutch idiom invoking the rich Burgundian court which ruled the Low Countries in the Middle Ages, renowned for its splendor and great feasts. It is the only Dutch culinary region that developed an <a href="/wiki/Haute_cuisine" title="Haute cuisine">haute cuisine</a>. Pastries are abundant, often with rich fillings of cream, custard or fruits. Cakes, such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Vlaai" title="Vlaai">Vlaai</a></i> from Limburg and the <i>Moorkop</i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bossche_Bol" title="Bossche Bol">Bossche Bol</a></i> from Brabant, are typical pastries.
