Savoury pastries also occur, with the <i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">worstenbroodje</i> (a roll with a sausage of <a href="/wiki/Ground_beef" title="Ground beef">ground beef</a>, literally translates into sausage bread) being the most popular. The traditional alcoholic beverage of the region is beer. There are many local brands, ranging from <i><a href="/wiki/Trappist_beer" title="Trappist beer">Trappist</a></i> to <i><a href="/wiki/Kriek_lambic" title="Kriek lambic">Kriek</a></i>. 5 of the 10 <i>International Trappist Association</i> recognised breweries in the world, are located in the Southern Dutch cultural area. Beer, like wine in French cuisine, is also used in cooking; often in stews.\n</p><p>In early 2014, <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> ranked the Netherlands as the country with the most nutritious, plentiful and healthy food, in a comparison of 125 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[235]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_heritage">Colonial heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Colonial heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indos_in_the_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Indos in the Dutch East Indies">Indos in the Dutch East Indies</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4964" data-file-width="7276" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg/200px-GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg/300px-GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg/400px-GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GezichtOpNieuwAmsterdam.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a> as it appeared in 1664; under British rule it became known as <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a></div></div></div>\n<p>From the exploitations of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> in the 17th century, to the <a href="/wiki/New_Imperialism" title="New Imperialism">colonisations</a> in the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch imperial possessions</a> continued to expand, reaching their greatest extent by establishing a hegemony of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> in the early 20th century. The Dutch East Indies, which later formed modern-day Indonesia, was one of the most valuable European colonies in the world and the most important one for the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[236]</a></sup> Over 350 years of mutual heritage has left a significant cultural mark on the Netherlands.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a> of the 17th century, the Netherlands urbanised considerably, mostly financed by corporate revenue from the Asian trade monopolies. Social status was based on merchants\' income, which reduced <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a> and considerably changed the dynamics of Dutch society. When the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Monarchy of the Netherlands">Dutch royal family</a> was established in 1815, much of its wealth came from Colonial trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[237]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG/200px-De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG/300px-De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG/400px-De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Eustachius_De_Lannoy" title="Eustachius De Lannoy">Eustachius De Lannoy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> surrenders to Maharaja <a href="/wiki/Marthanda_Varma" title="Marthanda Varma">Marthanda Varma</a> of the <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Travancore" title="Kingdom of Travancore">Kingdom of Travancore</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Colachel" title="Battle of Colachel">Battle of Colachel</a>. (Depiction at <a href="/wiki/Padmanabhapuram_Palace" title="Padmanabhapuram Palace">Padmanabhapuram Palace</a>)</div></div></div>\n<p>By the 17th century, the Dutch East India Company established their base in parts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylon" title="Ceylon">Ceylon</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>). Afterward, they established ports in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Malabar" title="Dutch Malabar">Dutch occupied Malabar</a>, leading to <a href="/wiki/Dutch_India" title="Dutch India">Dutch settlements and trading posts in India</a>. However, their expansion into <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> was halted, after their defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Colachel" title="Battle of Colachel">Battle of Colachel</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Travancore" title="Travancore">Kingdom of Travancore</a>, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Travancore-Dutch_War" title="Travancore-Dutch War">Travancore-Dutch War</a>. The Dutch never recovered from the defeat and no longer posed a large colonial threat to India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[239]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Universities such as the Royal <a href="/wiki/Leiden_University" title="Leiden University">Leiden University</a>, founded in the 16th century, have developed into leading knowledge centres for <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asian</a> and Indonesian studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[n]</a></sup> Leiden University has produced leading academics such as <a href="/wiki/Christiaan_Snouck_Hurgronje" title="Christiaan Snouck Hurgronje">Christiaan Snouck Hurgronje</a>, and still has academics who specialise in Indonesian languages and cultures. Leiden University and in particular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KITLV" title="KITLV">KITLV</a> are educational and scientific institutions that to this day share both an intellectual and historical interest in Indonesian studies. Other scientific institutions in the Netherlands include the Amsterdam <a href="/wiki/Tropenmuseum" title="Tropenmuseum">Tropenmuseum</a>, an anthropological museum with massive collections of Indonesian art, culture, ethnography and anthropology.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Europeaan_vaccineert_Indonesische_pati%C3%ABnten_met_neosalvarsaan_tegen_de_ziekte_framboesia_TMnr_10006691.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="638" decoding="async" height="219" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Europeaan_vaccineert_Indonesische_pati%C3%ABnten_met_neosalvarsaan_tegen_de_ziekte_framboesia_TMnr_10006691.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Dutch doctor vaccinating <a href="/wiki/Native_Indonesians" title="Native Indonesians">Indonesian</a> patients</div></div></div>\n<p>The traditions of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_East_Indies_Army" title="Royal Dutch East Indies Army">Royal Dutch East Indies Army</a> (KNIL) are maintained by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regiment_Van_Heutsz" title="Regiment Van Heutsz">Regiment Van Heutsz</a> of the modern <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Army" title="Royal Netherlands Army">Royal Netherlands Army</a>. A dedicated <i><a href="/wiki/Bronbeek" title="Bronbeek">Bronbeek</a> Museum</i>, a former home for retired KNIL soldiers, exists in <a href="/wiki/Arnhem" title="Arnhem">Arnhem</a> to this day.\n</p><p>A specific segment of Dutch literature called <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Indies_literature" title="Dutch Indies literature">Dutch Indies literature</a> still exists and includes established authors, such as <a href="/wiki/Louis_Couperus" title="Louis Couperus">Louis Couperus</a>, the writer of "The Hidden Force", taking the colonial era as an important source of inspiration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[240]</a></sup> One of the great masterpieces of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_literature" title="Dutch literature">Dutch literature</a> is the book "<a href="/wiki/Max_Havelaar" title="Max Havelaar">Max Havelaar</a>", written by <a href="/wiki/Multatuli" title="Multatuli">Multatuli</a> in 1860.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[241]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The majority of Dutchmen that repatriated to the Netherlands after and during the Indonesian revolution are <a href="/wiki/Indo_people" title="Indo people">Indo</a> (Eurasian), native to the islands of the Dutch East Indies. This relatively large Eurasian population had developed over a period of 400 years and were classified by colonial law as belonging to the European legal community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[242]</a></sup> In Dutch they are referred to as <i>Indische Nederlanders</i> or as Indo (short for Indo-European).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[243]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Including their second generation descendants, Indos are currently the largest foreign-born group in the Netherlands. In 2008, the Dutch Central Bureau for Statistics (CBS)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[244]</a></sup> registered 387,000 first- and second-generation Indos living in the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[245]</a></sup> Although considered fully assimilated into Dutch society, as the main ethnic minority in the Netherlands, these \'repatriants\' have played a pivotal role in introducing elements of Indonesian culture into Dutch mainstream culture.\n</p><p>Practically every town in the Netherlands has a "Toko" (Dutch Indonesian Shop) or a Chinese-Indonesian restaurant<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[246]</a></sup> and many \'<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pasar_Malam" title="Pasar Malam">Pasar Malam</a>\' (Night market in Malay/Indonesian) fairs are organised throughout the year. Many Indonesian dishes and foodstuffs have become commonplace in the Netherlands. <a href="/wiki/Rijsttafel" title="Rijsttafel">Rijsttafel</a>, a colonial culinary concept, and dishes such as <a href="/wiki/Nasi_goreng" title="Nasi goreng">Nasi goreng</a> and <a href="/wiki/Satay" title="Satay">satay</a> are very popular in the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[247]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="flag" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="21" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/48px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/64px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 2x" width="32"/></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Netherlands" title="Portal:Netherlands">Netherlands portal</a></span></li></ul></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_the_Netherlands" title="Outline of the Netherlands">Outline of the Netherlands</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The official motto is in French. The literal translation into English is \'I will maintain\'; an alternative translation, however, is \'I will hold firm\' or \'I will uphold\' (namely, the integrity and independence of the territory).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> </span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1816 the motto was abbreviated to <i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">\'<a href="/wiki/God_zij_met_ons" title="God zij met ons">God zij met ons</a>\'</i> (used on the edges of coins).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-central_cities-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-central_cities_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-central_cities_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">While Amsterdam is the constitutional capital, The&#160;Hague is the seat of the government.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-languages-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-languages_8-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-languages_8-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">West Frisian has official status in <a href="/wiki/Friesland" title="Friesland">Friesland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[3]</a></sup> Dutch Low Saxon and Limburgish are recognised as <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">regional languages</a> by the European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-official-and-recognised-languages_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-official-and-recognised-languages-5">[2]</a></sup> Papiamento is recognised by the Government of the Netherlands in relation to <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, and English in relation to <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-languages_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-languages-7">[4]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The euro is used in the European part of the Netherlands and replaced the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_guilder" title="Dutch guilder">Dutch guilder</a> in 2002. The US dollar is used in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a> and replaced the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antillean_guilder" title="Netherlands Antillean guilder">Netherlands Antillean guilder</a> in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[11]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">CET and CEST are used in the European Netherlands, and AST is used in the Caribbean Netherlands.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">599 was the country code designated for the now dissolved <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a>. The Caribbean Netherlands still use 599&#8211;7 (Bonaire), 599&#8211;3 (Sint Eustatius) and 599&#8211;4 (Saba).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">.nl is the common internet top level domain name for the Netherlands. The <a href="/wiki/.eu" title=".eu">.eu</a> domain is also used, as it is shared with other <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states. .bq is designated, but not in use, for the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Up one place from previous rankings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[23]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-158"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-158">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Only 11 stations are served less than twice an hour during weekdays.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-167"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-167">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Up from 31% vs. 19% naming the bike their main mode of transport for daily activities in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[156]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-203"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-203">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Provided statistics show Protestants by their allegiance to congregations of two denominations that do not exist anymore. In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed Church</a> (NHK), the <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Churches_in_the_Netherlands" title="Reformed Churches in the Netherlands">Reformed Churches in the Netherlands</a> (GKN) and the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in the Kingdom of the Netherlands">Evangelical Lutheran Church in the Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> merged to form the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Church_in_the_Netherlands" title="Protestant Church in the Netherlands">Protestant Church in the Netherlands</a> (PKN) and officially no longer exist. However, many people still tend to give their older affiliation even after the merger. People who declared themselves simply as belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Church_in_the_Netherlands" title="Protestant Church in the Netherlands">Protestant Church in the Netherlands</a> did not give an information about belonging to an older affiliation. For example, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutherans" title="Lutherans">Members</a> of the former <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in the Kingdom of the Netherlands">Evangelical Lutheran Church in the Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> happened to do so. People who identified with one of those three categories (NHK/GKN/or simply PKN) are all members of the Protestant Church in the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[191]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-204"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-204">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Including other Protestants that are not members of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Church_in_the_Netherlands" title="Protestant Church in the Netherlands">Protestant Church in the Netherlands</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-253"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-253">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some of the university faculties still include: Indonesian Languages and Cultures; South-east Asia and Oceania Languages and Cultures; Cultural Anthropology.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Netherlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="https://dutchrevolt.leiden.edu/dutch/spreuken/Pages/je%20maintiendrai.aspx" rel="nofollow">Dutch Revolt, Leiden University</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-official-and-recognised-languages-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-official-and-recognised-languages_5-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-official-and-recognised-languages_5-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="https://www.rijksoverheid.nl/onderwerpen/erkende-talen/vraag-en-antwoord/erkende-talen-nederland" rel="nofollow">"Welke erkende talen heeft Nederland?"</a> (in Dutch).
